Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Fulfilling Sajdah al-Tilawah with Ruku or Sujud in Prayer
Explaining how to fulfill sajdah within prayer using ruku or sujud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing Sajdah al-Tilawah within prayer using ruku or sujud, and identify the key conditions (intention, fuur).

Core Idea
In prayer, both ruku and sujud can fulfill Sajdah al-Tilawah, but sujud is better and intention is required only for ruku.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi explains the method of performing Sajdah al-Tilawah while in the middle of the obligatory prayer. The Hanafi school holds that the sajdah can be accomplished either by an extra ruku or sujud within the prayer, distinct from the obligatory ones. This lesson clarifies the basic ruling, the proof, and the practical preferences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is performing Sajdah al-Tilawah during prayer. The ruling is that it is wajib, and it can be fulfilled by a ruku or sujud that occurs within the prayer (not the obligatory ones).
The obligation is on the reciter and hearer; within prayer, a separate sajdah can be avoided by using ruku or sujud.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the transmitted effect (athar) that the Prophet performed ruku for sajdah within prayer, limiting the permission to within prayer.
The text states 'the effect is only transmitted regarding when he does ruku in it, so it is limited to the place of the effect.'
3
Analyze the qiyas
The reasoning (ta'lil) is that both ruku and sujud contain glorification (ta'zim), so ruku can substitute for sujud in fulfilling the wajib.
This is a qiyas jaliy: the illa is the common element of glorification.
4
Note the conditions for validity
For ruku: intention (niyyah) to perform the sajdah is required. For sujud: intention is not required, but the immediacy (fuur) must not be broken by reciting more than two (or three) verses after the sajdah verse.
The condition of fuur applies to both, but for sujud it is explicitly mentioned; for ruku, intention is necessary.
5
Evaluate the preference
Sujud is better because it achieves both the form (sujud itself) and the meaning (humility), while ruku only achieves the meaning.
The author states: 'Sujud is better because it achieves two nearnesses: the form of the obligation and its meaning.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتؤدى بركوع أو سجود كائنين (في الصلاة غير ركوع الصلاة (و) غير (سجودها) والسجود أفضل لأنه تحصيل قربتين صورة الواجب ومعناه وبالركوع المعنى وهو الخضوع وإذا كانت آخر تلاوته ينبغي أن يقرأ، ولو آيتين من سورة آخرى بعد قيامه منها حتى لا يصير بانياً الركوع على السجود ولو ركع بمجرد قيامه منها كره ويجزى عنها) أي عن سجدة التلاوة ركوع الصلاة إن نواها أي نوى أداءها فيه نص عليه محمد لأن معنى التعظيم فيهما واحد، وينبغي ذلك للإمام مع كثرة القوم أو حال المخافتة حتى لا يؤدي إلى التخليط (و) يجزي عنها أيضاً (سجودها) أي سجود الصلاة (وإن لم ينوها أي التلاوية (إذا لم ينقطع فور التلاوة) وانقطاعه بأن يقرأ أكثر من (آيتين) بعد آية سجدة التلاوة بالإجماع، وقال شمس الأئمة الحلواني: لا ينقطع الفور ما لم يقرأ أكثر من ثلاث آيات، وقال الكمال: إن قول شمس الأئمة هو الرواية . قوله: (في الصلاة) هذا القيد بالنسبة إلى الركوع فقط، فلا يجزى عنها ركوع في خارجها لأن الأثر إنما ورد فيما إذا ركع فيها فقط، فيقتصر على مورد الأثر لكن في البحر، واختار قاضيخان أن الركوع خارج الصلاة ينوب عنها، وفي النهر عن البزازية، وهو ظاهر المروي اهـ، فيحمل على اختلاف الرواية . قوله : (صورة الواجب) وهو السجود قوله : ( ومعناه) هو الخضوع كما أفاده بعده. قوله: (ينبغي أن يقرأ ولو آيتين الخ) قال في الفتح : فينبغي أن يقرأ ما بقي من السورة ، ولو آيتين كسورة الإسراء أو ثلاث آيات كانشقت وإن كانت الآية آخر السورة يقرأ من سورة أخرى، ثم يركع .اهـ. قوله : ( على السجود) أي أو على ركوع مثله قوله: (كره) أطلق في الكراهة وظاهره التحريم، ويحرر. قوله : (إن نواها) أي عند الركوع وإن نوى في الركوع ففيه قولان، وإن نوى بعد الرفع منه لا يجوز بالإجماع كما في البحر عن الاسبيجابي، وفي القهستاني عن الجلابي عن محمد أنه ينوب بدون نية قوله : (نص عليه محمد) أي على اشتراط النية كما يؤخذ من الشرح قوله : (فيهما (واحد) أي في السجود والركوع فكما يحصل التعظيم بالسجود كذلك يحصل بالركوع . قوله : ( وينبغي ذلك للإمام أن يجعلها في ركوع الصلاة إن كانت سرية، أو في سجودها إن كانت جهرية أي ولا يجعل لها ركوعاً أو سجوداً قوله : (إذا لم ينقطع) مرتبط بالركوع والسجود جميعاً. قوله : (بأن يقرأ أكثر من آيتين) اعلم أن الفور لا ينقطع بآية بعد آيتها، أو آيتين اتفاقاً وينقطع بأربع اتفاقاً، واختلف في الثلاث، فقيل: ينقطع واختاره خواهر زاده وقيل: لا واختاره الحلواني وهو أصح من جهة الرواية كما في الحلبي، والأول أصح من جهة الدراية لأنه أحوط كما ذكره المؤلف، وفي البدائع، وأكثر مشايخنا لم يقدروا في ذلك تقديراً، فكان الظاهر أنهم يفوضون ذلك إلى رأي المجتهد كما فعلوا ذلك في كثير من المواضع، وهو الأوجه أو يعتبر ما يعد طويلاً اهـ.
And it is performed by a ruku or sujud occurring in the prayer, other than the ruku of the prayer and other than its sujud. And sujud is better because it achieves two nearnesses: the form of the obligation and its meaning, while by ruku only the meaning (humility) is achieved. And if it is the last of his recitation, he should recite, even two verses from another surah after rising from it, so that he does not become one who builds ruku upon sujud. And if he does ruku immediately upon rising from it, it is disliked and suffices. (i.e., for the sajdah of recitation) the ruku of the prayer suffices if he intends it, i.e., intends to perform it, as textually stated by Muhammad because the meaning of glorification in both is one. And that is recommended for the imam when the congregation is large or in a case of raising the voice so as not to lead to confusion. And also its sujud (i.e., the sujud of the prayer) suffices although he does not intend it (the sajdah of recitation), if the fuur of recitation is not broken. And its break is by reciting more than two verses after the sajdah verse by consensus. And Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani said: fuur is not broken as long as he does not recite more than three verses. And al-Kamal said: indeed the saying of Shams al-A'imma is the narration. His statement: (in the prayer) this restriction applies to ruku only, so ruku outside of it does not suffice, because the effect is only transmitted regarding when he does ruku in it, so it is limited to the place of the effect. But in al-Bahr, Qadikhan chose that ruku outside of prayer suffices, and in al-Nahr from al-Bazzaziyya, it is apparent in the transmitted narration, so it is interpreted as a difference in narration. His statement: (form of the obligation) which is sujud. His statement: (and its meaning) which is humility as he explained afterwards. His statement: (he should recite even two verses etc.) said in al-Fath: he should recite what remains of the surah, even two verses like Surah al-Isra or three verses like al-Inshiqaq, and if the verse is at the end of the surah, he recites from another surah, then does ruku. His statement: (upon sujud) i.e., or upon similar ruku. His statement: (disliked) he made it general in dislike, and its apparent meaning is prohibition, but it needs investigation. His statement: (if he intends it) i.e., at the time of ruku, and if he intends in the ruku itself, there are two opinions, and if he intends after raising from it, it is not valid by consensus as in al-Bahr from al-Ispijabi, and in al-Qahistani from al-Jallabi from Muhammad that it suffices without intention. His statement: (textually stated by Muhammad) i.e., on the condition of intention as understood from the commentary. His statement: (in both (is one) i.e., in sujud and ruku, just as glorification is achieved by sujud, likewise it is achieved by ruku. His statement: (and that is recommended for the imam) that he makes it in the ruku of the prayer if it is silent, or in its sujud if it is loud, i.e., he does not make for it a separate ruku or sujud. His statement: (if it is not broken) is linked to both ruku and sujud. His statement: (by reciting more than two verses) know that the fuur is not broken by one verse after it, or two verses by agreement, and it is broken by four verses by agreement, and there is difference regarding three: some say it is broken, chosen by Khwahar Zada, and some say no, chosen by al-Halwani, and it is stronger from the perspective of narration as in al-Halabi, and the first is stronger from the perspective of reasoning because it is more cautious as mentioned by the author, and in al-Bada'i, most of our shaykhs did not set a specific estimate for that, so it appears that they refer it to the ijtihad of the mujtahid as they did in many places, and that is the most appropriate, or it is considered what is deemed lengthy.
Source pages p. 486

Commentary
This passage details the method of fulfilling Sajdah al-Tilawah during prayer. The matn states it can be performed by either an extra ruku or sujud within the prayer, distinct from the obligatory ones. Sujud is preferable because it physically enacts the obligation (sujud) while also achieving humility, whereas ruku only achieves the latter. If a verse is the last of the surah, the imam should recite at least two verses from the next surah to avoid building ruku upon sujud. Doing ruku immediately after standing is permissible but makruh. The hashiya clarifies that this applies only within prayer per the hadith evidence, though Qadikhan allows it outside. Intention is required for ruku to suffice; if not intended, it does not count. For sujud of the prayer, it suffices even without specific intention, provided the fuur (immediacy) is not broken by reciting more than two (or three according to some) verses after the sajdah verse. The commentary discusses various opinions on what breaks fuur, noting that most Hanafi scholars do not specify a number but refer to the mujtahid's judgment. The text concludes with a recommendation for the imam to incorporate the sajdah into the prayer's ruku or sujud to avoid confusion.

Key Terms
فور التلاوة (fuur al-tilawah): The immediate time period after reciting a sajdah verse during which the sajdah should be performed.
نية (niyyah): Intent to perform the sajdah of recitation when doing ruku or sujud.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, which of the following is true about performing Sajdah al-Tilawah during prayer using sujud?
A) It requires specific intention (niyyah)
B) It suffices without intention as long as the fuur is not broken
C) It is only allowed in loud prayers
D) It is makruh to do so

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, Sajdah al-Tilawah in prayer can be done via ruku or sujud, with sujud being optimal, and intention required only for ruku.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Intention and Immediacy in Sajdah al-Tilawah
Explaining how to fulfill sajdah within prayer using ruku or sujud (focus on niyyah and fuur)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the role of intention (niyyah) in fulfilling Sajdah al-Tilawah with ruku or sujud, and define the concept of fuur al-tilawah and its limits according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Intention is mandatory for ruku but not for sujud, while the fuur (immediacy) for sujud is broken by reciting more than two verses (or three in one opinion).

This lesson delves deeper into two critical conditions discussed in the passage: the requirement of intention for ruku and the concept of fuur for sujud. Understanding these nuances ensures the sajdah is performed correctly during prayer, avoiding invalidation or the need for repetition.

Guided Path
1
State the rule for intention in ruku
For ruku to fulfill Sajdah al-Tilawah, the worshiper must have the intention (niyyah) to perform the sajdah while bowing. This is textually reported from Imam Muhammad.
Without intention, the ruku only serves the prayer, not the recitation obligation.
2
Examine the rule for intention in sujud
For sujud, no specific intention for the sajdah is required. The sujud of the prayer automatically suffices, provided the immediacy (fuur) is preserved.
This is a relaxation because sujud is the original act of prostration.
3
Define fuur al-tilawah
Fuur is the immediate time after reciting a sajdah verse during which the sajdah should be performed. It is considered unbroken as long as no lengthy interruption occurs.
The text specifies that reciting one or two verses after the sajdah verse does not break fuur.
4
Analyze the dispute on the limit of fuur
There is consensus that four verses break fuur. Dispute exists on three verses: some say it breaks fuur (Khwahar Zada), others say it does not (al-Halwani). The more cautious view is that three breaks it, but al-Halwani's is stronger in narration.
Most Hanafi scholars did not fix a number but referred to the mujtahid's judgment.
5
Apply the rules to a scenario
For example: if after reciting a sajdah verse in prayer, the imam recites three more verses before going into sujud, according to the cautious view, fuur is broken and the sujud does not suffice; he must make a separate sajdah later.
The practical consequence differs based on which opinion is followed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Commentary
This passage details the method of fulfilling Sajdah al-Tilawah during prayer. The matn states it can be performed by either an extra ruku or sujud within the prayer, distinct from the obligatory ones. Sujud is preferable because it physically enacts the obligation (sujud) while also achieving humility, whereas ruku only achieves the latter. If a verse is the last of the surah, the imam should recite at least two verses from the next surah to avoid building ruku upon sujud. Doing ruku immediately after standing is permissible but makruh. The hashiya clarifies that this applies only within prayer per the hadith evidence, though Qadikhan allows it outside. Intention is required for ruku to suffice; if not intended, it does not count. For sujud of the prayer, it suffices even without specific intention, provided the fuur (immediacy) is not broken by reciting more than two (or three according to some) verses after the sajdah verse. The commentary discusses various opinions on what breaks fuur, noting that most Hanafi scholars do not specify a number but refer to the mujtahid's judgment. The text concludes with a recommendation for the imam to incorporate the sajdah into the prayer's ruku or sujud to avoid confusion.

Key Terms
فور التلاوة (fuur al-tilawah): The immediate time period after reciting a sajdah verse during which the sajdah should be performed.
نية (niyyah): Intent to perform the sajdah of recitation when doing ruku or sujud.

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the consequence if a worshiper recites three verses after a sajdah verse before performing sujud, according to the cautious view?
A) The sujud still suffices because intention is not required
B) The fuur is broken, so the sujud does not count; a separate sajdah is needed
C) The prayer becomes invalid
D) It is permissible but disliked

Key Takeaway
Intention is mandatory for ruku but not for sujud, and the fuur for sujud is generally broken by reciting more than two verses after the sajdah verse.

intermediate

Sajdah al-Tilawah Becomes a Debt When Fuur is Broken
Clarifying the consequence of breaking fuur for sajdah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when fuur of tilawah is broken and explain the Hanafi position on the necessity of intention for ruku and sujud in fulfilling the sajdah.

Core Idea
When the immediacy of recitation is lost, sajdah al-tilawah becomes a debt requiring specific intention to fulfill.

In this important note, al-Tahtawi clarifies that continuing to recite more than a couple of verses after a sajdah verse breaks the fuur (immediacy). The sajdah obligation does not vanish; it transforms into a debt (dayn) that must be paid with explicit intention. This leads to a nuanced discussion about whether that intention is required for ruku, sujud, both, or neither, with the preponderant Hanafi view requiring intention only for ruku.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition that breaks fuur
Recognize that the fuur of tilawah is broken when the reciter continues reading more than two or three verses after the sajdah verse. The text states 'إذا انقطع فور التلاوة' (when the fuur of recitation is cut).
The exact number (two or three) is derived from other Hanafi texts; the passage implies a clear break in immediacy.
2
State the consequence of broken fuur
The obligation of sajdah al-tilawah becomes a debt (dayn). It cannot be fulfilled by the ongoing prayer's ruku or sujud without specific intention. The worshiper must perform a separate ruku or sujud specifically for the sajdah, with the required intention.
3
Understand the imam-follower scenario
If the imam intends the sajdah in his ruku but the follower does not, the follower's prayer is not valid until he later prostrates and repeats the sitting. If he fully abandons it, the prayer is invalid. This ruling applies only to loud prayers (jihriyyah).
4
Analyze the ikhtilaf on intention
Three positions are presented: (1) no intention needed for either ruku or sujud, (2) intention needed for both, (3) intention needed only for ruku. The preponderant view (al-rajih) is the third: sujud fulfills the wajib in form and meaning, so no intention needed; ruku fulfills only in meaning, so intention is necessary.
Refer to the madhhab dispute map below for details.
5
Apply the ruling in practice
When fuur is broken, the worshiper must intentionally perform a separate ruku or sujud. For ruku, explicit intention is required; for sujud, the act itself suffices. After the prayer, if the imam intended the sajdah in ruku and the follower did not, the follower must make up the sajdah and repeat the sitting.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبيه مهم : إذا انقطع فور التلاوة صارت ديناً فلا بد من فعلها بنية فيأتي لها بسجود، أو ركوع خاص قال المحقق الكمال بن الهمام رحمه الله تعالى : فإن قلت قد قالوا : إن ركوع مستقلاً خوف الفساد من غيره ولو أخر ذلك بعد قوله وسجودها وإن لم ينوه لكان أولى، وفي الدر ولو نواها في ركوعه، ولم ينوها المؤتم لم يجزه ويسجد إذا سلم مع الإمام، ويعيد القعدة، ولو تركها فسدت صلاته كذا في القنية، وينبغي حمله على الجهرية اهـ، انظر هل الانبغاء للوجوب . قوله : (حتى لا يؤدي إلى التخليط أي على القوم إذا سجد لها سجوداً مستقلاً قوله : ( وإن لم ينوها لإحراز نية الصلاة لها لأنّ من نوى الصلاة نوى قراءتها، وهي من اتباع القراءة، واعلم أن في اشتراط النية وعدمه في كل من الركوع والسجود اختلافاً فمن لم يشترط قال : ينوب كل من الركوع والسجود عن سجدة التلاوة مطلقاً لأن الحاجة إلى تحصيل التعظيم في هذه الحالة وقد وجد ،نوى، أو لم ينو كالفرض ينوب عن تحية المسجد، وإن لم ينو، ومن اشترط قال : لاختلاف سبب الوجوب، فكان يعني سجدة التلاوة وكلا من الصلاة، وسجودها جنسين مختلفين فلا بد في إقامة غير الجنس عن الجنس من النية، ومن شرطها في الركوع دون السجود :قال هو بالسجود مؤد للواجب بصورته، ومعناه فلا يحتاج إلى النية، وأما بالركوع فمؤد له بمعناه فقط، فيحتاج إلى النية هذا ما يفيده كلام البدائع، وغيرها، وهناك أقوال أخرى حكاها العلامة الشمني وقد علمت الراجح، وهو ما في المصنف.
Important note: When the fuur of recitation is broken, it becomes a debt, so it must be performed with intention, so he performs for it a specific sujud or ruku. Al-Muhaqqiq Kamal ibn al-Humam, may Allah have mercy on him, said: For if you say: they have said that an independent ruku (is done) fearing corruption from another, and if he delays that after his statement 'and its sujud although he does not intend it' it would be more appropriate. And in al-Durr: if he intended it in his ruku, and the follower did not intend it, it is not valid for him, and he prostrates when he finishes with the imam, and he repeats the sitting, and if he leaves it, his prayer is invalidated, as in al-Quniyya, and it should be interpreted as in loud prayers. Look into whether the appropriateness indicates obligation. His statement: (so that it does not lead to confusion) i.e., upon the people if he prostrates for it independently. His statement: (and although he does not intend it) to secure the intention of prayer for it, because one who intends the prayer intends its recitation, and it is from following the recitation. And know that regarding the condition of intention or not in each of ruku and sujud, there is difference: those who do not condition it say: each of ruku and sujud absolutely suffices for sajdah al-tilawah because the need to achieve glorification in this situation exists, whether he intends or not, just as the obligatory (prayer) suffices for greeting the masjid even without intention. And those who condition it say: due to the difference in the cause of obligation, for sajdah al-tilawah and each of the prayer and its sujud are different genres, so it is necessary to have intention when substituting one genre for another. And those who condition it in ruku but not sujud said: he, by sujud, performs the wajib in its form and meaning, so does not need intention, but by ruku he performs it only in meaning, so needs intention. This is what the words of al-Bada'i' and others indicate, and there are other statements narrated by al-Shumni, and you know the preponderant, which is what is in the author's text.
Source pages p. 487

Commentary
This 'Important Note' addresses the consequence when the fuur (immediacy) of sajdah al-tilawah is broken—by reciting more than two (or three) verses after the sajdah verse. In such a case, the sajdah becomes a debt (dayn) on the reciter, meaning it cannot be fulfilled by the ongoing prayer's ruku or sujud without specific intention. Instead, one must perform a separate, intentional ruku or sujud specifically for the sajdah. The hashiya quotes Kamal ibn al-Humam, who discusses the case of an imam intending the sajdah in his ruku while the follower does not; the follower's prayer is not valid until he prostrates later and repeats the sitting. If he leaves it entirely, his prayer is invalid—but this applies only to loud prayers (jihriyyah). The commentary revisits the issue of intention for ruku vs. sujud, summarizing the three positions: (1) no intention needed for either, (2) intention needed for both, (3) intention needed only for ruku. The preponderant view (al-rajih) as per the author's text is that intention is required for ruku but not for sujud, provided fuur is not broken.

Key Terms
دين (dayn): A debt; here it means the obligation of sajdah remains pending and must be fulfilled with specific intention.
فور (fuur): Immediacy; the requirement to perform sajdah al-tilawah promptly upon reciting or hearing the verse, without significant delay.
نية (niyyah): Intention; here the specific intention to perform sajdah al-tilawah when substituting ruku or sujud for the obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does it mean to 'break the fuur' of sajdah al-tilawah in prayer?
A) Reciting the sajdah verse incorrectly
B) Reciting more than two or three verses after the sajdah verse before bowing
C) Forgetting to prostrate immediately after the verse
D) Changing the intention of the prayer

Key Takeaway
When the fuur of tilawah is broken, the sajdah al-tilawah becomes a debt requiring specific intention; according to the preponderant Hanafi view, intention is needed for ruku but not for sujud.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Intention for Sajdah al-Tilawah During Prayer
Explains the ruling of sajdah al-tilawah regarding intention and the interruption of faur

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state when intention is required for sajdah al-tilawah during prayer and identify the factor that triggers the requirement.

Core Idea
If faur is not interrupted, no intention needed; if interrupted, intention becomes wajib.

The Hanafi school recognizes a unique concept of faur (immediacy) for sajdah al-tilawah. During prayer, the normal bowing or prostration can substitute for the recitation prostration without separate intention, but only if the recitation's immediacy remains intact. This lesson unpacks the ruling, the ikhtilaf among Hanafi scholars, and the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The matn states that the prayer's prostration suffices for sajdah al-tilawah even without intention, as long as faur is not interrupted. Determine the hukm level: it is wajib but the substitution is valid without niyyah under this condition.
2
Define faur interruption
Interruption occurs by reciting more than two verses after the prostration verse (by consensus) or more than three (per al-Halwani). Also, extended actions can break faur.
Consensus on 2 or less not interrupting, 4 or more interrupting.
3
Understand the ikhtilaf
Some Hanafis require intention for substitution, citing different causes (sabab) of obligation. Others require intention only for bowing, not prostration. The chosen view is that intention is not needed within faur.
The disagreement is over whether ta'zim alone suffices.
4
Apply the ruling
If a person recites a prostration verse in prayer and immediately bows with the intention of the prayer's bowing, it counts for sajdah al-tilawah without separate niyyah. If faur is broken (e.g., recites 4 more verses), a separate prostration with intention is required.
The follower must intend the sajdah if the imam does not intend it; otherwise, he prostrates after salam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عنها أيضاً (سجودها) أي سجود الصلاة (وإن لم ينوها أي التلاوية (إذا لم ينقطع فور التلاوة) وانقطاعه بأن يقرأ أكثر من (آيتين) بعد آية سجدة التلاوة بالإجماع، وقال شمس الأئمة الحلواني: لا ينقطع الفور ما لم يقرأ أكثر من ثلاث آيات، وقال الكمال: إن قول شمس الأئمة هو الرواية .
تنبيه مهم : إذا انقطع فور التلاوة صارت ديناً فلا بد من فعلها بنية فيأتي لها بسجود، أو ركوع خاص قال المحقق الكمال بن الهمام رحمه الله تعالى : فإن قلت قد قالوا : إن ركوع مستقلاً خوف الفساد من غيره ولو أخر ذلك بعد قوله وسجودها وإن لم ينوه لكان أولى، وفي الدر ولو نواها في ركوعه، ولم ينوها المؤتم لم يجزه ويسجد إذا سلم مع الإمام، ويعيد القعدة، ولو تركها فسدت صلاته كذا في القنية، وينبغي حمله على الجهرية اهـ، انظر هل الانبغاء للوجوب . قوله : (حتى لا يؤدي إلى التخليط أي على القوم إذا سجد لها سجوداً مستقلاً قوله : ( وإن لم ينوها لإحراز نية الصلاة لها لأنّ من نوى الصلاة نوى قراءتها، وهي من اتباع القراءة، واعلم أن في اشتراط النية وعدمه في كل من الركوع والسجود اختلافاً فمن لم يشترط قال : ينوب كل من الركوع والسجود عن سجدة التلاوة مطلقاً لأن الحاجة إلى تحصيل التعظيم في هذه الحالة وقد وجد ،نوى، أو لم ينو كالفرض ينوب عن تحية المسجد، وإن لم ينو، ومن اشترط قال : لاختلاف سبب الوجوب، فكان يعني سجدة التلاوة وكلا من الصلاة، وسجودها جنسين مختلفين فلا بد في إقامة غير الجنس عن الجنس من النية، ومن شرطها في الشمني وقد علمت الراجح، وهو ما في المصنف. قوله : (إذا لم ينقطع) مرتبط بالركوع والسجود جميعاً. قوله : (بأن يقرأ أكثر من آيتين) اعلم أن الفور لا ينقطع بآية بعد آيتها، أو آيتين اتفاقاً وينقطع بأربع اتفاقاً، واختلف في الثلاث، فقيل: ينقطع واختاره خواهر زاده وقيل: لا واختاره الحلواني وهو أصح من جهة الرواية كما في الحلبي، والأول أصح من جهة الدراية لأنه أحوط كما ذكره المؤلف، وفي البدائع، وأكثر مشايخنا لم يقدروا في ذلك تقديراً، فكان الظاهر أنهم يفوضون ذلك إلى رأي المجتهد كما فعلوا ذلك في كثير من المواضع، وهو الأوجه أو يعتبر ما يعد طويلاً اهـ. قوله : (تنبيه مهم الخ) الأولى ما فعله السيد من حذفه لأن المؤلف وضع للمبتدي، وهذا لا يليق به، بل محل إيضاحه باب القياس من كتب الأصول. قوله : (إذا انقطع فور التلاوة) أي بتلاوة أربع آیات بعد آيتها اتفاقاً، وبالثلاث على الخلاف أو بما يعد طويلاً قوله : (فيأتي لها بسجود، أو ركوع خاص لفوات المحل، والدين يقضي بما له لا بما عليه والركوع والسجود عليه، فلا يتأدى بهما الدين بخلاف ما لم تصر ديناً كما لو ركع، أو سجد فور التلاوة، لأن الحاجة هو تأديتها في ضمن الركوع هو القياس والاستحسان عدمه والقياس هنا مقدم على الاستحسان فأسعفني بكشف هذا المقام فالجواب أن مرادهم من الاستحسان ما خفي من المعاني التي يناط بها الحكم ومن القياس ما كان ظاهراً متبادراً فظهر من هذا أن الاستحسان لا يقابل بالقياس المحدود في الأصول بل هو أعم منه فقد يكون الاستحسان بالنص، وقد يكون بمن مقدم في كشف التعظيم عند تلك التلاوة، وقد وجد في ضمنها فيكفي كداخل المسجد إذا صلى الفرض كفاه عن تحية المسجد لحصول تعظيم المسجد أفاده في الشرح.
Also from it (its prostration) i.e. the prostration of prayer (even if he did not intend it) i.e. the recitation prostration (if the immediacy of the recitation has not been interrupted) and its interruption is by reciting more than (two verses) after the verse of the prostration of recitation by consensus. Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani said: the immediacy is not interrupted unless he recites more than three verses. Al-Kamal said: the statement of Shams al-A'imma is the narration. Important note: If the immediacy of the recitation is interrupted, it becomes a debt, so it is necessary to perform it with intention, so one brings for it a prostration or a specific bowing. Al-Muhaqqiq Kamal ibn al-Humam said: if you say: they said: independent bowing for fear of corruption from other than it, and if he delayed that after his statement 'and its prostration even if he did not intend it' would be better. In al-Durr: if he intended it in his bowing, and the follower did not intend it, it does not suffice him, and he prostrates when he says salam with the imam, and repeats the sitting, and if he leaves it, his prayer becomes invalid. Likewise in al-Quniya, and it should be applied to the audible prayers. Look: is the 'should' for obligation? His statement: (so that it does not lead to confusion) i.e. for the people if they prostrate for it independently. His statement: (even if he did not intend it) because the intention of prayer includes it, because whoever intends prayer intends its recitation, and it is part of following the recitation. Know that there is a difference of opinion on the condition of intention in both bowing and prostration. Those who do not stipulate it say: each of bowing and prostration substitutes for the recitation prostration absolutely, because the need to attain magnification in this case has been found, whether he intended or not, like the obligatory prayer suffices for the greeting of the mosque even if he did not intend. Those who stipulate say: due to the difference in the cause of obligation, so the recitation prostration and each of prayer and its prostration are two different genera, so it is necessary to have intention when substituting one genus for another. Those who stipulate it in bowing but not prostration say: he performs the obligation with prostration in form and meaning, so he does not need intention; as for bowing, he performs it only in meaning, so he needs intention. This is what the words of al-Bada'i' and others indicate. There are other sayings narrated by al-Shamni, and you have known the preponderant, which is what is in the matn. His statement: (if it is not interrupted) is connected to both bowing and prostration. His statement: (by reciting more than two verses) know that the immediacy is not interrupted by one verse after it, or two verses by agreement, and it is interrupted by four by agreement. There is a difference in three: it is said it is interrupted – chosen by Kharazada, and it is said it is not – chosen by al-Halwani, and it is more correct in terms of narration as in al-Halabi, and the first is more correct in terms of reasoning because it is more precautionary as mentioned by the author. In al-Bada'i': most of our shaykhs did not set an estimate for that, so it appears that they delegated that to the opinion of the mujtahid, as they did in many places, and it is the most appropriate, or what is considered lengthy is considered. His statement: (Important note, etc.) The best is what al-Sayyid did in deleting it, because the author wrote for beginners, and this is not suitable for him; rather, its place of clarification is the chapter of qiyas in books of usul. His statement: (if the immediacy of the recitation is interrupted) i.e. by reciting four verses after its verse by agreement, and by three according to the difference, or by what is considered lengthy. His statement: (then he brings for it a prostration or a specific bowing) because the occasion has passed, and a debt is repaid with what is for it not with what is upon it; bowing and prostration are upon it [the prayer], so the debt is not performed by them, unlike when it has not become a debt, like if he bowed or prostrated immediately after the recitation, because the need is to perform it within the bowing – this is qiyas, and istihsan is its absence, and here qiyas is given precedence over istihsan. So assist me in uncovering this matter. The answer: they mean by istihsan the hidden meanings upon which the ruling is based, and by qiyas what is apparent and obvious, so it appears from this that istihsan is not opposed to the qiyas defined in usul, but rather it is more general than it, for istihsan may be by text, and may be by precedence in uncovering the magnification at that recitation, and it has been found within it, so it suffices, like the one entering a mosque: if he prays the obligatory prayer, it suffices him for the greeting of the mosque due to obtaining magnification of the mosque. This is stated in al-Sharh.
Source pages p. 487

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi is a critical refinement of the rulings on sajdah al-tilawah (prostration of recitation) within the prayer. The author begins by stating the ruling: the normal prostration (sajdah) or bowing (ruku') of prayer can substitute for the sajdah al-tilawah even without specific intention, provided that the immediacy (faur) of the recitation has not been interrupted. The interruption of faur is defined by consensus as reciting more than two verses after the verse of prostration; al-Halwani reports a narration that it is three verses, and al-Kamal prefers this as the transmitted view. The author then discusses the important note (tanbih muhimm): if the faur is interrupted, the sajdah becomes a debt (dayn) on the person, and it must be performed with specific intention, either by a separate prostration or a specific bowing. Kamal ibn al-Humam notes that some scholars said a separate bowing is fear of corruption from other factors, and delaying it after the prayer's prostration would be better. Referring to al-Durr, if a person intends the sajdah in their bowing but the follower does not, the follower's prayer is not invalidated but he must prostrate after the imam's salam and repeat the tashahhud; leaving it altogether invalidates the prayer. This ruling is applicable to audible prayers. The author then clarifies the condition of intention: there is ikhtilaf among Hanafi scholars. Some say intention is not required because both bowing and prostration achieve the same magnification (ta'zim) as the recitation prostration, similar to how an obligatory prayer suffices for the greeting of the mosque (tahiyyat al-masjid) without separate intention. Others say intention is required because the causes of obligation differ, so the acts are different genera, and substitution requires intention. A third view requires intention for bowing but not for prostration, because prostration fulfills both form and meaning, while bowing fulfills only meaning. The author notes that the preponderant (rajih) view is that in the matn (Maraqi al-Falah), which is the position of the majority. The passage then elaborates on the estimation of faur interruption: consensus says one or two verses do not interrupt, four do, and there is difference on three. Some scholars set no fixed number, delegating to the observer's judgment, which is considered the most appropriate (awjah). The author criticizes the inclusion of the tanbih in the matn for beginners, saying it belongs in usul al-fiqh. Finally, the passage addresses a potential objection about giving precedence to qiyas over istihsan in this ruling. The response is that the qiyas here is apparent (jali) while the istihsan is hidden (khafi), and they are not the same as defined in usul; the qiyas is given precedence due to stronger evidence, including reports from Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn 'Umar allowing bowing to substitute for the prostration, with no known opposition, making it akin to consensus.

Key Terms
الفور (al-fawr): Immediacy: the short period after reciting a verse of prostration during which one can substitute the prayer's prostration or bowing for sajdah al-tilawah without separate intention.
الدين (al-dayn): Debt: a missed obligation that becomes due after the faur period, requiring deliberate performance with intention.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the chosen Hanafi position, when does the normal prostration or bowing in prayer NOT require a separate intention for sajdah al-tilawah?
A) After reciting more than two verses
B) When the faur is not interrupted
C) When the imam intends it for the follower
D) At any time during the prayer

Key Takeaway
Sajdah al-tilawah during prayer can be fulfilled by the prayer's own sujud or ruku' without intention as long as the faur (immediacy) is not interrupted; if interrupted, intention becomes required and the sajdah becomes a debt.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Qiyas Over Istihsan: Ruku' Substituting for Sajdah al-Tilawah
Resolving qiyas vs istihsan via companion precedent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school gives precedence to qiyas over istihsan in permitting ruku' to substitute for sajdah al-tilawah, and state the practical difference between the two views.

Core Idea
When companion practice supports qiyas, it overrides istihsan — even though istihsan normally takes precedence.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi addresses a nuanced dispute within the Hanafi school: whether ruku' during prayer can substitute for the obligatory sajdah al-tilawah. The general principle is that istihsan (juristic preference) overrides qiyas (analogy), but here the author shows that qiyas is given precedence due to strong supporting evidence from the Companions. Understanding this case clarifies how the Hanafi school prioritises different proof sources when they conflict.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ikhtilaf (Dispute)
Recognize that the dispute is about the scope of substituting ruku' for sajdah al-tilawah: some limit it to within prayer, others apply it absolutely. The core conflict is between qiyas (allowing substitution) and istihsan (disallowing it).
The text notes ikhtilaf on the scope, but focuses on the qiyas-istihsan conflict.
2
State the Qiyas Argument
Qiyas holds that the purpose of both ruku' and sujud is ta'zim (magnification) of Allah. Since both achieve the same goal, ruku' can fulfill the obligation of sajdah al-tilawah.
The 'illa is ta'zim, which is a jali (apparent) cause.
3
State the Istihsan Argument
Istihsan argues that the obligation is ta'zim with a specific description (the act of prostration). Therefore, no other act can substitute.
This is a hidden qiyas (qiyas khafi) that normally prevails over apparent qiyas.
4
Identify the Tarjih (Preponderance) and Its Basis
Imam Muhammad preferred qiyas because reports from Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn 'Umar permitted bowing to substitute, and no companion opposed, creating an implied consensus (sukut = ijma). This strengthened the qiyas, overriding the istihsan.
The existence of a preponderance (murajjih) is key: companion practice and tacit consensus.
5
Note the Thamarah al-Khilaf (Practical Consequence)
According to the qiyas-based view, if a person in prayer recites a prostration verse and then goes into ruku', the ruku' suffices. According to istihsan, a separate prostration is still required.
This affects whether the prayer is valid without additional sujud.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (فإن قلت الخ) اختلف في محل القياس، والاستحسان فذكر العامة أنه في إقامة الركوع مقام السجدة في الصلاة فقط، وقال بعضهم في إقامته عنها مطلقاً، وقد علمت الخلاف في ذلك، قوله: (هو القياس) وجه القياس أن المقصود من السجود تعظيم الله تعالى أما اقتداء عظمه، وهم أولياؤه تعالى، أو مخالفة لمن استكبر، وهم أعداؤه تعالى، وذلك يحصل بالركوع كما يحصل بالسجود فهما في التعظيم جنس واحد قوله والاستحسان (عدمه أي عدم His statement: ('If you say, etc.') There is a difference in the place of qiyas and istihsan. The general scholars mentioned that it is specifically about substituting bowing for prostration in prayer only. Some said it is about substituting it absolutely, and you have known the difference in that. His statement: ('It is qiyas') The basis of qiyas is that the purpose of prostration is to magnify Allah Almighty, either by emulating His greatness – and they are His friends – or by opposing those who are arrogant – they are His enemies – and that is achieved by bowing just as it is by prostration, so they are one genus in magnification. His statement: 'and istihsan (is) its absence' i.e., the non-performance of it within it, because the obligatory is magnification with a specific description, so nothing else stands in its place. His statement: ('and qiyas here') i.e., in this issue, is given precedence over istihsan. Muhammad said: we adopt qiyas, even though the principle is to act by istihsan, because qiyas is strengthened by what is reported from Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn 'Umar: they permitted bowing in place of prostration in prayer, and no opposition was seen from others, so it was like consensus, so it was given precedence over istihsan due to the existence of a preponderance. His statement: ('so assist me') with a 'ayn then 'fa', meaning fulfilling the need, i.e., fulfill my need, as the Qamus explained. So his statement 'by uncovering this matter' may mean the 'ba' is for illustration with an opinion: fulfill the need which is this matter, and it may mean the need is understanding, so the 'ba' is for causation, and the intent is to explain why qiyas is given precedence here over istihsan. The answer will come that it is given precedence due to the strength of its evidence. What occurs in other versions from other than this root is a corruption. His statement: ('of the meanings') i.e., the effective causes. His statement: ('upon which') i.e., are attached the rulings, whether the istihsan is by text, necessity, or qiyas. His statement: ('obvious') clear, perceived with minimal reflection. His statement: ('from this') i.e., the intended meaning. His statement: ('is not opposed to the qiyas defined in usul') Know that qiyas linguistically means estimation: one says 'I measured the sandal with the sandal' i.e., I estimated it with it. In Shari'ah, as in al-Manar: the estimation of the branch from the original in the 'illa and the ruling. Al-Muhaqqiq in al-Tahrir chose that it is the equality of one place to another in the 'illa of a legal ruling that is not understood from its text by mere linguistic understanding, so it is not measured linguistically. Abu Mansur al-Maturidi defined it: making evident the like of the ruling of one of the two mentioned things with the like of its 'illa in the other. Istihsan linguistically: counting something good. In al-Talwih: opinions have settled that it is a name for an agreed-upon evidence, whether it be text, consensus, or hidden qiyas, when it occurs in opposition to a qiyas that first comes to mind, so that it is not applied to the evidence itself without opposition. Thus it is a proof according to everyone without conceivable disagreement. Then it prevailed in the terminology of usul specifically for hidden qiyas, just as the name qiyas prevailed for apparent qiyas, to distinguish between them.
Source pages p. 488

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi continues the discussion on substituting ruku' for sajdah al-tilawah, focusing on the conflict between qiyas and istihsan. The author begins by noting ikhtilaf on the scope of the issue: some say it is limited to substituting bowing for prostration only within a prayer, while others say it applies absolutely. He then presents the basis of qiyas: the purpose of prostration is ta'zim (magnification) of Allah, which is achieved by both sujud and ruku' because both are acts of humility. Thus they are of the same genus in magnification. The opposing view, istihsan, holds that the obligation is ta'zim with a specific description (the act of prostration itself), so nothing else can substitute. The author then gives the tarjih: Imam Muhammad said we adopt qiyas, even though normally istihsan takes precedence, because here qiyas is strengthened by reports from Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn 'Umar who permitted bowing to substitute for prostration in prayer, and no companion opposed them, so it is like ijma' (consensus). Therefore, qiyas is given precedence over istihsan due to this preponderance. The author then explains the meaning of 'fasa'fani' and the structure of the objection and answer. The passage concludes with definitions of qiyas and istihsan from usul al-fiqh: qiyas linguistically means estimation, and technically means equating a branch to an original in its 'illa and ruling. Istihsan technically means a hidden qiyas that prevails over an apparent qiyas due to stronger evidence. Thus, in this issue, the apparent qiyas supporting substitution is considered istihsan in a broader sense, but the qiyas given precedence is the one supported by companion practice.

Key Terms
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): A hidden qiyas that is preferred over an apparent qiyas due to stronger evidence, or a ruling based on public interest (maslahah) without strict analogy.
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning: equating a branch case to an original case in the effective cause ('illa) to apply the same ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did Imam Muhammad prefer qiyas over istihsan in allowing ruku' to substitute for sajdah al-tilawah?
A) Because istihsan is not a valid source
B) Because the qiyas was supported by companion practice with no opposition
C) Because the matn explicitly stated so
D) Because qiyas is always stronger than istihsan

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, qiyas can override istihsan when supported by companion consensus.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Can Sajdah Tilawah Be Performed Within Ruku'? Qiyas vs Istihsan
Methodological dispute on substituting ruku' for sajdah tilawah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling that sajdah tilawah can be performed within ruku' and evaluate the methodological conflict between qiyas and istihsan.

Core Idea
Ruku' can substitute for sajdah tilawah because both share the same purpose of reverence, supported by Companion practice.

This lesson examines a subtle methodological debate: can the wajib act of sajdah tilawah be fulfilled by bowing (ruku') during prayer? The Hanafi school navigates between two legal reasoning methods — qiyas and istihsan — to arrive at the operative ruling. Understanding this dispute illuminates how preference (tarjih) works when multiple reasoning tools conflict.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
Determine what is being debated: whether performing sajdah tilawah within ruku' is valid. Note that the dispute is between qiyas (allowing it) and istihsan (disallowing it).
The passage also notes a related dispute on whether this substitution applies only in prayer or absolutely.
2
Analyze the qiyas argument
Understand the basis of the analogy: both ruku' and sujud aim to show reverence (ta'zim) to Allah. Since reverence is the common goal, they are considered one genus (jins wahid). Therefore, ruku' suffices for sajdah.
The 'illa is ta'zim.
3
Analyze the istihsan argument
Istihsan argues that the obligation is reverence with a specific posture (sajdah), and that specific description cannot be substituted by another posture.
The istihsan here is based on the idea that the specific form matters.
4
Evaluate the preponderating evidence
The qiyas is given precedence (muqaddam) over istihsan because it is supported by the practice of Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn 'Umar, who allowed it, with no known opposition — making it akin to consensus (ka'l-ijma').
Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani is reported to have said: 'We take by qiyas.'
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The operative ruling (mufta bihi) is that performing sajdah tilawah within ruku' is valid and suffices, based on the preponderance of qiyas.
This is the view acted upon in the Hanafi school.

عنه
If you say... there is a difference regarding the place of qiyas and istihsan. The general scholars mentioned that it is in substituting ruku' for prostration in prayer only, and some said absolutely. You know the disagreement on that. His statement: 'It is qiyas.' The basis of qiyas is that the purpose of prostration is to show reverence to Allah Almighty, either in emulation of His greatness (which is done by His friends) or in opposition to those who are arrogant (His enemies). This is achieved by ruku' as it is achieved by prostration, so they are one genus in reverence. His statement: 'And istihsan is its absence.' That is, the non-performance within it, because what is obligatory is reverence with a specific description, so nothing else takes its place. His statement: 'And qiyas here,' i.e., in this issue, is given precedence over istihsan. Muhammad said: We act by qiyas, even though the principle is to act by istihsan, because qiyas is preponderated by what is narrated from Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn 'Umar that they allowed performing ruku' in place of prostration in prayer, and no opposition from others was seen, so it is like consensus, so qiyas was given precedence due to the presence of a preponderating factor. His statement: 'So assist me' ... The letters are 'ayn and fa, meaning fulfilling a need, i.e., fulfill my need. So his statement 'by uncovering this place' may have the ba for representation, meaning fulfill the need that is this place, or it may be that the need is understanding, so the ba is for causality, and the meaning is to explain why qiyas is given precedence over istihsan here. It will come in the answer that it was given precedence due to the strength of its evidence. What occurs in copies other than this material is corruption. His statement: 'Of the meanings,' i.e., the causes. His statement: 'Upon which it depends,' i.e., to which rulings are attached, whether istihsan is by text, necessity, or qiyas. His statement: 'Prevalent,' i.e., clear, perceived with minimal reflection. His statement: 'From this,' i.e., the intended meaning. His statement: 'Is not comparable to qiyas as defined in usul.' Know that qiyas linguistically is estimation: it is said 'I measured the sandal with the sandal' i.e., I estimated it with it. In Shari'ah, as in al-Manar, it is the estimation of a branch with the root in the 'illa and ruling. The verifier in al-Tahrir chose that it is the equality of a place with another in the 'illa of a Shari'ah ruling that is not perceived from its text by mere linguistic understanding, so qiyas is not in language. Abu Mansur al-Maturidi defined it as showing the like of the ruling of one of the two mentioned with the like of its 'illa in the other. Istihsan in language is regarding something as good. In al-Talwih: opinions have settled that it is a name for an agreed-upon evidence, whether text, consensus, or hidden qiyas, when it occurs in opposition to a qiyas that minds jump to first, so it is not applied to the evidence itself without opposition. Thus it is a proof for everyone without conceiving a disagreement. Then it became predominant in the terminology of usul to specifically mean hidden qiyas, just as the name qiyas became predominant for apparent qiyas, to differentiate between them necessarily. And it may be by qiyas if there is another prevalent qiyas, and that is hidden, and it is the correct qiyas, so the hidden one is called istihsan relative to that prevalent one. Thus it is established that the name istihsan in some forms is the correct qiyas, and its counterpart is called qiyas due to similarity, and because the counterpart qiyas is what is apparent relative to istihsan. Muhammad ibn Salamah thought that the solid [?] is the one that stands in place of ... in the two qiyas. As for branches, applying istihsan to text and consensus when they occur in opposition to apparent qiyas is common. This is from the commentary of Shaykh Zain on al-Manar. His statement: 'Rather it is,' i.e., istihsan. His statement: 'It may be' in the context of explaining the generality. His statement: 'By text,' such as salam (forward sale), because qiyas forbids its permissibility due to the absence of the contracted item at the time of contract, but we leave qiyas by the text: 'Whoever gives salam, let him give salam...' and the hadith forbidding selling what is not with a person, but allowing salam. His statement: 'And it may be by necessity,' like purifying vessels, wells, and basins, because qiyas forbids purifying these things after their najasah due to the unavailability of water for the well's purification, and likewise the water in the basin, and what springs from the well that became najis by meeting impurity, and the bucket becomes najis as well, so it continues to bubble while still najis, and likewise water if there is no hole at its bottom because the najis water collects at its base, so it is not ruled pure. His statement: 'And it may be by qiyas,' like the purity of the leftover (su'r) of birds of prey such as the falcon and hawk, because the apparent qiyas is that their leftover is najis since they are predators, but in istihsan it is pure because the predator is not inherently najis, evidenced by the permissibility of utilizing it legally, and its najasah is established necessarily due to the prohibition of its meat, so we established a ruling between two rulings, which is neighboring najasah. Thus the quality of najasah is established in its moisture and saliva. Birds of prey drink with their beak by taking and then swallowing, and the bone is pure in itself, free from the neighbor of najasah. Do you not see that the bone of a dead animal is pure? So the bone of a living animal is more so. Thus for this, there is an inner that negates that apparent [najasah], so the ruling of the apparent falls due to its absence, but it is makruh because they do not avoid dead animals, so they are like a roaming chicken. This is from the mentioned commentary. The author remained silent on what is istihsan by consensus, which is what people deal with called istisna' (commissioned manufacture) like the stitching of the khuff, while qiyas forbids it because it is a sale of a non-existent item. His statement: 'When there is another prevalent qiyas,' such as the leftover of land predators, because the apparent qiyas for it is najasah as mentioned. And here it is complete. His statement: 'And that is hidden,' i.e., istihsan which is by qiyas. His statement: 'And it is the correct qiyas,' i.e., the hidden qiyas expressed as istihsan. His statement: 'So the hidden one is called,' i.e., the correct hidden qiyas. His statement: 'To that prevalent one,' i.e., the clear apparent qiyas such as najasah in the leftover of birds of prey for example. His statement: 'In some forms,' including the leftover of birds of prey. His statement: 'And it is the correct qiyas,' i.e., the hidden qiyas, which is the purity of their leftover. His statement: 'Counterpart,' i.e., counterpart to the correct one, which is the apparent qiyas. His statement: 'Due to similarity,' i.e., its similarity to qiyas in appearance, otherwise it is corrupt, outside the correct qiyas. His statement: 'And because of the qiyas being,' attached to 'thought.' His statement: 'the counterpart,' with jar as an adjective for qiyas, and his statement 'what appeared' is the predicate.
Source pages p. 488

Commentary
This is a critical refinement from Al-Tahtawi's Hashiyah on Maraqi al-Falah, analyzing the debate between qiyas and istihsan regarding performing the prostration of recitation (sajdah tilawah) within the bowing (ruku') of prayer. The passage type is a methodological dispute within the Hanafi school about which legal reasoning takes precedence. The author first presents the positions: by qiyas, performing sajdah in ruku' suffices because both ruku' and sujud involve the same essential purpose — ta'zim (reverence) of Allah. The basis of the analogy is that the purpose of prostration is to show reverence, which is equally achieved by bowing. Thus they are of the same genus ('jins wahid') in reverence. By istihsan, it does not suffice because the obligation is reverence with a specific posture (sajdah), and that specific description cannot be substituted by another. Imam Muhammad (al-Shaybani) is reported to have said: 'We act by qiyas,' even though the general principle is to act by istihsan. The preponderance of qiyas here is due to the transmission from Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn 'Umar that they allowed performing ruku' in place of sajdah in prayer, and no opposition from others was known, making it akin to consensus (ka'l-ijma'). Thus qiyas is given precedence because of this supporting evidence. The rest of the passage expands on the definitions of qiyas and istihsan from usul al-fiqh, clarifying that istihsan is often a hidden analogy (qiyas khafi) opposed to an apparent analogy (qiyas jaliy). Numerous examples are given: istihsan by text (salam sale), by necessity (purification of wells), and by qiyas (purity of leftover of birds of prey). The key lesson is that when two modes of reasoning conflict, the one with stronger evidence (whether textual or rational) is given preference, and in this case qiyas prevailed due to the quasi-consensus of the Sahaba. All examples are classic Hanafi applications of istihsan.

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning: applying the ruling of an original case (asl) to a new case (far') due to a shared effective cause ('illa). In this passage, qiyas is used to equate ruku' with sujud in terms of reverence.
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Juristic preference: a method of departing from an apparent analogy due to a stronger evidence (text, consensus, necessity, or hidden analogy). In this text, it is the view that performing sajdah within ruku' does not suffice.
سجدة التلاوة (sajdat al-tilawah): The prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a verse of prostration (ayat al-sajdah) in the Quran.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the main reason the qiyas argument is given precedence over istihsan for sajdah tilawah within ruku'?
A) Qiyas is inherently stronger than istihsan in all cases.
B) There is an explicit Quranic verse allowing ruku' to replace sujud.
C) The practice of Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn 'Umar supporting it, with no known opposition, is like consensus.
D) The majority of Hanafi scholars prefer istihsan, but Imam Muhammad disagreed.

Key Takeaway
When qiyas and istihsan conflict, the one with stronger evidence (here, quasi-ijma') is given precedence, and the operative ruling is that performing sajdah tilawah within ruku' is valid.

Definitions and Types of Qiyas and Istihsan in Hanafi Usul
Definitions and types of qiyas and istihsan with examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define qiyas and istihsan as per Hanafi usul and identify the three types of istihsan (by text, necessity, and qiyas) with examples.

Core Idea
Istihsan is a hidden analogy that departs from apparent qiyas due to a stronger evidence, and it has three categories: text, necessity, and hidden qiyas.

In the latter part of the Hashiyah passage, the author provides a detailed exposition of the definitions of qiyas and istihsan, clarifying their technical meanings in Hanafi usul. This lesson unpacks these definitions and illustrates istihsan with classic examples: the salam sale, purification of wells, and the purity of the leftover of birds of prey.

Guided Path
1
Define qiyas and istihsan linguistically and technically
Start with the basic meanings: qiyas is estimation, istihsan is regarding something as good. Then move to the Shar'i definitions as given in the text.
The passage quotes al-Manar and al-Maturidi for qiyas, and al-Talwih for istihsan.
2
Differentiate between apparent (jaliy) and hidden (khafiy) qiyas
Understand that apparent qiyas is the first analogy that comes to mind, while hidden qiyas is a more subtle analogy that is often called istihsan.
This distinction is crucial for understanding why istihsan is sometimes equated with hidden qiyas.
3
Identify the three types of istihsan
The passage lists istihsan by text (e.g., salam), by necessity (e.g., purification of wells), and by qiyas (e.g., purity of birds of prey's leftover).
The author also mentions istihsan by consensus (istisna') but says the author remained silent on it.
4
Work through the example of salam (forward sale)
Apparent qiyas forbids it because the item is not present, but istihsan by text allows it based on the hadith permitting salam.
This shows that a specific text overrides general analogy.
5
Work through the example of birds of prey's leftover
Apparent qiyas classifies the saliva as najis because birds are predators. Hidden qiyas (istihsan) rules it pure because they drink by beak and the bone is pure, and they are not inherently najis.
This is a classic example of hidden qiyas overriding apparent qiyas.

عنه
If you say... there is a difference regarding the place of qiyas and istihsan. The general scholars mentioned that it is in substituting ruku' for prostration in prayer only, and some said absolutely. You know the disagreement on that. His statement: 'It is qiyas.' The basis of qiyas is that the purpose of prostration is to show reverence to Allah Almighty, either in emulation of His greatness (which is done by His friends) or in opposition to those who are arrogant (His enemies). This is achieved by ruku' as it is achieved by prostration, so they are one genus in reverence. His statement: 'And istihsan is its absence.' That is, the non-performance within it, because what is obligatory is reverence with a specific description, so nothing else takes its place. His statement: 'And qiyas here,' i.e., in this issue, is given precedence over istihsan. Muhammad said: We act by qiyas, even though the principle is to act by istihsan, because qiyas is preponderated by what is narrated from Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn 'Umar that they allowed performing ruku' in place of prostration in prayer, and no opposition from others was seen, so it is like consensus, so qiyas was given precedence due to the presence of a preponderating factor. His statement: 'So assist me' ... The letters are 'ayn and fa, meaning fulfilling a need, i.e., fulfill my need. So his statement 'by uncovering this place' may have the ba for representation, meaning fulfill the need that is this place, or it may be that the need is understanding, so the ba is for causality, and the meaning is to explain why qiyas is given precedence over istihsan here. It will come in the answer that it was given precedence due to the strength of its evidence. What occurs in copies other than this material is corruption. His statement: 'Of the meanings,' i.e., the causes. His statement: 'Upon which it depends,' i.e., to which rulings are attached, whether istihsan is by text, necessity, or qiyas. His statement: 'Prevalent,' i.e., clear, perceived with minimal reflection. His statement: 'From this,' i.e., the intended meaning. His statement: 'Is not comparable to qiyas as defined in usul.' Know that qiyas linguistically is estimation: it is said 'I measured the sandal with the sandal' i.e., I estimated it with it. In Shari'ah, as in al-Manar, it is the estimation of a branch with the root in the 'illa and ruling. The verifier in al-Tahrir chose that it is the equality of a place with another in the 'illa of a Shari'ah ruling that is not perceived from its text by mere linguistic understanding, so qiyas is not in language. Abu Mansur al-Maturidi defined it as showing the like of the ruling of one of the two mentioned with the like of its 'illa in the other. Istihsan in language is regarding something as good. In al-Talwih: opinions have settled that it is a name for an agreed-upon evidence, whether text, consensus, or hidden qiyas, when it occurs in opposition to a qiyas that minds jump to first, so it is not applied to the evidence itself without opposition. Thus it is a proof for everyone without conceiving a disagreement. Then it became predominant in the terminology of usul to specifically mean hidden qiyas, just as the name qiyas became predominant for apparent qiyas, to differentiate between them necessarily. And it may be by qiyas if there is another prevalent qiyas, and that is hidden, and it is the correct qiyas, so the hidden one is called istihsan relative to that prevalent one. Thus it is established that the name istihsan in some forms is the correct qiyas, and its counterpart is called qiyas due to similarity, and because the counterpart qiyas is what is apparent relative to istihsan. Muhammad ibn Salamah thought that the solid [?] is the one that stands in place of ... in the two qiyas. As for branches, applying istihsan to text and consensus when they occur in opposition to apparent qiyas is common. This is from the commentary of Shaykh Zain on al-Manar. His statement: 'Rather it is,' i.e., istihsan. His statement: 'It may be' in the context of explaining the generality. His statement: 'By text,' such as salam (forward sale), because qiyas forbids its permissibility due to the absence of the contracted item at the time of contract, but we leave qiyas by the text: 'Whoever gives salam, let him give salam...' and the hadith forbidding selling what is not with a person, but allowing salam. His statement: 'And it may be by necessity,' like purifying vessels, wells, and basins, because qiyas forbids purifying these things after their najasah due to the unavailability of water for the well's purification, and likewise the water in the basin, and what springs from the well that became najis by meeting impurity, and the bucket becomes najis as well, so it continues to bubble while still najis, and likewise water if there is no hole at its bottom because the najis water collects at its base, so it is not ruled pure. His statement: 'And it may be by qiyas,' like the purity of the leftover (su'r) of birds of prey such as the falcon and hawk, because the apparent qiyas is that their leftover is najis since they are predators, but in istihsan it is pure because the predator is not inherently najis, evidenced by the permissibility of utilizing it legally, and its najasah is established necessarily due to the prohibition of its meat, so we established a ruling between two rulings, which is neighboring najasah. Thus the quality of najasah is established in its moisture and saliva. Birds of prey drink with their beak by taking and then swallowing, and the bone is pure in itself, free from the neighbor of najasah. Do you not see that the bone of a dead animal is pure? So the bone of a living animal is more so. Thus for this, there is an inner that negates that apparent [najasah], so the ruling of the apparent falls due to its absence, but it is makruh because they do not avoid dead animals, so they are like a roaming chicken. This is from the mentioned commentary. The author remained silent on what is istihsan by consensus, which is what people deal with called istisna' (commissioned manufacture) like the stitching of the khuff, while qiyas forbids it because it is a sale of a non-existent item. His statement: 'When there is another prevalent qiyas,' such as the leftover of land predators, because the apparent qiyas for it is najasah as mentioned. And here it is complete. His statement: 'And that is hidden,' i.e., istihsan which is by qiyas. His statement: 'And it is the correct qiyas,' i.e., the hidden qiyas expressed as istihsan. His statement: 'So the hidden one is called,' i.e., the correct hidden qiyas. His statement: 'To that prevalent one,' i.e., the clear apparent qiyas such as najasah in the leftover of birds of prey for example. His statement: 'In some forms,' including the leftover of birds of prey. His statement: 'And it is the correct qiyas,' i.e., the hidden qiyas, which is the purity of their leftover. His statement: 'Counterpart,' i.e., counterpart to the correct one, which is the apparent qiyas. His statement: 'Due to similarity,' i.e., its similarity to qiyas in appearance, otherwise it is corrupt, outside the correct qiyas. Commentary
This is a critical refinement from Al-Tahtawi's Hashiyah on Maraqi al-Falah, analyzing the debate between qiyas and istihsan regarding performing the prostration of recitation (sajdah tilawah) within the bowing (ruku') of prayer. The passage type is a methodological dispute within the Hanafi school about which legal reasoning takes precedence. The author first presents the positions: by qiyas, performing sajdah in ruku' suffices because both ruku' and sujud involve the same essential purpose — ta'zim (reverence) of Allah. The basis of the analogy is that the purpose of prostration is to show reverence, which is equally achieved by bowing. Thus they are of the same genus ('jins wahid') in reverence. By istihsan, it does not suffice because the obligation is reverence with a specific posture (sajdah), and that specific description cannot be substituted by another. Imam Muhammad (al-Shaybani) is reported to have said: 'We act by qiyas,' even though the general principle is to act by istihsan. The preponderance of qiyas here is due to the transmission from Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn 'Umar that they allowed performing ruku' in place of sajdah in prayer, and no opposition from others was known, making it akin to consensus (ka'l-ijma'). Thus qiyas is given precedence because of this supporting evidence. The rest of the passage expands on the definitions of qiyas and istihsan from usul al-fiqh, clarifying that istihsan is often a hidden analogy (qiyas khafi) opposed to an apparent analogy (qiyas jaliy). Numerous examples are given: istihsan by text (salam sale), by necessity (purification of wells), and by qiyas (purity of leftover of birds of prey). The key lesson is that when two modes of reasoning conflict, the one with stronger evidence (whether textual or rational) is given preference, and in this case qiyas prevailed due to the quasi-consensus of the Sahaba. All examples are classic Hanafi applications of istihsan.

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning: estimating a branch to a root in the 'illa and ruling.
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Juristic preference: a departure from an apparent analogy due to a stronger evidence (text, consensus, necessity, or hidden qiyas).
سجدة التلاوة (sajdat al-tilawah): The prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a verse of prostration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the birds of prey example, what is the hidden 'illa that makes istihsan rule the leftover pure?
A) The bird is a predator, so its saliva is impure.
B) The bird drinks with its beak and its bone is pure, so the apparent najasah does not transfer.
C) The bird's meat is halal, so its saliva is pure.
D) The bird is wild, so its leftover is pure.

Key Takeaway
Istihsan is a legitimate Hanafi method of inference that departs from apparent qiyas when a stronger evidence (text, necessity, or hidden qiyas) supports a different ruling.
