Substituting Ruku' for Sajdah al-Tilawah: Qiyas vs. Istihsan
Intra-Hanafi dispute on substituting ruku' for tilawah prostration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi intra-school dispute on using ruku' for sajdah al-tilawah and state the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Ruku' can replace sujud for sajdah al-tilawah because both share the purpose of glorification.

This lesson examines a nuanced dispute within the Hanafi school: whether the obligatory prostration of recitation (sajdah al-tilawah) can be fulfilled by bowing (ruku') instead of prostrating. Imam Muhammad ibn al-Hasan initially differentiated between qiyas (which permits) and istihsan (which requires sujud), but the later mashayikh adopted the qiyas view. Understanding this dispute reveals how Hanafi jurists balance textual specificity with broader purposes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
Determine the exact legal question: can a person performing salah substitute ruku' for the sujud of sajdah al-tilawah?
The issue arises when one recites a tilawah verse during prayer and intends to fulfill the wajib by bowing instead of prostrating.
2
State Muhammad al-Shaybani's dual position
Muhammad presents two perspectives: according to qiyas, ruku' suffices because both are acts of prayer aimed at ta'zim; according to istihsan, only sujud fulfills the obligation because the legislated form is specific.
His initial statement distinguishes between the apparent ruling (qiyas) and the hidden preference (istihsan).
3
Analyze the reasoning for each view
For qiyas: glorification (ta'zim) is the shared meaning; for istihsan: the obligation is tied to the specific action of sujud, as evidenced by the fact that sujud alone suffices but ruku' alone does not.
Analogies: a missed fast day cannot compensate for another missed fast; similarly, one prostration cannot replace another obligation.
4
Note the tarjih (preference) of the mashayikh
The generality of the later Hanafi scholars (عامة المشايخ) overruled Muhammad's istihsan preference and adopted the qiyas ruling as the operative position.
This tarjih is based on the commonality of ta'zim and practical ease in worship.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: if one deliberately bows for sajdah al-tilawah, the obligation is discharged according to the mufta bihi view. If one follows Muhammad's initial istihsan, one would need to prostrate separately.
This is a valid ikhtilaf within the school; both positions are grounded in sound methodology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَسُئِلَ مُحَمَّدُ بْنُ سَلَمَةَ عَنِ الصُّلْبِيَّةِ هَلْ تَقُومُ مَقَامَ التِّلاَوِيَّةِ؟ فَقَالَ: أَمَّا فِي الْقِيَاسِ فَتَقُومُ، وَفِي الاِسْتِحْسَانِ لاَ تَقُومُ بَلِ الرُّكُوعُ هُوَ الْقَائِمُ مَقَامَهُمَا لِأَنَّ سُقُوطَ السَّجْدَةِ بِالسَّجْدَةِ أَمْرٌ ظَاهِرٌ فَكَانَ هُوَ الْقِيَاسَ، وَفِي الاِسْتِحْسَانِ لاَ يَجُوزُ لِأَنَّ السَّجْدَةَ قَائِمَةٌ مَقَامَ نَفْسِهَا فَلاَ تَقُومُ مَقَامَ غَيْرِهَا كَصَوْمِ يَوْمٍ مِنْ رَمَضَانَ لاَ يَقُومُ قَضَاءً عَنْ نَفْسِهِ وَعَنْ يَوْمٍ آخَرَ فَصَحَّ أَنَّ الْقِيَاسَ وَهُوَ الأَمْرُ الظَّاهِرُ هُنَا مُقَدَّمٌ عَلَى الاِسْتِحْسَانِ بِخِلاَفِ قِيَامِ الرُّكُوعِ مَقَامَهَا فَإِنَّ الْقِيَاسَ يَأْبَى الْجَوَازَ لأَنَّهُ الظَّاهِرُ وَفِي الاِسْتِحْسَانِ يَجُوزُ وَهُوَ الْخَفِيُّ فَكَانَ حِينَئِذٍ مِنْ تَقْدِيمِ الاِسْتِحْسَانِ لاَ الْقِيَاسِ لَكِنَّ عَامَّةَ الْمَشَايِخِ عَلَى أَنَّ الرُّكُوعَ هُوَ الْقَائِمُ مَقَامَهُمَا كَذَا ذَكَرَهُ مُحَمَّدٌ رَحِمَهُ اللهُ فِي الْكِتَابِ فَإِنَّهُ قَالَ: قُلْتُ: فَإِنْ أَرَادَ أَنْ يَرْكَعَ بِالسَّجْدَةِ نَفْسِهَا هَلْ يُجْزِيهِ ذَلِكَ؟ قَالَ: أَمَّا فِي الْقِيَاسِ فَالرَّكْعَةُ فِي ذَلِكَ وَالسَّجْدَةُ سَوَاءٌ لأَنَّ كُلَّ ذَلِكَ صَلاَةٌ وَأَمَّا فِي الاِسْتِحْسَانِ فَيَنْبَغِي لَهُ أَنْ يَسْجُدَ وَبِالْقِيَاسِ مَا ذَكَرَ مُحَمَّدٌ أَنَّ مَعْنَى التَّعْظِيمِ فِيهِمَا وَاحِدٌ فَكَانَا فِي حُصُولِ التَّعْظِيمِ بِهِمَا جِنْساً وَاحِداً وَالْحَاجَةُ إِلَى تَعْظِيمِ اللهِ إِمَّا اقْتِدَاءً بِمَنْ عَظَّمَ وَإِمَّا مُخَالَفَةً لِمَنِ اسْتَكْبَرَ فَكَانَ الظَّاهِرُ هُوَ الْجَوَازُ وَجْهُ الاِسْتِحْسَانِ أَنَّ الْوَاجِبَ هُوَ التَّعْظِيمُ بِجِهَةٍ مَخْصُوصَةٍ وَهِيَ السُّجُودُ بِدَلِيلِ أَنَّهُ لَوْ سَجَدَ مُسْتَقْبِلَ الْقِبْلَةِ وَحْدَهُ أَجْزَأَهُ دُونَ الرُّكُوعِ
And Muhammad ibn Salamah was asked: Does the back (spinal) prostration [of the prayer] take the place of the recitation prostration? He said: In qiyas it does, but in istihsan it does not; rather, bowing takes the place of both because the omission of prostration by prostration is an apparent matter, so that is qiyas. In istihsan it is not permissible because the prostration takes the place of itself, so it does not take the place of another, like a day of Ramadan fast does not make up for itself and another day. So it is established that qiyas—which is the apparent matter here—is given precedence over istihsan, unlike bowing taking its place, for qiyas prohibits permissibility because that is the apparent, while istihsan permits it, and it is the hidden, so at that time it is from giving precedence to istihsan, not qiyas. However, the generality of the mashayikh (senior scholars) hold that bowing is what takes the place of both. Thus Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) mentioned in the book, for he said: I said: If one intends to bow with the prostration itself, does that suffice him? He said: In qiyas, bowing and prostration are equal in that because all that is prayer. In istihsan, he should prostrate. And according to qiyas, what Muhammad mentioned that the meaning of glorification in both is one, so they are in attaining glorification through them of one type, and the need for glorifying Allah is either in imitation of one who glorified or in opposition to one who was arrogant, so the apparent is permissibility. The face of istihsan is that the obligatory is glorification in a specific manner, which is prostration, evidenced by the fact that if he prostrates facing the qiblah alone, it suffices him, unlike bowing.
Source pages p. 489

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether the prostration of recitation (sajdah al-tilawah) can be performed by bowing (ruku') instead of actual prostration (sujud) during prayer. The text presents the views of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani and the later consensus of the mashayikh. Muhammad initially distinguishes between qiyas (analogy) and istihsan (juristic preference): according to qiyas, since both ruku' and sujud are acts of prayer and involve glorification, one can substitute ruku' for the tilawah prostration; but according to istihsan, the obligatory act is specifically prostration, and one act cannot substitute for another distinct obligation, analogizing to a missed fast not making up for another. Later, Muhammad reports that in his own book (al-Jami' al-Saghir or similar), he states that in qiyas, ruku' and sujud are equivalent because both are prayer, but in istihsan, one should prostrate. However, the majority of later Hanafi scholars (the mashayikh) prefer the qiyas ruling, allowing ruku' to substitute for sajdah al-tilawah. The text also explains the reasoning: the underlying purpose is glorification, which is common to both acts, but istihsan emphasizes the specific form prescribed by the Lawgiver. The final relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that ruku' does suffice and is even considered the better of the two views, as mentioned by the commentator.

Key Terms
سجدة التلاوة (sajdah al-tilawah): The prostration required upon reciting or hearing certain verses of the Quran.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that departs from a clear analogy (qiyas jali) in favor of a hidden analogy (qiyas khafi) or other evidence for a more equitable result.
صلبية (sulbiyyah): The 'back' or 'spinal' prostration, referring to the obligatory prostration within the formal prayer (sajdah of salah), as opposed to tilawah prostration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of Hanafi mashayikh, can one perform sajdah al-tilawah by bowing (ruku') instead of prostrating?
A) Yes, it is valid because both are acts of prayer and share the meaning of glorification.
B) No, istihsan requires specific prostration.
C) Yes, but only if one cannot physically prostrate.
D) No, because qiyas is overridden by the clear text.

Key Takeaway
Ruku' suffices for sajdah al-tilawah according to the mufta bihi Hanafi view, based on the shared purpose of glorification.

Sajdat al-Tilawa: Qiyas vs Istihsan
Explains the rule that qiyas is preferred over istihsan in the case of substituting ruku' for sajdat al-tilawa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on substituting ruku' for sajdat al-tilawa and explain why qiyas is preferred over istihsan in this case.

Core Idea
Ruku' cannot replace sajdat al-tilawa; the later Hanafi view prefers qiyas over istihsan due to stronger evidence.

This lesson examines a specific ruling within the Hanafi school: when you hear or recite a verse of prostration during prayer, must you prostrate, or can you simply bow (ruku')? The passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi unravels a subtle debate between qiyas (apparent analogy) and istihsan (juristic preference) and shows how the later scholars resolved it by giving priority to the stronger evidence.

Guided Path
1
State the apparent conflict
Present the two views: qiyas says ruku' does not suffice, istihsan says it does.
2
Identify the early school position
Note that most early mashayikh and even Muhammad al-Shaybani initially allowed ruku' as per istihsan.
3
Follow the later tarjih
Explain why the later scholars preferred qiyas, citing the proof from Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn 'Umar and the tacit consensus (ijma suktuti).
4
Understand the usul principle
Recognize that preference between qiyas and istihsan depends on the strength of underlying meanings, and induction shows qiyas prevails in limited cases.
5
Apply the mufta bihi
Conclude that the operative ruling is to prostrate; ruku' does not fulfill the wajib.

فالقياس في هذا الرجم، وفي الإستحسان لا يرجم، وبالقياس أخذ ومنها لو تزوج امرأة على غير مهر مسمى وأعطاها رهناً بمهرها ثم طلقها قبل الدخول لها المتعة، ولو هلك الرهن عندها يذهب بالمتعة في قول محمد استحساناً، والقياس أن لا يذهب بها، وهو قول أبي يوسف وللمرأة مطالبة الزوج بالمتعة، ومنها لو وكل الحربي المستأمن مثله بخصومة في دار الإسلام، ثم الحق الموكل بدار الحرب، ويقي الوكيل في دار الإسلام بطلت الوكالة في القياس، وفي الإستحسان، لا وبالقياس نأخذ
The prostration of recitation is not the bowing. So the qiyas according to his statement is that the obligatory prostration stands in its place, and in istihsan it does not stand but rather the bowing. Because the falling of the prostration by prostration is an apparent matter, so it is the qiyas. And in istihsan it is not allowed because the prostration stands in place of itself, so it does not stand in place of something else, like the fast of a day of Ramadan does not stand in place of itself for another day. So it is correct that the qiyas, which is the apparent matter here, is preferred over istihsan, contrary to the standing of bowing in its place: qiyas rejects permissibility because it is the apparent, and in istihsan it is allowed, and it is the hidden, so then it is a case of preferring istihsan, not qiyas. But most mashayikh hold that the bowing is what stands in place of both. Thus Muhammad (rahimahullah) mentioned it in the book, for he said: I said: If he intends to bow for the prostration itself, does that suffice him? He said: As for qiyas, the rak'ah in that and the prostration are equal because all of that is prayer. As for istihsan, he should prostrate. And by qiyas, what Muhammad mentioned that the meaning of glorification in both is one, so they are in attaining glorification by them one genus, and the need to glorify Allah is either by following one who glorified [the prophets] or by opposing one who was arrogant [the disbelievers]. So the apparent is permissibility. The face of istihsan is that the obligatory is glorification by a specific mode, which is prostration, evidenced by... Because of the fact that qiyas is the apparent and istihsan is what opposes it, he thought that it was clearer. His statement: (Regarding istihsan) means that istihsan is the hidden qiyas that opposes the apparent, so qiyas only opposes the apparent if istihsan is intended. As for qiyas in the sense that is predominant among usuliyyun, it is the manifest. His statement: (He thought that Muhammad ibn Salamah...) means that he ruled that qiyas is preferred over istihsan, and the apparent qiyas here is the validity of the obligatory prostration standing in place of the recitation prostration, and istihsan is invalidity because the obligatory stands in place of itself and not another. And he made performing it by bowing istihsan, and qiyas rejects it because he made qiyas the apparent and its opposite is istihsan. If he had considered what he said in 'we said', he would make performing it by bowing qiyas, not istihsan. His statement: (so the qiyas) i.e. the apparent, and 'that it stands' is the predicate of 'was'. His statement: (And in istihsan) the first [letter] is omitted in his statement: (but the bowing) i.e., and qiyas is preferred so it does not stand with him, and that is indicated by his later statement 'but the generality'. His statement: (because the falling) is the cause for his statement 'so the qiyas upon his statement'. His statement: (And in istihsan it is not allowed) is repeated to give the reason. His statement: (here) i.e. in performing the recitation prostration by the obligatory one. His statement: (then the qiyas [؟] permissibility) because it is performing the obligatory without its form. His statement: (so it became) i.e. performing it by bowing. His statement: (then) i.e. when istihsan permits it and qiyas prevents it, and they mentioned that qiyas here is preferred over istihsan, and that requires the invalidity of performing it by bowing, and that is due to his thought that qiyas is the apparent and istihsan is its opposite. If he looked at what follows, he would make it qiyas, thus preferred over istihsan. His statement: (because all that is prayer) i.e. from its acts. His statement: (he should prostrate because in it is performing the obligatory with its form and meaning. His statement: (either following here one who glorified) they are the prophets. His statement: (or opposing one who was arrogant) they are the disbelievers. Then they took qiyas due to the strength of its evidence, that is because they narrated from Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn 'Umar that they allowed bowing for prostration in prayer, and no disagreement is reported from others, so they preferred qiyas. Because preference is not for the hidden due to its concealment, nor for the apparent due to its obviousness, but rather in preference they return to the meanings (i.e., causes) associated with them. So when the hidden is strong, they take it; or when the apparent is strong, they take it. However, their induction necessitated the scarcity of the apparent that is predominant relative to the hidden that opposes it, so they limited the instances where qiyas is preferred over istihsan to about ten or more places, known in usul, and this is one of them, and there is no limit to its opposite. (And if he hears) a verse of prostration. His statement: (until the recitation became long on three verses, and you know the disagreement on length. His statement: (and that) i.e., the strong evidence. His statement: (and no disagreement is reported from others) so it is consensus. His statement: (so they preferred qiyas) i.e., due to the strength of its evidence, and this is the essence of the answer, so the gist is that it was preferred due to its strong evidence. His statement: (for the hidden) i.e., which is istihsan. His statement: (of the meanings) i.e., the causes. His statement: (however their induction) i.e., their examination of the particulars in which the hidden and the apparent met. His statement: (so) i.e., their induction necessitated the scarcity of the strength of the apparent. His statement: (in about ten more places known in usul, among them this, which is performing the recitation prostration by bowing when it is prayer-related, and among them if he says: If you give birth to a boy, you are divorced, and she says she gave birth, and the husband denies her, in qiyas she is not believed and divorce does not occur, and they took qiyas in it. And among them: two men have a house in their hands, each establishes evidence that so-and-so pledged it with him and handed it over to him, in qiyas it is not a pledge for either of them, and we take qiyas, and in istihsan each has half of it as a pledge for half the debt. And among them: if the buyer says: I entered into salam with you for a Herawi cloth of length six cubits by three cubits, and the seller says: length five cubits by three, they take an oath as qiyas, and we take that, and in istihsan the statement is of the seller. And among them: if four bear witness against a man for zina and two bear witness for his ihsan, and the judge orders his stoning, then the imam finds the two witnesses of ihsan are slaves or they retract, and the stoned one did not die yet but sustained wounds, in qiyas he is to be given the hadd of zina of one hundred lashes, which is their statement (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) because what happened after stoning was not by way of ruling due to their being slaves, so it is like non-existence, and in istihsan the hadd is waived from him. And among them: if they bear witness against a man for zina, and the judge rules his flogging of one hundred, then two witnesses testify that he is muhsan, and the flogging is not completed, in qiyas he is stoned, and in istihsan he is not stoned, and qiyas is taken. And among them: if a man marries a woman without a specified mahr and gives her a pledge for her mahr, then divorces her before consummation, she is entitled to mut'ah. If the pledge perishes with her, it is deducted from the mut'ah according to Muhammad's istihsan, and in qiyas it is not deducted, which is the statement of Abu Yusuf, and the woman can claim the mut'ah from the husband. And among them: if a harbi or musta'min appoints someone like him as agent for litigation in Dar al-Islam, then the principal goes to Dar al-Harb, and the agent remains in Dar al-Islam, the agency is void in qiyas, and in istihsan it is not, and we take qiyas.
Source pages p. 490

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi is a critical refinement of the text of Maraqi al-Falah regarding the ruling on substituting ruku' (bowing) for sajdat al-tilawa (prostration of recitation) during prayer. The author, Allamah al-Tahtawi, explains the debate between qiyas (apparent analogy) and istihsan (juristic preference) in this matter. The text first presents the apparent qiyas: sajdat al-tilawa cannot be performed by ruku'; one must actually prostrate. This is because the obligation is to perform a prostration, and a prostration only fulfills its own obligation, not a different act. The author compares it to a missed fast of Ramadan which cannot be compensated by another fast of the same day. However, istihsan (hidden analogy) holds that ruku' can substitute because both involve glorification of Allah. The text notes that most Hanafi mashayikh (scholars) actually hold that ruku' does stand in place of sajdat al-tilawa, seemingly following the istihsan. But then the discussion shifts to the general principle: after examining the evidence, the later scholars (the muta'akhkhirin) adopted qiyas in this specific case because its evidence was stronger. The strong evidence is the practice of the Companions Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn 'Umar, who allowed ruku' for sajdat al-tilawa during prayer, and no other Companion disagreed, thus forming a consensus (ijma). The text explains that preference between qiyas and istihsan is not merely based on which is apparent or hidden, but on the strength of the underlying meanings (ma'ani). An inductive survey of the cases by Hanafi usul scholars showed that instances where qiyas is preferred over istihsan are limited to about a dozen cases, and this is one of them. The passage then lists other examples from Hanafi fiqh where qiyas is taken over istihsan, such as: a husband denying his wife's claim of childbirth, a dispute over a pledged house, a disagreement in a salam contract, cases of zina witnesses, and agency of a harbi. The consistent methodology is that when the evidence for qiyas is stronger, it is preferred. The final ruling (mufta bihi) is that one must prostrate for sajdat al-tilawa; ruku' does not suffice.

Key Terms
سجدة التلاوة (sajdat al-tilawa): The prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a verse of prostration in the Quran.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning in Islamic law. Here it refers to the apparent analogy (qiyas jaliy) that a specific act cannot be replaced by another act of the same genus if the mode is different.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference, a method of departing from an apparent analogy in favor of a hidden analogy or stronger evidence. Here it is the view that ruku' can substitute for sajdat al-tilawa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi view in this passage, what should one do upon hearing a verse of prostration during prayer?
A) Perform ruku' instead of prostration.
B) Perform prostration (sajdah) after finishing the recitation.
C) Perform ruku' and then prostration.
D) Prostrate immediately if the recitation is long.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's relied-upon view is that sajdat al-tilawa must be performed by prostration; ruku' does not substitute, based on the strength of the supporting evidence from the Companions.

Other Cases Where Qiyas is Preferred Over Istihsan
Lists several fiqh cases where the Hanafi school takes qiyas over istihsan, illustrating the principle of tarjih based on evidence strength.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify other fiqh cases where the Hanafi school prefers qiyas over istihsan and state the ruling for each.

Core Idea
Qiyas is preferred over istihsan in about a dozen specific cases, including disputes over divorce, pledges, and witnesses.

The passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi not only discusses the sajdat al-tilawa ruling but also provides a list of other cases where the Hanafi school gave precedence to qiyas over istihsan. This lesson explores those cases, each illustrating the methodological principle that preference depends on the strength of underlying meanings, not merely on appearance. By studying these furu', you will grasp how the usul principle is applied consistently across different areas of fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle
Recall that the later Hanafi scholars limited the cases where qiyas is preferred over istihsan to about a dozen, based on induction. This lesson lists several of those cases.
2
Examine the first case: divorce and birth
If a husband says 'If you give birth to a boy, you are divorced' and she claims she gave birth, in qiyas she is not believed; in istihsan she is believed. The Hanafi school takes qiyas.
This involves the principle of istishab and the burden of proof.
3
Examine the second case: pledge of a house
Two men claim a house was pledged to them separately; in qiyas it is not a pledge for either; in istihsan each gets half. The school takes qiyas.
4
Examine further cases
Work through the remaining examples: salam contract disputes, witnesses for zina, agency of a harbi, and others. For each, note the qiyas ruling and the istihsan alternative.
These cases cover mu'amalat, hudud, and family law.
5
Understand the rationale
Recognize that in each case, the qiyas ruling was preferred because its evidence was stronger. The list illustrates the Hanafi methodological commitment to preferring the stronger proof.

The prostration of recitation is not the bowing. So the qiyas according to his statement is that the obligatory prostration stands in its place, and in istihsan it does not stand but rather the bowing. Because the falling of the prostration by prostration is an apparent matter, so it is the qiyas. And in istihsan it is not allowed because the prostration stands in place of itself, so it does not stand in place of something else, like the fast of a day of Ramadan does not stand in place of itself for another day. So it is correct that the qiyas, which is the apparent matter here, is preferred over istihsan, contrary to the standing of bowing in its place: qiyas rejects permissibility because it is the apparent, and in istihsan it is allowed, and it is the hidden, so then it is a case of preferring istihsan, not qiyas. But most mashayikh hold that the bowing is what stands in place of both. Thus Muhammad (rahimahullah) mentioned it in the book, for he said: I said: If he intends to bow for the prostration itself, does that suffice him? He said: As for qiyas, the rak'ah in that and the prostration are equal because all of that is prayer. As for istihsan, he should prostrate. And by qiyas, what Muhammad mentioned that the meaning of glorification in both is one, so they are in attaining glorification by them one genus, and the need to glorify Allah is either by following one who glorified [the prophets] or by opposing one who was arrogant [the disbelievers]. So the apparent is permissibility. The face of istihsan is that the obligatory is glorification by a specific mode, which is prostration, evidenced by... Because of the fact that qiyas is the apparent and istihsan is what opposes it, he thought that it was clearer. His statement: (Regarding istihsan) means that istihsan is the hidden qiyas that opposes the apparent, so qiyas only opposes the apparent if istihsan is intended. As for qiyas in the sense that is predominant among usuliyyun, it is the manifest. His statement: (He thought that Muhammad ibn Salamah...) means that he ruled that qiyas is preferred over istihsan, and the apparent qiyas here is the validity of the obligatory prostration standing in place of the recitation prostration, and istihsan is invalidity because the obligatory stands in place of itself and not another. And he made performing it by bowing istihsan, and qiyas rejects it because he made qiyas the apparent and its opposite is istihsan. If he had considered what he said in 'we said', he would make performing it by bowing qiyas, not istihsan. His statement: (so the qiyas) i.e. the apparent, and 'that it stands' is the predicate of 'was'. His statement: (And in istihsan) the first [letter] is omitted in his statement: (but the bowing) i.e., and qiyas is preferred so it does not stand with him, and that is indicated by his later statement 'but the generality'. His statement: (because the falling) is the cause for his statement 'so the qiyas upon his statement'. His statement: (And in istihsan it is not allowed) is repeated to give the reason. His statement: (here) i.e. in performing the recitation prostration by the obligatory one. His statement: (then the qiyas [؟] permissibility) because it is performing the obligatory without its form. His statement: (so it became) i.e. performing it by bowing. His statement: (then) i.e. when istihsan permits it and qiyas prevents it, and they mentioned that qiyas here is preferred over istihsan, and that requires the invalidity of performing it by bowing, and that is due to his thought that qiyas is the apparent and istihsan is its opposite. If he looked at what follows, he would make it qiyas, thus preferred over istihsan. His statement: (because all that is prayer) i.e. from its acts. His statement: (he should prostrate because in it is performing the obligatory with its form and meaning. His statement: (either following here one who glorified) they are the prophets. His statement: (or opposing one who was arrogant) they are the disbelievers. Then they took qiyas due to the strength of its evidence, that is because they narrated from Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn 'Umar that they allowed bowing for prostration in prayer, and no disagreement is reported from others, so they preferred qiyas. Because preference is not for the hidden due to its concealment, nor for the apparent due to its obviousness, but rather in preference they return to the meanings (i.e., causes) associated with them. So when the hidden is strong, they take it; or when the apparent is strong, they take it. However, their induction necessitated the scarcity of the apparent that is predominant relative to the hidden that opposes it, so they limited the instances where qiyas is preferred over istihsan to about ten or more places, known in usul, and this is one of them, and there is no limit to its opposite. (And if he hears) a verse of prostration. His statement: (until the recitation became long on three verses, and you know the disagreement on length. His statement: (and that) i.e., the strong evidence. His statement: (and no disagreement is reported from others) so it is consensus. His statement: (so they preferred qiyas) i.e., due to the strength of its evidence, and this is the essence of the answer, so the gist is that it was preferred due to its strong evidence. His statement: (for the hidden) i.e., which is istihsan. His statement: (of the meanings) i.e., the causes. His statement: (however their induction) i.e., their examination of the particulars in which the hidden and the apparent met. His statement: (so) i.e., their induction necessitated the scarcity of the strength of the apparent. His statement: (in about ten more places known in usul, among them this, which is performing the recitation prostration by bowing when it is prayer-related, and among them if he says: If you give birth to a boy, you are divorced, and she says she gave birth, and the husband denies her, in qiyas she is not believed and divorce does not occur, and they took qiyas in it. And among them: two men have a house in their hands, each establishes evidence that so-and-so pledged it with him and handed it over to him, in qiyas it is not a pledge for either of them, and we take qiyas, and in istihsan each has half of it as a pledge for half the debt. And among them: if the buyer says: I entered into salam with you for a Herawi cloth of length six cubits by three cubits, and the seller says: length five cubits by three, they take an oath as qiyas, and we take that, and in istihsan the statement is of the seller. And among them: if four bear witness against a man for zina and two bear witness for his ihsan, and the judge orders his stoning, then the imam finds the two witnesses of ihsan are slaves or they retract, and the stoned one did not die yet but sustained wounds, in qiyas he is to be given the hadd of zina of one hundred lashes, which is their statement (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) because what happened after stoning was not by way of ruling due to their being slaves, so it is like non-existence, and in istihsan the hadd is waived from him. And among them: if they bear witness against a man for zina, and the judge rules his flogging of one hundred, then two witnesses testify that he is muhsan, and the flogging is not completed, in qiyas he is stoned, and in istihsan he is not stoned, and qiyas is taken. And among them: if a man marries a woman without a specified mahr and gives her a pledge for her mahr, then divorces her before consummation, she is entitled to mut'ah. If the pledge perishes with her, it is deducted from the mut'ah according to Muhammad's istihsan, and in qiyas it is not deducted, which is the statement of Abu Yusuf, and the woman can claim the mut'ah from the husband. And among them: if a harbi or musta'min appoints someone like him as agent for litigation in Dar al-Islam, then the principal goes to Dar al-Harb, and the agent remains in Dar al-Islam, the agency is void in qiyas, and in istihsan it is not, and we take qiyas.
Source pages p. 490

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi is a critical refinement of the text of Maraqi al-Falah regarding the ruling on substituting ruku' (bowing) for sajdat al-tilawa (prostration of recitation) during prayer. The author, Allamah al-Tahtawi, explains the debate between qiyas (apparent analogy) and istihsan (juristic preference) in this matter. The text first presents the apparent qiyas: sajdat al-tilawa cannot be performed by ruku'; one must actually prostrate. This is because the obligation is to perform a prostration, and a prostration only fulfills its own obligation, not a different act. The author compares it to a missed fast of Ramadan which cannot be compensated by another fast of the same day. However, istihsan (hidden analogy) holds that ruku' can substitute because both involve glorification of Allah. The text notes that most Hanafi mashayikh (scholars) actually hold that ruku' does stand in place of sajdat al-tilawa, seemingly following the istihsan. But then the discussion shifts to the general principle: after examining the evidence, the later scholars (the muta'akhkhirin) adopted qiyas in this specific case because its evidence was stronger. The strong evidence is the practice of the Companions Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn 'Umar, who allowed ruku' for sajdat al-tilawa during prayer, and no other Companion disagreed, thus forming a consensus (ijma). The text explains that preference between qiyas and istihsan is not merely based on which is apparent or hidden, but on the strength of the underlying meanings (ma'ani). An inductive survey of the cases by Hanafi usul scholars showed that instances where qiyas is preferred over istihsan are limited to about a dozen cases, and this is one of them. The passage then lists other examples from Hanafi fiqh where qiyas is taken over istihsan, such as: a husband denying his wife's claim of childbirth, a dispute over a pledged house, a disagreement in a salam contract, cases of zina witnesses, and agency of a harbi. The consistent methodology is that when the evidence for qiyas is stronger, it is preferred. The final ruling (mufta bihi) is that one must prostrate for sajdat al-tilawa; ruku' does not suffice.

Key Terms
سجدة التلاوة (sajdat al-tilawa): Not applicable in this lesson; the key terms are the same as the first lesson.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning, here the preferred method in the listed cases.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference, rejected in these cases in favor of qiyas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of two men claiming a house was pledged to them, what is the Hanafi ruling (mufta bihi)?
A) The house is divided equally between them.
B) The house is not a pledge for either of them.
C) The house goes to the one who first presented evidence.
D) The house is given to the original owner.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prefers qiyas over istihsan in a limited set of cases, each decided based on the strength of the evidence, not on whether the qiyas is apparent or hidden.

Preferring Qiyas over Istihsan: The Ruling on Delayed Ruku' for Sajdah
Commentary on a fiqh ruling with a usul digression on qiyas vs istihsan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school ruled that delaying ruku' for sajdah invalidates the intention, and apply the principle of preferring qiyas over istihsan when evidence is stronger.

Core Idea
Qiyas prevails over istihsan when its evidence is stronger, even if the apparent meaning favors istihsan.

This lesson addresses a specific fiqh ruling about bowing (ruku') intended to fulfill the obligation of prostration of recitation (sajdah) when the recitation becomes long. The Hanafi position is that such bowing does not suffice. The commentary then expands on a key usul point: why qiyas (analogy) was preferred over istihsan (juristic preference) in this case, and generally in the Hanafi school. Understanding this methodological preference is essential for grasping the school's legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its conditions
State the ruling: if a person delays ruku' until recitation becomes long (over three verses) and then intends that ruku' for sajdah, it is invalid. Identify the condition of immediacy.
The condition is tied to the length of recitation; the commentary clarifies 'long' as three or more verses.
2
Trace the evidence (dalil) for the ruling
The commentator cites narrations from Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn 'Umar that they allowed bowing for sajdah during prayer, and no opposition was recorded. This silence forms a consensus (ijma sukuti), which strengthens the qiyas argument.
The evidence is zanni in transmission but strong in indication.
3
Understand the preference for qiyas over istihsan
The passage explains that preference is not based on whether the reasoning is hidden (khafi) or apparent (jali), but on the strength of accompanying meanings (ilal). Here, the evidence for qiyas is stronger, so it is preferred.
Istihsan would allow the bowing based on ease, but the school followed qiyas.
4
Survey the examples of qiyas preferred over istihsan
The commentary lists about a dozen cases where qiyas is chosen, such as divorce on unknown child, pawn disputes, salam contracts, hudud, agency, and torts. These illustrate the principle.
The list is not exhaustive; the opposite scenario (istihsan preferred) is more numerous.
5
Apply the principle to a new scenario
Given a hypothetical where qiyas and istihsan conflict, determine which evidence is stronger by examining the proof (e.g., text, ijma, necessity). The stronger proof determines the ruling.
This is the skill the student should develop: evaluating legal evidence.

If he does not bow immediately until the recitation becomes long, then intends with the bowing that it be for the prostration, it is not permissible. Then they took by qiyas due to the strength of its evidence, because they narrated from Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn 'Umar that they allowed bowing for prostration while in prayer, and no opposition from others was narrated, so qiyas was given precedence. For there is no preference for the hidden due to its hiddenness, nor for the apparent due to its apparentness; rather, preference is based on the meanings (causes) that accompany them. Whenever the hidden is strong, they take by it, or the apparent is strong, they take by it. However, their deduction (istiqra') indicated the scarcity of the apparent (immediate meaning) relative to the opposing hidden, so they limited the positions of preferring qiyas over istihsan to about a dozen places known in usul; this is one of them, and the opposite is not limited, end. His statement: '(Even if he hears)' a verse. His statement: 'until the recitation becomes long beyond three verses' and you have known the difference regarding length. His statement: 'prostration'. His statement: 'That is' meaning the strong evidence. His statement: 'No opposition from others was narrated' so it was consensus. His statement: 'So qiyas was given precedence' meaning due to the strength of its evidence, and this is the essence of the answer; its summary is that it was given precedence due to its strong evidence. His statement: 'for the hidden' meaning istihsan. His statement: 'from the meanings' meaning the causes. His statement: 'However, their deduction' meaning their examination of the particulars in which the hidden and apparent come together. His statement: 'So' meaning their deduction necessitated the weakness of the apparent's strength. And among them: a man has a son from another's slave woman by marriage; the father buys this slave woman for his insane son; in qiyas the purchase is for the father, not for the insane son; in istihsan it is for the son, and qiyas is taken. And among them: if a man falls into a well dug in a road and grabs another, and that other grabs another, and they all fall and die, found in the well on top of each other; the well-digger pays blood-money for the first, the first pays for the second, the second pays for the third, and that is on their 'aqila; this is qiyas and we take by it; there is another view which is istihsan. The intent is not to limit them to what was mentioned; Fakhr al-Islam said, 'This is a rare category.' I have counted up to twenty-two issues. As for the category in which istihsan is preferred over qiyas, it is too numerous to count. From Sharh al-Manar by 'Allamah Zayn, summarized. His statement: 'and the opposite is not limited' preferring istihsan over qiyas, and istihsan is evidence according to us; whoever denies it does not know what it is, as in al-Tahrir.
Source pages p. 491

Commentary
This passage from the Hashiya explores a specific ruling and then delves into a methodological discussion about the relationship between qiyas (analogy) and istihsan (juristic preference) in the Hanafi school. The initial ruling: If a person delays the ruku' so that the recitation becomes long (more than three verses), and then intends that ruku' to fulfill the obligation of sajdah (prostration of recitation), it is not valid. The base text (Marqiy al-Falah) states this, and the commentator (al-Tahtawi) explains the proof: narrations from Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn 'Umar indicate that bowing can serve for sajdah within prayer, and no companion opposed, making it a consensus (ijma'). Thus qiyas is given precedence over istihsan in this case. The commentary then expands on the principle that preference between qiyas khafi (hidden analogy) and qiyas jali (apparent analogy) or istihsan is not based on inherent hiddenness or apparentness, but on the accompanying meanings (ilal). The Hanafi scholars surveyed particulars and found only about a dozen cases where qiyas is preferred over istihsan; a list of examples is given, including marriage, pawning, salam contracts, hudud, agency, and torts. The passage emphasizes that qiyas is the foundational method, and istihsan is only preferred in numerous other cases. The commentary concludes that istihsan is valid evidence according to the Hanafis, and its deniers are ignorant. This passage is a critical refinement of the matn, clarifying the legal reasoning.

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning; extending a ruling from an original case to a new case due to shared effective cause ('illa).
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Juristic preference; departing from an analogical ruling for a stronger reason (e.g., necessity, custom, ease).
الإجماع السكوتي (ijma sukuti): Tacit consensus: when silence of scholars on a ruling indicates agreement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did the Hanafi scholars give precedence to qiyas over istihsan in the ruling about bowing for sajdah?
A) Because qiyas is always stronger than istihsan.
B) Because the evidence for qiyas (narrations from Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn 'Umar with no opposition) was stronger.
C) Because the apparent meaning (zahir) was weak.
D) Because the hidden analogy (qiyas khafi) was preferred.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prefers qiyas over istihsan when the evidence for qiyas is stronger, as in the case of bowing for sajdah after long recitation, supported by Companion consensus.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
6 min
Ruling on Follower Hearing Imam Recite Sajdah Verse
Critical refinement of sajdah tilawah for followers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a follower who catches the imam after the sajdah verse and explain the reasoning based on maziyyat al-salah.

Core Idea
A follower who catches the rak'ah after the imam's sajdah is legally deemed to have performed it.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi clarifies a key nuance in sajdah tilawah for followers. The commentator refines the ruling by citing al-Atabi, explaining that if a follower joins the imam's rak'ah after the sajdah verse, the sajdah is considered performed by virtue of being in the prayer, due to the special merit of prayer (maziyyat al-salah). Intentionally leaving this wajib is sinful.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognize the situation: a follower hears the imam recite a sajdah verse after the imam has already performed the sajdah, but the follower joins before the rak'ah ends.
The follower's hearing is based on the imam's recitation, which occurred in prayer.
2
State the ruling
The follower does not need to prostrate at all—neither in nor out of prayer. He is legally considered to have performed the sajdah by catching the rak'ah.
This is the mufta bihi position.
3
Understand the reasoning
The sajdah acquires the 'merit of prayer' (maziyyat al-salah). Since it was performed in prayer, it cannot be completed outside prayer because that would be less perfect.
Al-Atabi's clarification is cited as authority.
4
Apply the analogy
The ruling is analogous to catching the imam in the ruku' of the third rak'ah of witr, which gives the follower the qunut.
Both cases involve catching a part that includes the obligation.
5
Note the consequence
Intentionally leaving the sajdah tilawah is sinful, just as intentionally leaving Friday prayer is sinful.
This underscores the wajib nature of sajdah tilawah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( وهو التلاوة الملزمة) خرج غير الملزمة كتلاوة النائم على أحد قولين صوناً لها عن الضياع لو تركها قوله وللصلاة عن (الزائد لو سجدها فيها، وهو راجع لقوله سجد خارج الصلاة على سبيل النشر المرتب. قوله : (وأشار في بعض النسخ الخ) ظاهره أن الضمير للمصنف، وفيه أنّ الإشارة تؤخذ من قوله في المتن في الأظهر، والذي في كبيره، وقال العتابي : أشار في بعض النسخ إلى أنها تسقط عنه بالإقتداء في غير ركعتها لأن السماع بناء على التلاوة، وقد وجدت في الصلاة فكانت السجدة صلوية، فلم تؤد خارجها اهـ ولعل ضمير أشار في كلام العتابي إلى ما شرح عليه قوله : (فيصير مؤدياً لها حكماً) فمن أدرك الإمام في ركوع ثالثة الوتر فإنه يكون مدركاً للقنوت. قوله : (فلا يسجدها أصلاً) أي مطلقاً لا في الصلاة، ولا خارجها، وقد علل المؤلف للوجهين قوله : لأنّ لها مزية أي مزية الصلاة، فلا تتأدى بالسجود خارجها لأنه أنقص من السجود فيها . قوله الائمه بتعمد تركها لأنها واجبة، والواجب يأثم المكلف بتركه قوله : (كالجمعة) أي كترك الجمعة فإنه يأثم به إن كان تركها
His statement: '(And it is the obligatory recitation)' excludes non-obligatory recitation, like the recitation of a sleeping person according to one view, to preserve it from being wasted if he leaves it. His statement: 'and for the prayer against the extra' if he performs sajdah in it, and it refers to his statement 'he prostrates outside the prayer' in a correlated manner. His statement: '(And he indicated in some copies)' apparently the pronoun refers to the author; it includes that the indication is taken from his statement in the text 'in the most apparent view', and what is in his big commentary. Al-Atabi said: 'He indicated in some copies that it drops from him by following in a rak'ah other than its rak'ah, because hearing is based on recitation, and it was found in prayer, so the sajdah becomes prayer-related, thus it is not performed outside it.' Perhaps the pronoun of 'indicated' in Atabi's speech refers to what he explained. His statement: '(Thus he becomes performing it legally)' so whoever catches the imam in the ruku' of the third witr, he catches the qunut. His statement: '(So he does not prostrate it at all)' meaning absolutely not in prayer nor outside it. The author explained the two aspects: His statement: 'Because it has a merit' meaning the merit of prayer, so it is not fulfilled by prostration outside it because that is less than prostration inside. His statement: 'The imam' with intentional leaving because it is obligatory, and the obligated person sins by leaving an obligatory. His statement: '(Like Friday)' meaning like leaving Friday prayer; he sins by leaving it.
Source pages p. 492

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on the rulings for sajdah tilawah (prostration of recitation). The commentator clarifies the matn's statement about 'obligatory recitation' (al-tilawah al-mulzima): it refers to recitation that obligates sajdah, excluding non-obligatory recitation like that of a sleeping person (according to one view). The purpose is to preserve the sajdah from being wasted if one leaves it. Then the commentary addresses the scenario of a follower hearing the imam recite a sajdah verse: if the follower joins the prayer after the imam has performed the sajdah, but in the same rak'ah, he is legally deemed to have performed the sajdah (i.e., it is fulfilled for him) and need not prostrate at all—neither in prayer (to avoid conflicting with the imam) nor outside. The reasoning is that the sajdah has the 'merit of prayer' (maziyyat al-salah) and thus cannot be performed outside the prayer because that is less complete. The commentator also analogizes to catching the imam in the ruku' of the third witr, which gives one the qunut. Finally, intentionally leaving this sajdah (which is wajib) is sinful, analogous to intentionally leaving Friday prayer. The passage is a critical refinement explaining the nuances of when the sajdah is considered performed or dropped.

Key Terms
التلاوة الملزمة (al-tilawah al-mulzima): Obligatory recitation that necessitates sajdah, i.e., recitation of a verse of sajdah.
مزية الصلاة (maziyyat al-salah): The special merit or virtue that prayer has, making acts within prayer more complete than outside.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the reasoning for the sajdah not being performed outside prayer after being caught in prayer?
A) Because the sajdah is optional outside prayer.
B) Because the sajdah has the merit of prayer and performing it outside is less complete.
C) Because the follower did not actually hear the verse.
D) Because the imam is responsible for the follower.

Key Takeaway
A follower who catches the rak'ah of the imam's sajdah tilawah is legally deemed to have performed it and need not prostrate, due to the merit of prayer.

When to Prostrate: Sajdah al-Tilawah for a Listener of the Imam
States sajdah rulings for one hearing imam's recitation outside or inside prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three scenarios for a listener's obligation of sajdah al-tilawah and apply the rule that catching the imam's rak'ah after his sajdah fulfills the obligation within the prayer.

Core Idea
Catching the imam's rak'ah after he prostrates for sajdah al-tilawah fulfills the obligation within the prayer.

In this lesson, we examine the detailed rulings from the Hanafi school regarding sajdah al-tilawah for a person who hears the imam recite a sajdah verse. The classical commentators carefully distinguish when the listener must prostrate externally and when the prayer itself suffices, based on whether the listener is in the same rak'ah as the verse and when he joins the imam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the listener's status
Determine whether the listener is praying behind the imam or not, and if praying, in which rak'ah he is relative to the sajdah verse.
The listener may be: (1) not following at all (e.g., in another prayer or not praying), (2) following in a different rak'ah, or (3) following in the same rak'ah.
2
Check if the listener catches the imam before or after his sajdah
If the listener is in the same rak'ah, determine whether he joins the imam before or after the imam has performed the sajdah al-tilawah.
This affects whether he prostrates with the imam or it is waived.
3
Apply the ruling for each scenario
Scenario 1: Never follows → prostrate outside prayer. Scenario 2: Follows in another rak'ah → prostrate outside prayer. Scenario 3: Follows in same rak'ah after imam's sajdah → no separate prostration (fulfilled by prayer). Scenario 3 variant: Follows before imam's sajdah → must prostrate with him.
The cause (hearing valid recitation) is present; the only preventer is being in the relevant rak'ah.
4
Identify the proof for the third scenario
The text states 'by agreement of the narrations' (باتفاق الروايات), indicating consensus among the Hanafi imams that catching the rak'ah counts as performing the sajdah.
This is a proof from ijma' (consensus) of the early Hanafi authorities.
5
Note the consequence of deliberate omission
Intentionally leaving a wajib sajdah al-tilawah is sinful and requires repentance, similar to leaving Friday prayer.
This underscores the wajib status of sajdah al-tilawah in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السجدة (من إمام فلم يأتم به أصلاً (أو أنتم) به ( في ركعة أخرى) غير التي تلي الآية فيها وسجد لها الإمام (سجد) السامع سجوداً (خارج الصلاة) لتحقق السبب وهو التلاوة الملزمة، أو السماع من تلاوة صحيحة على اختلاف المشايخ في السبب وقوله (في الأظهر) متعلق بالمسئلة الأخيرة صوناً لها عن الضياع، وللصلاة عن الزائد، وأشار في بعض النسخ إلى أنها تسقط عنه بالاقتداء في غير ركعتها بناء على أنها صلوية (وإن انتم السامع قبل سجود إمامه لها سجد معه لوجود السبب وعدم المانع (فإن اقتدى) السامع (به) أي بالإمام (بعد سجودها) وكان اقتداؤه في ركعتها صار السامع (مدركاً لها) أي للسجدة (حكماً) بإدراكه ركعتها فيصير مؤدياً لها حكماً فلا يسجدها أصلاً) باتفاق الروايات لأنه لا يمكنه أن في الصلاة لما فيه من مخالفة الإمام، ولا بعد فراغه منها لأنها صلوية (ولم نقض الصلاتية (خارجها لأنّ لها مزية فلا تتأدى بناقص، وعليه التوبة لإثمه بيتعمد تركها كالجمعة
The prostration (from an imam and he does not follow him at all, or he follows him in another rak'ah other than the one in which the verse was recited and the imam prostrated for it, the listener prostrates a prostration (outside the prayer) because the cause is realized, which is the recitation that obligates, or hearing from a valid recitation, according to the difference of the mashayikh on the cause. And his statement (in the most apparent) pertains to the last issue, to protect it from being lost, and to protect the prayer from the extra. And he indicated in some copies that it is dropped from him by following in a rak'ah other than its rak'ah, based on it being a prayer-prostration. And if the listener followed him before his imam's prostration for it, he prostrates with him due to existence of the cause and absence of the preventer. And if the listener followed him after his prostration for it, and his following was in its rak'ah, the listener becomes a perceiver of it (i.e., the prostration) in terms of ruling by perceiving its rak'ah, so he becomes performing it in terms of ruling, so he does not prostrate it at all, by agreement of the narrations, because he cannot prostrate it in the prayer due to opposing the imam, nor after finishing it because it is a prayer-prostration. And we do not fulfill the prayer-prostration outside it because it has a merit, so it is not fulfilled by a deficient one, and upon him is repentance for his sin if he intentionally leaves it, like Friday.
Source pages p. 492

Commentary
This passage is a commentary expanding on the matn of Al-Hidayah regarding sajdah al-tilawah. The commentator clarifies the ruling for a person who hears an imam recite a sajdah verse. Three scenarios are covered: (1) If the listener never follows the imam (e.g., is in another prayer or not praying), he prostrates externally after the imam's sajdah. (2) If the listener follows the imam in a different rak'ah (not the one with the verse), he also prostrates externally because the cause (hearing a valid recitation) is present but he is not in that rak'ah. (3) If the listener follows the imam in the same rak'ah after the imam's sajdah, the listener is considered to have caught the rak'ah and thus the sajdah is fulfilled by the prayer itself; he does not prostrate separately. The commentator notes that if the listener follows before the imam prostrates, he must prostrate with him. The phrase 'by agreement of the narrations' indicates ijma' (consensus). The final point: intentionally leaving a wajib sajdah is sinful and requires repentance, analogous to leaving Friday prayer. The authority weight is Zahir al-Riwayah as the ruling is from the core books.

Key Terms
السجدة (al-sajdah): The prostration of recitation (sajdah al-tilawah) performed upon reciting or hearing a specific verse of prostration.
الصلوية (al-salawiyyah): Relating to the prayer (salah); here, 'sajdah salawiyyah' means the sajdah that is part of the prayer itself, not an external act.
المدرك (al-mudrik): One who catches the imam in a rak'ah, thus being considered to have performed that rak'ah with the imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person hears an imam recite a sajdah verse but follows him in a different rak'ah, what does the Hanafi school require?
A) Prostrate immediately inside the prayer.
B) Prostrate externally after the prayer.
C) The sajdah is waived entirely.
D) Repeat the entire prayer.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires sajdah al-tilawah for a listener, but catching the imam's rak'ah after his prostration fulfills the obligation within the prayer—no separate prostration is needed.

Rulings on Repetition of Sajdah and Change of Place
Explains when multiple sajdahs are required and effect of changing place

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on whether one or two sajdahs are required when a sajdah verse is recited multiple times, and explain the effect of changing the place (majlis) on that ruling.

Core Idea
One sajdah suffices for multiple recitations in the same session; changing the place requires two prostrations.

In this lesson, we examine a refined ruling from the Hashiyah on sajdah al-tilawah. The key issue: when a sajdah verse is recited multiple times, does one prostration cover all, or is each recitation distinct? The Hanafi answer hinges on the concept of 'majlis' (session) and the strength of prayer-prostration. We will explore the authoritative position from Zahir al-Riwayah and the contrasting view from Nawadir, along with al-Sarakhsi's reconciliation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that sajdah al-tilawah is wajib. The passage rules on multiplicity: how many sajdahs are wajib when a verse is recited multiple times in and out of prayer.
2
Locate the dalil
The ruling is based on the apparent narrations (Zahir al-Riwayah) from the core books of Imam Muhammad. The term 'Zahir al-Riwayah' itself functions as evidence.
The passage also mentions Nawadir as a weaker alternative.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The reasoning: prayer-prostration is stronger (salawiyyah) and thus can integrate the external recitation into itself, provided the place (majlis) remains unchanged.
If the place changes, the condition of continuity is lost, requiring two separate prostrations.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Nawadir holds that two sajdahs are required even without physical change of place, because entering prayer itself changes the majlis. Al-Sarakhsi reconciled: speech (kalam) changes the place, but entering prayer does not.
This reconciliation does not alter the precedence of Zahir al-Riwayah.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The mufta bihi is the position of Zahir al-Riwayah: one prostration in prayer suffices for both external and internal recitation if the place remains the same. Al-Sarakhsi's reconciliation is accepted in methodology.
Authority weight: zahir_riwayah.

Thus it is benefited from the Sharh.
Source pages p. 492

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement from the hashiyah, explaining in detail the rulings on multiple sajdahs and the effect of changing the place (majlis). Key points: (1) The obligating recitation is defined, excluding non-obligating ones like sleep. (2) If one recites a sajdah verse again in prayer after having already prostrated externally, a new sajdah is required inside the prayer because the prayer-prostration is stronger and not a follower of the external one. (3) If one did not prostrate earlier outside, one prostration inside suffices for both (external and internal recitation) in the apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwayah). (4) If the place changes (e.g., by eating more than two morsels, walking more than two steps), two prostrations become necessary because a condition (continuity of place) is lost. (5) The passage also discusses the ruling for menstruating women (exempted) and the linguistic issue of the term 'salawiyyah' vs 'salatiyyah'. The authority weight is Zahir al-Riwayah for the apparent narration, while Nawadir is mentioned as a contrast. The commentator refines points from earlier commentaries, citing al-Atabi, al-Kamal, al-Sarakhsi, and others.

Key Terms
المجلس (al-majlis): The physical session or place where one recites or hears the sajdah verse; changing it (e.g., by eating, walking) affects whether multiple sajdahs are required.
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The apparent and most authoritative narrations from the six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, which form the foundation of the school.
رواية النوادر (riwayat al-nawadir): Rare or non-mainstream narrations transmitted from the founding imams but not part of the six core books; less authoritative.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwayah), if someone recites a sajdah verse outside prayer, does not prostrate, then enters prayer and recites the same verse, what is required?
A) Two prostrations (one outside, one inside)
B) One prostration inside, which suffices for both
C) One prostration outside after prayer
D) No prostration is required

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a single prostration in prayer suffices for multiple sajdah verses recited in the same session due to the strength of the prayer-prostration, provided the place has not changed.

Sajdah Tilawah: One or Two Prostrations for Repeated Recitation?
Ruling on prostration for recitation twice: outside then inside prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling that one prostration inside prayer suffices for a prior recitation outside the prayer, and identify when a change of majlis necessitates a separate prostration.

Core Idea
One prostration inside prayer covers earlier recitation if the majlis stays unchanged.

Reciting or hearing a verse of prostration (āyah al-sajdah) obligates a prostration (sajdah tilawah) in the Hanafi school. A common scenario arises when a person recites the verse outside prayer, then enters prayer and recites it again. Does this require two prostrations or just one? The Ḥāshiyat al-Ṭaḥṭāwī clarifies that, according to the well-known transmission (ẓāhir al-riwāyah), a single prostration performed in prayer suffices for both recitations – provided the session (majlis) has not changed. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its proof, and the subtle conditions that can require two prostrations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
Read the passage and identify the three possible sequences: (a) recitation outside then inside prayer, with prior prostration; (b) recitation outside without prostration then inside; (c) change of majlis between recitations.
The key variable is whether the majlis (e.g., physical place or continuity of session) changes.
2
Understand Tadākhul (Overlap)
Grasp the principle of tadākhul: multiple causes (recitations) yield a single obligation if they occur in one continuous session. This is based on the Prophet's practice and istiḥsān to avoid hardship.
Zāhir al-riwāyah applies tadākhul to the causes, not the rulings.
3
Apply the Concept of Ṣalawiyyah
Recognize that the prostration performed inside prayer has a stronger connection to prayer (ṣalawiyyah). This strength makes the outside prostration subordinate to it, so one inside suffices for both.
The text states: 'due to its strength (li-qūwatihā)', meaning the prayer-prostration overrides the earlier one.
4
Distinguish When Two Prostrations Are Required
Identify what constitutes a change of majlis: eating more than two bites, walking more than two steps, speaking, or any act that breaks the continuity. In such cases, two separate prostrations are obligatory.
The ḥāshiyah also mentions the narration of al-Nawādir, which considers entering prayer itself a change – but the relied-upon position is the ẓāhir al-riwāyah.

If he performed it inside and then the prayer became invalid, he does not repeat the prostration because the invalidator is a concurrent part that prevents building upon it. The menstruating woman is exempt from the prostration due to menstruation, like prayer, and the same ruling applies to the postpartum woman. If he recites a verse outside the prayer and prostrates for it, then enters the prayer and repeats the recitation in it, i.e., in the prayer in his place, he performs another prostration because it is not subordinate to the outside one due to the strength of the prayer's status. Thus it is derived from the commentary.
Source pages p. 493

Commentary
This passage is a critical commentary on a matn from Maraqi al-Falah regarding the rulings of Sajdah al-Tilawah (prostration of recitation) when a verse of prostration is recited outside of prayer and then again inside prayer. The hashya provides detailed elaboration on different scenarios. The main ruling is that if someone recites a sajdah verse outside prayer, prostrates, then enters prayer and recites the same verse again, a second prostration is required during prayer because the first prostration is not subordinate to the second due to the stronger connection of the latter to prayer. However, if the person did not prostrate when reciting outside, then the one prostration performed inside suffices for both recitations, according to the 'zahir al-riwayah' (the well-known transmission). This is because the prayer-related prostration has a stronger status, making the outside one subordinate. If the 'majlis' (session) changes—for example, by eating, walking more than two steps, or talking—then two separate prostrations are required. The hashya also discusses intra-Hanafi disputes: in the narration of al-Nawadir, two prostrations are required even without a change of place, because entering prayer constitutes a change of majlis. The reconciling position of al-Sarakhsi is mentioned, distinguishing between cases where speech occurs (which cuts the ruling of the majlis) versus where it does not. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the zahir al-riwayah. The commentary emphasizes the concept of 'tadakhul' (overlap) and the strength of the prayer's connection ('salawiyyah') in these rulings.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The well-known and authoritative transmission within the Hanafi school, as recorded in the six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.
صلوية (salawiyyah): The attribute of being connected to or having the ruling of prayer; here, the prostration performed during prayer has a stronger 'salawiyyah' than one performed outside, making it cover multiple recitations.
تداخل (tadakhul): Overlap or consolidation of acts; multiple causes (recitations) yield a single ruling (one prostration) when in one session, due to the principle of avoiding hardship and following the Prophet's practice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone recites a sajdah verse outside prayer without prostrating, then enters prayer and recites the same verse, how many prostrations are required according to zahir al-riwayah?
A) One prostration, performed inside the prayer.
B) Two prostrations, one for each recitation.
C) One prostration, performed outside the prayer.
D) No prostration is required.

Key Takeaway
When a sajdah verse is recited outside the prayer then again inside the same majlis, one prostration inside suffices if no prior outside prostration was performed; otherwise two are needed.

Sajdah Tilawah After Salam and Tadakhul in Cause
Ruling on sajdah after salam and tadakhul principle

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sajdah tilawah after prayer and explain the distinction between tadakhul fi al-sabab and tadakhul fi al-hukm.

Core Idea
Multiple sajdah recitations in one session require one prostration, but recitation after salam needs a new one.

This lesson examines a subtle issue from the hashya: if a person recites a sajdah verse during prayer and then again after salam, does the first prostration suffice? The answer hinges on the concept of 'salawiyyah' (prayer-connection) and the Hanafi principle of tadakhul (overlap). Understanding this distinction between overlap in the cause and overlap in the ruling is essential for correctly applying the rules of sajdah tilawah and for appreciating how Hanafi usul lenifies worship while maintaining strictness in punishments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being discussed? Reciting the same sajdah verse during prayer and then again after salam. According to zahir al-riwayah, a second prostration is wajib.
The ruling is based on loss of salawiyyah after salam.
2
Understand the role of salawiyyah
The prostration performed during prayer has a special connection to prayer (salawiyyah) that is stronger than an independent act. After salam, this connection is lost, so a new recitation is considered a fresh cause requiring its own prostration.
This distinguishes the case from multiple recitations all outside prayer.
3
Contrast with multiple recitations in one session
If the recitations all occur in a single session (majlis) without a break in the prayer connection, only one prostration suffices due to tadakhul fi al-sabab (overlap in the cause).
The Prophet's practice and avoidance of hardship support this.
4
Distinguish tadakhul fi al-sabab from tadakhul fi al-hukm
In acts of worship, tadakhul is applied to the cause (multiple recitations are treated as one cause), so one prostration covers all. In punishments, tadakhul is applied to the ruling (multiple offenses yield one penalty, but recurrence after punishment triggers a new penalty).
This distinction reflects the different objectives: leniency in worship, deterrence in punishment.
5
Apply the distinction to the given case
Since the first recitation was during prayer (high salawiyyah) and the second after salam (no salawiyyah), they are not part of the same cause. Even if the session is one, the change in state (prayer vs non-prayer) prevents tadakhul. Hence two prostrations are required.
The same principle applies if the verse is recited by two different people in the same session: one prostration suffices because the cause is the same session.

وإذا سجد في الصلاة ثم أعادها بعد سلامه يسجد أخرى في ظاهر الرواية لعدم بقاء الصلوية حكماً كمن كررها أي الآية الواحدة في مجلس واحد حيث تكفيه سجدة واحدة سواء كانت في ابتداء التلاوة، أو أثنائها، أو بعدها الوجوب عملاً بالقياس لعدم الحرج. قوله : (وهذا تداخل في السبب بأن تجعل التلاوات المتعدّدة حقيقة كتلاوة واحدة حكماً، فتكون الواحدة سبباً، والباقي تبعاً لها لأنها جنس واحد، فيجب حكم واحد، ويلحق ما تأخر منها عن السجود بما تقدم عليه قوله : (لأنه أليق بالعبادات) بيان ذلك أن التداخل إذا كان في الحكم دون السبب كانت الأسباب باقية على تعددها، فيلزم ترك العبادة مع وجود سببها الموجب لها، وهو شنيع لأنّ فيه ترك الاحيتاط فيما يجب فيه الاحتياط، فقلنا بتداخل الأسباب فيها ليكون جميعها بمنزلة سبب واحد ترتب عليه حكمه إذا وجد دليل الجمع، وهو اتحاد المجلس، فأما العقوبات فليست مما يحتاط فيها بل في درئها فيجعل التداخل في الحكم ليكون عدم الحكم مع وجود الموجب مضافاً إلى عفو الله تعالى. قوله: (والتداخل في الحكم الخ) هو جعل الأسباب المتعدّدة موجبة حكماً واحداً مع بقاء تعددها، فلا يلحق ما تأخر منها عن الحكم بما تقدم عليه، وهو الأصل في التداخل لأن التداخل أمر حكمي يثبت بخلاف القياس إذ الأصل أن لكل سبب حكماً فيليق بالأحكام لثبوت الأسباب حساً بخلاف الأحكام، واعتبار الثابت حساً غير ثابت أبعد من اعتبار الثابت حكماً غير ثابت. قوله : (مراراً) عائد إلى الشرب، وإلى الزنا أي لو شرب مراراً في مجلس بحيث تبقى رائحة الشرب
And if he prostrates in the prayer, then repeats it after his salam, he prostrates another according to the apparent narration, because the ruling of the prayer-connection does not remain, like one who repeats it, i.e., the same verse in one session, where one prostration suffices him, whether it is at the beginning of the recitation, or during it, or after it, due to overlap (tadakhul), because the Prophet (ﷺ) used to recite it to his companions repeatedly and prostrate once, and this is overlap in the cause, not in the ruling, so it stands in for what comes before and after it, because it is more suitable for acts of worship. Overlap in the ruling only stands in for the previous, not the subsequent, and it is more suitable for punishments. So the hadd penalty after drinking or fornication multiple times is sufficient for them, and if it returns, it is repeated because it is for deterrence, and... His saying: 'because the ruling of the prayer-connection does not remain' said in the commentary: because what is recited in the prayer does not exist in reality or in ruling, and what exists is that which follows, not what is non-existent. So it is not said that the session is one and the recited is one, and its consequence is that one prostration suffices due to the difference in the repeated between being one, even if it preceded what is repeated. His saying: 'like one who repeats it in one session' there is no difference in the repeated between being one or multiple, such as if he hears the prostration from a man, then hears it in that session from another, then recites it therein, then one prostration suffices him. His saying: 'whether it was at the beginning of the recitation, etc.' it is better to say at the beginning of the repetition. He said in al-Qunyah: and it is better to hasten and prostrate then repeat, and it was objected in al-Bahr that it is better to delay the prostration because it has been said that the overlap in it is in the ruling, not in the cause. So caution dictates this delay, as is not hidden. And in the commentary, repeating the salutation upon the Prophet (ﷺ) is recommended, not the prostration of recitation. His saying: 'because the Prophet, etc.' And because repeating the recitation is needed for memorization and teaching, so if the obligation were repeated, hardship would be required, and it is removed, unlike when the session or the recited increases, where the obligation is repeated operationally due to analogy, because there is no hardship. His saying: 'and this is overlap in the cause' by making the multiple recitations in reality like one recitation in ruling, so the one is the cause and the rest are subordinate to it because they are one genus, so one ruling is obligatory, and what is delayed from the prostration follows what precedes it. His saying: 'because it is more suitable for acts of worship' the explanation of that is that if the overlap is in the ruling without the cause, the causes remain multiple, so it necessitates abandoning the act of worship while its causing reason exists, which is abominable because it involves abandoning caution in what requires caution. So we said that the causes overlap in them so that all of them are like one cause upon which its ruling is based when the evidence of combination is found, which is the unity of the session. As for punishments, they are not something in which caution is exercised, rather caution is in averting them. So the overlap is made in the ruling so that the absence of the ruling despite the presence of the cause is attributed to the forgiveness of Allah. His saying: 'and overlap in the ruling, etc.' is to make multiple causes necessitate one ruling while their multiplicity remains, so what is delayed from the ruling does not follow what precedes it, and this is the original in overlap because overlap is a legal matter that is established contrary to analogy, since the original is that each cause has a ruling. So it is suitable for rulings because the causes are established sensibly, unlike rulings. And considering what is sensibly established as non-established is more remote than considering what is legally established as non-established. His saying: 'repeatedly' refers to drinking and to fornication, meaning if he drinks repeatedly in a session such that the smell of drink remains...
Source pages p. 494

Commentary
This passage from the hashya addresses the scenario where a person performs the sajdah tilawah during prayer, then after completing the prayer (salam), recites the same prostration verse again. According to the zahir al-riwayah, a second prostration is required because the 'salawiyyah' (prayer-connection) no longer exists after the prayer ends. The commentary then delves into the general principle of tadakhul (overlap) for multiple recitations of the same sajdah verse in one session. The key principle is that if multiple recitations occur in a single majlis (session) without change of place, one prostration suffices. This is based on the Prophet's practice and the need to avoid hardship. The commentary distinguishes between tadakhul in the cause (asbāb) and tadakhul in the ruling (hukm). For acts of worship ('ibadat), the Hanafi school applies tadakhul in the cause, meaning multiple recitations are treated as one cause, so one prostration covers them all. For punishments ('uqubat), tadakhul is applied in the ruling: a single punishment suffices for multiple offenses in one session, but if the offense recurs after the punishment, it is repeated because the purpose is deterrence. This distinction is justified by the different objectives: caution and avoidance of burden in worship, versus deterrence and leniency in punishments. The passage also discusses a minor issue: whether one should prostrate immediately upon recitation or delay. The preferred view is to delay until after completing the repetition, to ensure the overlap is in the cause.

Key Terms
تداخل في السبب (tadakhul fi al-sabab): Overlap in the cause: multiple recitations are considered as a single cause for the obligation of prostration, so one prostration suffices.
تداخل في الحكم (tadakhul fi al-hukm): Overlap in the ruling: multiple offenses are covered by a single punishment (hadd), and the punishment does not repeat unless the offense recurs after execution.
صلوية (salawiyyah): The status of being connected to prayer; after salam, this status is lost, so a new prostration is required for recitation after prayer even if the same verse was recited during prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person recites a sajdah verse during prayer and prostrates, then recites the same verse again after finishing the prayer (salam), how many prostrations are required according to zahir al-riwayah?
A) One prostration, because the verse is the same and the session is one.
B) Two prostrations: one during prayer and one after salam.
C) No prostration, because the first sufficed.
D) One prostration after salam, because the prayer is over.

Key Takeaway
Sajdah tilawah after salam requires a new prostration because the prayer connection is lost, and this case is distinct from multiple recitations in a single session where one prostration suffices due to tadakhul fi al-sabab.
