Tadakhul in Sajdat al-Tilawah: Repeated Recitation in One Sitting
Explains ruling and rationale for single prostration when verse repeated in same sitting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on repeated sajdat al-tilawah in one sitting, explain the principle of tadakhul (legal overlap), and distinguish between tadakhul in sabab (cause) and tadakhul in hukm (ruling).

Core Idea
One prostration suffices for multiple recitations in one sitting because tadakhul in the cause merges them into a single obligation.

In this lesson, we examine a refined ruling from the late Hanafi tradition: when a verse of sajdah is recited multiple times in the same sitting, only one prostration is required. This is based on the principle of tadakhul (legal overlap), which operates differently for acts of worship than for punishments. Al-Tahtawi's commentary on Maraqi al-Falah clarifies the underlying distinction and its practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine the hukm of sajdat al-tilawah (wajib) and the specific scenario: multiple recitations in one sitting.
2
State the Hanafi position
One prostration suffices for all recitations in one sitting, whether at the beginning, during, or after the recitations.
3
Analyze the dalil
The Prophet's practice of reciting the verse repeatedly and prostrating once is cited. Identify the proof type (sunnah ahad) and its implications.
4
Distinguish tadakhul in sabab vs. hukm
For acts of worship, tadakhul is in the sabab (cause), while for punishments it is in the hukm. Explain why this distinction matters.

Like one who repeats the same verse in one sitting: one prostration suffices, whether at the beginning of recitation, during it, or after it, due to tadakhul (overlap). Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to recite it repeatedly to his companions and prostrate once. This is tadakhul in the cause (sabab), not the ruling (hukm). It suffices for what came before and after because it is more fitting for acts of worship. Tadakhul in the ruling only suffices for what preceded, not what follows, and is more fitting for punishments. So the hadd punishment after repeated drinking or zina in one sitting suffices for all. Source pages p. 494

Commentary
This is a passage from the Hashiya of al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah, refining the earlier commentary. It addresses the ruling when a verse of prostration is recited multiple times in one sitting (majlis). The key principle is tadakhul (overlap/integration). The author differentiates between tadakhul in the cause (sabab) and tadakhul in the ruling (hukm). For acts of worship, tadakhul is in the cause: multiple recitations are treated as one cause, thus one prostration fulfills all. For punishments, tadakhul is in the ruling: multiple acts produce one penalty, but if acts are in separate sittings, penalties repeat. The proof is the Prophet's practice and the principle of avoiding hardship (haraj). The author also discusses a nuance: if one repeats the prostration after prayer, it does not overlap because the 'prayer-state' no longer exists. Additionally, the commentary critiques the preferred practice of delaying prostration vs. immediate prostration before repeating.

Key Terms
تداخل (tadakhul): Legal overlap where multiple causes produce a single effect due to unity of gathering or other connecting factor.
مجلس (majlis): The sitting or assembly in which recitation occurs; unity of majlis triggers tadakhul.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Two prostrations are required.
D) Sajdah is not required unless recited in prayer.

Key Takeaway
One prostration suffices for multiple recitations of the same sajdah verse in one sitting due to tadakhul in the cause.

When Does a New Majlis Obligate a New Prostration?
Lists cases defining change of majlis for sajdat al-tilawah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify whether a given action constitutes a change of majlis for sajdat al-tilawah according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Three steps in open, weaving, swimming – change the majlis; moving within a mosque does not.

The obligation of sajdat al-tilawah upon reciting or hearing a sajdah verse is affected by whether a change of majlis (sitting/standing place) has occurred. The Hanafi fiqh provides precise criteria – from three steps to weaving – to determine this. This lesson unpacks the key cases and exceptions from the text, helping you apply the rule with confidence.

Guided Path
1
Understand the General Principle
The majlis changes when one physically departs from the original location. The text specifies thresholds and activities that constitute valid departure.
This is based on the concept that a new prostration is only required if a new ‘assembly’ is formed.
2
Examine Open Space Movements
Moving three steps in a desert or road (open area) constitutes a change. This is the baseline threshold.
The number of steps is significant; fewer than three does not change the majlis.
3
Analyze Specific Activities
Weaving (tasdiya) when moving the loom, moving from one tree branch to another, swimming in a large river or tank, threshing, and walking around a mill each change the majlis. For weaving, the sounder view (al-asahh) is that it changes.
The activity must involve substantial movement or a shift in location.
4
Identify Exceptions
Moving within a small house (to its corners) or within a large mosque (even to another corner) does not change the majlis. The mosque remains one majlis for the sake of iqtida' (following the imam).
This exception is based on the continuity of the gathering.
5
Apply the Tarjih for Weaving
The text states 'fi al-asahh' (in the soundest view) for weaving. This means the relied-upon position is that weaving changes the majlis, although some earlier views differed.
The mufta bihi (operative for fatwa) is that weaving does change the majlis.

Source pages p. 495

Commentary
This passage enumerates specific cases that determine whether a change of majlis occurs, which would necessitate a new prostration if the same verse is recited again. The threshold for change in open spaces is moving three steps. For a weaver, the sounder view is that the majlis changes when he moves the loom. Other cases: moving between branches of the same tree (according to Zahir al-Riwayah), swimming in a large body of water, threshing, walking around a mill. Conversely, moving within a small house or a large mosque does not change the majlis. The note at the end extends the concept of tadakhul to sneezing and sending salawat upon the Prophet, citing different scholarly opinions.

Key Terms
تبدل المجلس (tabaddul al-majlis): Legal change of sitting/assembly, determined by physical movement or change of location, affecting obligation of prostration.
تسدية (tasdiya): The act of weaving at a loom; debated whether it constitutes a change of majlis.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defines change of majlis through specific physical movements and locations, with clear exceptions for mosques and small houses.

Actions That Change the Majlis in Sujud al-Tilawah
Ruling on what changes the majlis for sujud al-tilawah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which actions constitute a change of majlis for sujud al-tilawah and apply the ruling to these cases.

Core Idea
Moving three steps, weaving, or swimming breaks the majlis; you must prostrate again.

In this lesson, we explore the key principle that the obligation of sujud al-tilawah repeats only if the majlis (gathering) changes. The text from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi lists specific actions that constitute change, such as taking three steps, moving between tree branches, and swimming in a large body of water. Understanding these triggers ensures correct performance of this wajib act.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base rule
The default is that one prostration is required unless the gathering changes.
2
List the actions that change the majlis
From the text: three steps in desert/road, weaving (tasdiya), moving from one tree branch to another, swimming in river or large basin, threshing, going around a mill.
3
Apply to a scenario
Given a case, determine if the action qualifies as a change.
4
Note the exception
The weaver who operates a wheel (dawwara) does not change majlis if he remains in place.

He is deterred by the first (not) in (two gatherings) due to lack of what necessitates overlapping. The gathering changes by moving from it by three steps in the desert and road, even if he is weaving (tasdiya) in the most correct view, such that he goes with the warp in his hand and throws it onto sticks inserted in the wall and ground, not the one who operates a wheel called a 'dawwara' onto which he throws the warp, while he is sitting or standing in a place. And the gathering changes by moving from one branch of a tree to another branch of it in the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah), and it is correct. And the gathering changes in swimming (hawm) i.e., swimming in a river or swimming in a large basin, and threshing and going around a mill due to the change of place. His statement (in the most correct applies to all the issues). And (does not change) the gathering of hearing and recitation by the corners of a small house. And (does not) change the gathering of recitation by the corners of a mosque, even if it is large, due to the validity of following (iqtida) with spaciousness within it. And (does not) change the gathering of recitation and hearing by the movement of a ship, as if it were stationary. And (does not) change by one rak'ah in which recitation is repeated, by agreement. And (does not) change by two rak'ahs according to Abu Yusuf, contrary to Muhammad, and likewise the difference in the second pair (shaf') of the obligatory (prayer) if he repeats it therein, and by repeating it in the second pair of the sunnah of zuhr, he prostrates a second time. And (does not) change by drinking one sip, eating two mouthfuls, and walking two steps in the desert, contrary to more than that. Nor by leaning, sitting, and standing without walking in the desert. And (does not) change by mounting and dismounting occurring in his place of recitation as in al-Khaniyyah. And (does not) change the gathering by the movement of his riding beast if he repeats it while praying, because the gathering is considered one due to the necessity of the validity of prayer. And the obligation is repeated upon the listener if his gathering changes while the gathering of the reciter is one, such that he heard a reciter in a place, then the listener went away and returned and heard him repeating it; prostration is repeated upon the listener by consensus. And (does not) the obligation is repeated upon the listener in a case like when he moves in a ship without movement.
Source pages p. 495

Commentary
This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi explains the rules regarding the repetition of sujud al-tilawah (prostration of recitation) when a verse of prostration is recited multiple times. The key principle is that the obligation is repeated only if the 'majlis' (gathering/place) changes. The passage defines what constitutes a change of majlis and what does not. The author lists specific scenarios: 1) Moving three steps in the desert or road changes the majlis, even if one is engaged in weaving (tasdiya). 2) Moving from one branch of a tree to another, according to the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah), changes it. 3) Swimming in a river or large basin, threshing, and going around a mill change it. However, moving within the corners of a small house or a large mosque does not change the majlis, because the validity of following the imam (iqtida) holds even with spaciousness. Similarly, riding on a ship that is stationary does not change it. Within prayer, reciting in one rak'ah does not require multiple prostrations by agreement. For two rak'ahs, Abu Yusuf holds that one prostration suffices, while Muhammad holds that two are required; this difference also applies to the second pair (shaf') of obligatory prayer. For the sunnah of zuhr, repeating in the second pair requires a second prostration. Small actions like drinking one sip, eating two mouthfuls, walking two steps, leaning, sitting, standing without walking, mounting or dismounting in the same place do not break the majlis. However, if the listener changes his location while the reciter remains in one place, the listener's obligation is repeated by consensus. This passage clarifies the delicate fiqh of spatial continuity and its effect on devotional acts.

Key Terms
المجلس (al-majlis): The physical location or place where one is present; also the conceptual 'gathering' that determines whether multiple acts are considered in one sitting.
السجود التلاوة (sujud al-tilawah): The prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a specific verse of the Quran that contains a command of sajdah.
التسدية (al-tasdiyah): Weaving or the action of a weaver moving back and forth; considered a change of majlis if done significantly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following actions changes the majlis?
A) Walking two steps in the desert
B) Moving from one branch of a tree to another
C) Leaning on a pillow
D) Drinking a sip of water

Key Takeaway
The obligation of sujud al-tilawah repeats when the physical place (majlis) changes, defined by three steps, weaving, tree branch movement, swimming, threshing, or going around a mill.

Actions That Do Not Change the Majlis and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling on what does not change the majlis and the dispute on two rak'ahs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify actions that do not change the majlis and explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement regarding two rak'ahs.

Core Idea
Corners of a mosque, stationary ship, and two rak'ahs after Abu Yusuf do not break the majlis.

This lesson continues the study of change of majlis in sujud al-tilawah. The text lists scenarios where the gathering remains intact despite physical movement: moving within corners of a house or mosque, riding on a stationary ship, and performing actions like drinking one sip or eating two mouthfuls. It also addresses a key intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf holds that reciting a sajdah verse in two rak'ahs of the same prayer requires only one prostration, while Muhammad requires two. The relied-upon view is that of Abu Yusuf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base rule for non-change
The majlis remains intact unless a significant action occurs.
2
List actions that do not change the majlis
From text: moving within corners of a small house or large mosque, riding a stationary ship, one rak'ah, two rak'ahs (according to Abu Yusuf), small actions (one sip, two mouthfuls, two steps), leaning, sitting, standing without walking, mounting/dismounting in the same place, movement of riding beast while praying.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute on two rak'ahs
Abu Yusuf vs Muhammad: tahrimah unites the prayer as one place vs each rak'ah separate.
4
Apply the rule to the listener
If the listener changes his place while the reciter remains, the listener's obligation repeats by consensus. But if the listener is on a moving ship, it does not repeat.

Change of Assembly for the Reciter of Sajdah
Ruling on when reciter's assembly changes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when a change of assembly (majlis) occurs for sajdat al-tilawah and distinguish between minor and major actions according to the relied-upon view.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fiqh, the assembly for sajdat al-tilawah is not changed by minor actions or by the unity of prayer.

When reciting or hearing a verse of sajdah multiple times, the number of prostrations required depends on whether the assembly (majlis) has changed. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi criteria for a change of assembly, clarifying what constitutes a minor action versus a significant break. We will explore the intra-Hanafi difference between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on the effect of two rak'ahs and learn the relied-upon ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act under discussion is sajdat al-tilawah (prostration upon recitation/hearing a sajdah verse). In the Hanafi school, it is wajib. The question is: when repeated, how many sujud are required?
The ruling on sajdat al-tilawah itself is not detailed here; the focus is on the change of assembly.
2
Understand the concept of majlis (assembly)
The majlis is the setting in which the recitation occurs. A change of assembly typically requires a new sujud upon repetition. The Hanafi school defines change by significant movement or action.
Minor actions like drinking a sip or eating a morsel do not change the assembly.
3
Apply the principle of prayer unity
When the recitation occurs within a prayer, the takbirat al-ihram unifies the entire prayer as one assembly. Therefore, repeating a sajdah verse within the same prayer does not change the majlis.
This is the basis of Abu Yusuf's view that even two rak'ahs are considered one assembly.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on two rak'ahs
Imam Muhammad holds that each rak'ah is a separate assembly, so two sujud would be required. The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) follows Abu Yusuf, as indicated by 'al-ashah'.
This ikhtilaf also applies to the second set (shaf' thani) of obligatory prayer and sunnah of Zuhr.
5
Distinguish between minor and major actions
The passage lists actions that do not change assembly: drinking one sip, eating two morsels, walking two steps in desert, leaning, sitting, standing without walking, riding/dismounting in same place, movement of mount while praying. Actions exceeding these (e.g., walking more than two steps) do change the assembly.
The threshold for walking in the desert is two steps; more changes it. Actions like sailing on a ship do not change regardless.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفضاء فيه (ولا) يتبدل مجلس التلاوة والسماع بسير سفينة كما لو كانت واقفة (ولا) يتبدل (بركعة) تكررت فيها التلاوة اتفاقاً (و) لا يتبدل (بركعتين) عند أبي يوسف خلافاً لمحمد وكذا الخلاف في الشفع الثاني من الفرض إذا كررها فيه وبتكرارها في الشفع الثاني من سنة الظهر يسجد ثانياً (و) لا يتبدل بشرب شربة وأكل لقمتين ومشي خطوتين) في الصحراء بخلاف الأكثر منها ولا باتكاء وقعود وقيام بدون مشي في الصحراء (وركوب ونزول) كائن في محل (تلاوته كما في الخانية (و) لا يتبدل المجلس (بسير دابته) إذا كررها (مصلياً) لجعل المجلس متحداً ضرورة جواز الصلاة
The space in it: (and) the assembly of recitation and hearing is not changed by the movement of a ship, just as if it were stationary. (And) it is not changed by one rak'ah in which recitation is repeated, by agreement. (And) it is not changed by two rak'ahs according to Abu Yusuf, contrary to Muhammad. And similarly the difference in the second set of the obligatory prayer if one repeats it therein, and by repeating it in the second set of the sunnah of Zuhr, one prostrates a second time. (And) it is not changed by drinking a sip, eating two morsels, and walking two steps in the desert, contrary to more than that. And not by leaning, sitting, and standing without walking in the desert. (And) riding and dismounting that occurs in the place of his recitation, as in al-Khaniyyah. (And) the assembly is not changed by the movement of his mount when he repeats it while praying, because the assembly is considered unified by necessity of the validity of prayer.
Source pages p. 496

Commentary
This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi discusses the rulings on change of assembly (majlis) for the reciter of a verse of sajdah. The passage type is a critical refinement of the base text of Maraqi al-Falah. The author clarifies that certain actions do not constitute a change of assembly, thus if one repeats a verse of sajdah, they are only required to perform one sujud. For example, moving on a ship does not change the assembly, whether the ship is moving or stationary. Likewise, reciting in one rak'ah even if the recitation is repeated does not change the assembly by agreement. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding two rak'ahs: according to Abu Yusuf, two rak'ahs do not change the assembly, while Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that they do. This difference applies also to the second set of the obligatory prayer and the second set of the sunnah of Zuhr, where according to Abu Yusuf one sujud suffices, while Muhammad requires a second sujud. Minor actions like drinking one sip, eating two morsels, or walking two steps in the desert do not change the assembly, but more than that does. Actions like leaning, sitting, or standing without walking in the desert also do not change the assembly. Riding and dismounting in the same place do not change it. The movement of one's mount while praying does not change the assembly because the prayer requires unifying the place.

Key Terms
مجلس التلاوة (majlis al-tilawah): The assembly or setting in which a verse of sajdah is recited; a change of assembly may necessitate a new sujud upon repetition.
سجدة التلاوة (sajdat al-tilawah): The prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a specific verse of sajdah in the Quran.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Two sujoods are required because each rak'ah is a new assembly.
C) No sujud is required because it is within prayer.
D) It depends on whether the prayer is obligatory or supererogatory.

Key Takeaway
The assembly for sajdat al-tilawah remains unchanged by minor actions and by the unity of a single prayer, with Abu Yusuf's view being the mufta bihi.

Change of Assembly and Repetition of Sujud for the Listener
Ruling on when the listener's assembly changes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that the listener's sujud obligation repeats only when his own assembly changes, and distinguish between the two scenarios of assembly change.

Core Idea
The listener's sujud obligation is triggered by recitation, not hearing, so it repeats only when his assembly changes, not the reciter's.

We often think that hearing a sajdah verse multiple times requires multiple prostrations. However, the Hanafi school makes a nuanced distinction based on assembly change. In this lesson, we explore when the obligation of sujud al-tilawah repeats for the listener and why the majority view grounds this in the recitation as the cause.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Scenarios
The author presents two cases: (1) listener changes his assembly while the reciter stays; (2) reciter changes his assembly while the listener stays. Recognize which case is ruled by consensus and which by the most correct view.
In case 1, sujud repeats by consensus; in case 2, one sujud suffices according to al-ashah.
2
State the Ruling for Each Scenario
For scenario 1 (listener moves): obligation repeats upon the listener. For scenario 2 (reciter moves): obligation does not repeat; one sujud suffices.
3
Trace the Underlying Legal Cause (Sabab)
The difference hinges on whether the cause (sabab) of the obligation for the listener is the recitation (tilaawah) or the hearing (sama'). Determine which view the jumhur adopt and why.
The jumhur hold that the cause is the recitation; hearing is a condition (shart).
4
Apply Qiyas to the Reciter's Position
The reciter's obligation is due to his own recitation. By analogy, the listener's obligation is also due to the recitation, not the hearing. Therefore, if the reciter repeats the verse but the listener remains, the recitation is considered a single cause, so one sujud suffices.
This reasoning supports the most correct view.
5
Note the Ikhtilaf and Tarjih
Some Hanafi scholars (e.g., al-Aspijabi) hold that the cause is hearing, leading to repeat sujud in both scenarios. However, the relied-upon view is the jumhur's, with al-ashah and fatwa upon it.
Know the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf): in the second scenario, one sujud vs two.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويتكرر الوجوب على السامع بتبديل مجلسه و الحال أنه قد اتحد مجلس التالي) كأن سمع تالياً بمكان فذهب السامع ثم عاد فسمعه يكررها تكرر على السامع السجود إجماعاً (ولا) يتكرر الوجوب على السامع (بعكسه) وهو اتحاد مجلس السامع، واختلاف مجلس التالي بأن تلا فذهب ثم عاد مكرراً فسمعه الجالس أيضاً تكفيه سجدة على الأصح
And the obligation is repeated upon the listener by changing his assembly while the assembly of the reciter is unified - such as when he hears a reciter in a place, then the listener goes and returns and hears him repeating it; the prostration is repeated upon the listener by consensus. (And) the obligation is not repeated upon the listener in the opposite case - that is, when the listener's assembly is unified and the reciter's assembly changes, such as when the reciter recites and goes, then returns and repeats, and the sitting person hears it again; one prostration suffices him, according to the most correct view.
Source pages p. 496

Commentary
This passage discusses the change of assembly for the listener of a sajdah verse. The author distinguishes two scenarios. First, if the listener changes his assembly while the reciter remains in the same place, and the listener hears the reciter repeat the verse after returning, then the obligation of sujud is repeated upon the listener by consensus. This is because the listener's assembly changed. Second, if the listener remains in one place but the reciter changes his assembly (goes away and comes back to recite again), then the listener is only required to perform one sujud, according to the most correct view, because the listener's assembly did not change. The underlying dispute is whether the cause of obligation for the listener is the recitation (tilaawah) or the hearing (sama'). The majority (jumhur) hold that the cause is the recitation, but the condition for the listener is hearing. In the second scenario, since the listener's assembly is unified, the hearing is considered one event, so one sujud suffices.

Key Terms
السامع (al-sami'): The person who hears the recitation of a verse of sajdah; the ruling of sujud applies to him under certain conditions.
السبب (al-sabab): The legal cause that triggers the obligation of sujud; in this context, whether it is the recitation itself or the act of hearing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One sujud suffices because the listener's assembly did not change.
B) Two sujoods are required because the reciter changed his assembly.
C) No sujud is required because the listener did not move.
D) Four sujoods are required.

Key Takeaway
The obligation of sujud al-tilawah on the listener depends on the change of his own assembly, not the reciter's, because the cause is the recitation, and hearing is a condition.

Etiquette of Reciting Verses of Sajdah
Rulings on disliked and recommended acts regarding sajdah verses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings on skipping, reciting alone, and concealing the verse of sajdah, and apply them in recitation practice.

Core Idea
Skipping a sajdah verse within a surah is like disdain; but reciting it alone is fine, and adding more verses and concealing is recommended.

Reciting the Qur'an with proper etiquette (adab) is essential for a believer. One specific area involves verses of sajdah (prostration). This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi clarifies what is disliked (makruh) and what is recommended (mandub) when reciting such verses. Understanding these rulings helps avoid behavior that may resemble disdain (istinkaf) and ensures we fulfill the act with mindfulness and consideration for others.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
First, find the main ruling about skipping a sajdah verse when reciting a surah. The text states it is disliked (makruh). Understand the reason: it resembles disdain (istinkaf).
Istinkaf is the act of Iblis who refused to prostrate.
2
Differentiate the exception
Note that reciting the sajdah verse alone is not disliked. This is because it is an act of hastening to the prostration, not avoidance.
The key is intention: skipping vs. singling out.
3
List the recommended acts
Identify three recommended (mandub) actions: (1) adding extra verses to the sajdah verse, (2) concealing the verse from unprepared listeners, and (3) standing for prostration if reciting while sitting.
These are praiseworthy but not obligatory.
4
Reflect on the rationale
Consider the wisdom behind each ruling: avoiding resemblance to Iblis, showing eagerness, removing suspicion of preference, and showing compassion for listeners.
Hanafi fiqh often provides rationale (ta'lil) for rulings.
5
Apply to a scenario
Imagine you are reciting a surah with a sajdah verse in a gathering. Use the rulings to decide how to proceed: do not skip the verse, consider adding a few verses, and assess if the listeners are ready for prostration; if not, recite quietly.
Application solidifies understanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكره أن يقرأ سورة ويدع آية (السجدة منها لأنه يشبه الاستنكاف عنها (لا) يكره أن وهو يفرد آية السجدة بالقراءة لأنه مبادرة إليها (و) لكن ندب ضم آية أو) ضم (أكثر) من آية (إليها) أي إلى آية السجدة لدفع توهم التفضيل (وندب إخفاؤها) يعني استحب المشايخ إخفاءها عن غير متأهب لها شفقة على السامعين إن لم يتهيؤا لها (وندب القيام لمن تلا جالساً (ثم السجود لها) روي ذلك الله عنها
And it is disliked that one recites a surah and leaves out the verse of sajdah from it, because that resembles disdain for it. (No) it is not disliked that one recites the verse of sajdah alone, because it is an act of hastening to it. (And) but it is recommended to add a verse or more to it, i.e., to the verse of sajdah, to remove the suspicion of preference. (And) it is recommended to conceal it, meaning the scholars recommended concealing it from those not prepared for it, out of compassion for the listeners if they are not ready for it. (And) it is recommended that one who recites while sitting should stand for the prostration, then prostrate for it. That has been narrated from Aisha, may Allah be pleased with her.
Source pages p. 497

Commentary
This passage details the etiquettes (adab) related to reciting verses of sajdah. The author states that it is disliked (makruh) to recite a surah that contains a sajdah verse and intentionally skip that verse, because this resembles disdain (istinkaf) for the prostration. Such behavior is not befitting of a believer, as it could imply avoidance of obligation and abandonment of part of the Quran. However, it is not disliked to recite only the verse of sajdah by itself, as that is an act of hastening to fulfill the duty. It is recommended (mandub) to include an additional verse or more along with the sajdah verse to avoid the misconception that one favors the sajdah verse over others. It is also recommended to recite the verse quietly (ikhfa') if there are listeners who may not be prepared to prostrate, out of consideration for them. Finally, it is recommended that if one recites while sitting, he should stand for the prostration, as narrated from Aisha. This recommendation applies similarly to a rider who should dismount to prostrate on the ground.

Key Terms
الاستنكاف (al-istinkaf): Disdain or refusal to prostrate; the text considers skipping the sajdah verse as resembling istinkaf.
ندب (nadb): Recommended (mandub) act; performing it is rewarded but omitting it is not sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on reciting a surah that contains a verse of sajdah and intentionally omitting that verse?
A) It is recommended to omit it to avoid repetition.
B) It is disliked because it resembles disdain for the prostration.
C) It is permissible without any dislike.
D) It is obligatory to include it.

Key Takeaway
Skipping a sajdah verse within a surah is makruh tahrimi, while reciting it alone is fine; adding verses and concealing are recommended to show respect and compassion.

Cause for Listener's Sajdah: Same' or Tilawah?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on sabab of listener's sajdah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on the cause for the listener's sajdah and apply them to a scenario of multiple recitations.

Core Idea
The listener's sajdah may repeat if the cause is tilawah, not sama'.

When reciter repeats a sajdah verse in different sessions, must a listener who remains seated perform multiple sajdahs? Hanafi scholars disagree on the underlying cause (sabab). This lesson examines two valid positions and their proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
The reciter recites a sajdah verse, leaves, returns, and recites it again while the listener stays seated. The core question: does the listener owe one sajdah or multiple?
2
State the Asahh Opinion
The most sound opinion (asahh) holds that one sajdah suffices because the cause for the listener is hearing (sama'), and his session remains unchanged. This view is supported by hadith and many authorities (Hidayah, Qadikhan).
Asahh here means preferred within this transmitted evidence.
3
State the Alternative Opinion
Al-Asbijabi and Fakhr al-Islam hold that the obligation repeats for the listener because the cause is the reciter's recitation (tilawah), not hearing. Hearing is only a condition. Since the reciter's session changes, each recitation triggers a new wajib.
This view also has fatwa.
4
Examine the Proofs
Both opinions rely on the same hadith from Aisha (رضي الله عنها) which states obligation on the listener but does not specify the cause. The difference lies in whether the ruling is attached to the cause (tilawah) or the condition (sama').
The hadith is zanni al-thubut, allowing ijtihad.
5
Note the Tarjih
Al-Sayyid states that tarjih (preference) differs among scholars. Both positions are considered operative (mufta bihi) by different authorities. No single preference is declared.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اتحاد مجلس السامع، واختلاف مجلس التالي بأن تلا فذهب ثم عاد مكرراً فسمعه الجالس أيضاً تكفيه سجدة على الأصح لأن السبب في حقه السماع، ولم يتبدل مجلسه ويؤيده ما عن عائشة رضي الله عنها نأخذ وبه على الأصح وعليه الفتوى نهر واختاره صاحب الهداية، وقاضيخان قال الحلبي : قال في المنح : وهذا يفيد تصحيح القول بأن السبب في حق السامع هو السماع دون التلاوة، مر من الأثر السجدة على من سمعها ،أهـ، وقيل: يتكرر على السامع أيضاً، وهو اختيار الأسبيجابي وعليه الفتوى ونقله الأكمل بقيل، وعليه الفتوى، وهو قول فخر الإسلام إذ مجلس التالي إذا تكرر دون السامع يتكرر الوجوب على السامع لأن الحكم يضاف إلى السبب، وهو التلاوة لا إلى الشرط، وهو السماع، وهذا هو ما عليه الجمهور لأن الصحيح أن السبب في حق السامع هو التلاوة كالتالي والسماع بشرط عمل التلاوة في حق السامع اهـ، وليس في الحديث بيان السبب، بل بيان الوجوب على السامع اهـ كذا في الشرح. قال السيد : فقد اختلف الترجيح.
The unity of the listener's session and the difference of the reciter's session: if he recited then left then returned repeatedly and the sitting one heard him again, one prostration suffices according to the most sound opinion because the cause for him is hearing, and his session did not change. It is supported by what is [reported] from Aisha, may Allah be pleased with her, which we take and act upon, according to the most sound opinion and upon it is the fatwa, as in al-Nahr, and it was chosen by the author of al-Hidayah and Qadikhan. Al-Halabi said: He said in al-Minh: This benefits confirming the statement that the cause for the listener is hearing without recitation, from the transmitted effect: 'Prostration is upon whoever hears it.' End. And it was said: It repeats for the listener as well, and it is the choice of al-Asbijabi and upon it is the fatwa, al-Akmal transmitted it with 'qil', and upon it is the fatwa, and it is the statement of Fakhr al-Islam: when the reciter's session repeats without the listener, the obligation repeats upon the listener because the ruling is attributed to the cause, which is recitation, not to the condition, which is hearing. This is what the majority are upon because the correct opinion is that the cause for the listener is recitation like the reciter, and hearing is a condition for the effect of recitation regarding the listener, end. There is no statement of the cause in the hadith, rather a statement of obligation upon the listener, end. Thus in the commentary. Al-Sayyid said: So the tarjih differs.
Source pages p. 497

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the cause (sabab) that obligates sajdat al-tilawah for a listener. The core issue: when the reciter recites a sajdah verse in multiple separate sessions while the listener remains in one session, does one sajdah suffice or must multiple be performed? The most sound opinion (asahh) states that one sajdah suffices because the cause for the listener is hearing (sama'), and the listener's session did not change. This is supported by a hadith from Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) and is the relied-upon fatwa according to many authorities including al-Hidayah and Qadikhan. However, another opinion (attributed to al-Asbijabi and Fakhr al-Islam) holds that the obligation repeats for the listener because the true cause is the recitation (tilawah) by the reciter, and hearing is merely a condition for the effect. They argue that since the reciter's session changes, each recitation triggers a new obligation. Al-Sayyid notes that the tarjih (preference) differs among scholars. The author is critically analyzing these positions within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
اتحاد مجلس السامع (ittihād majlis al-sāmi'): The listener remains in the same physical session without changing location.
السبب (al-sabab): The cause that triggers the obligation of sajdah: either hearing (sama') or recitation (tilawah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the listener's session remains the same and the cause is hearing.
B) Because the reciter's intention is to repeat the same verse.
C) Because the listener must imitate the reciter exactly.
D) Because the verse is considered the same act of worship.

Key Takeaway
The sabab for the listener's sajdah is either sama' or tilawah, leading to different rulings on repetition; both views are within Hanafi orthodoxy.

Rulings on Reciting Sajdah Verses
Rulings on reciting sajdah verses and listener etiquette.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings related to reciting sajdah verses (makruh, mandub) and explain the rationale behind each.

Core Idea
Skipping a sajdah verse is makruh because it resembles disdain; reciting it alone is recommended as hastening.

This lesson covers the etiquettes (adab) of sajdat al-tilawah as detailed in the Hanafi school. You will learn when it is disliked to omit a sajdah verse, what is recommended when reciting such verses, and how listeners should respond. The rulings are based on the principles of avoiding resemblance to arrogance (istinkaf) and showing compassion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary ruling
What is the hukm for skipping a sajdah verse when reciting a surah? The text states it is makruh.
2
Understand the rationale
Why is it makruh? Because it resembles disdain (istinkaf) for prostration.
Istinkaf is a blameworthy trait.
3
Note the exception
Is it also makruh to recite only the sajdah verse? No, it is not disliked because it is mubadara (hastening to obedience).
4
List the recommendations
What are the recommended actions? Adding at least one verse to the sajdah verse, concealing the recitation from unprepared listeners, standing if sitting, and not raising the head before the reciter.
These are mandub, not obligatory.
5
Clarify the nature of following
How does the listener follow the reciter? It is not real iqtida, so no need for rows or stepping forward.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكره أن يقرأ سورة ويدع آية السجدة منها لأنه يشبه الاستنكاف عنها ولا يكره أن هو يفرد آية السجدة بالقراءة لأنه مبادرة إليها ولكن ندب ضم آية أو ضم أكثر من آية إليها أي إلى آية السجدة لدفع توهم التفضيل وندب إخفاؤها يعني استحب المشايخ إخفاءها عن غير متأهب لها شفقة على السامعين إن لم يتهيؤا لها وندب القيام لمن تلا جالساً ثم السجود لها روي ذلك عن عائشة رضي الله عنها وندب أن لا يرفع السامع تلاوتها رأسه منها أي السجدة قبل رفع رأس تاليها لأنها الأصل في إيجابها فيتبع في أدائها، وليس هو حقيقة اقتداء، ولذا لا يؤمر التالي بالتقدم ولا يؤمر السامعون بالاصطفاف فيسجدون معه حيث كانوا وكيف كانوا قاله شيخ الإسلام
And it is disliked to recite a surah and omit the sajdah verse from it because it resembles disdain for it. And it is not disliked that one recites the sajdah verse alone because it is a hastening towards it. But it is recommended to join a verse or more than a verse to it, i.e. to the sajdah verse, to repel the presumption of preference. And it is recommended to conceal it, meaning the mashayikh recommended concealing it from those not prepared for it out of compassion for the listeners if they are not ready for it. And it is recommended for one who recited while sitting to stand then prostrate for it; that was reported from Aisha, may Allah be pleased with her. And it is recommended that the listener of its recitation does not raise his head from it, i.e. from the prostration, before the raising of the head of the reciter, because he (the reciter) is the origin in its obligation, so he (the listener) follows in its performance, and it is not real following. Therefore the reciter is not commanded to go forward, nor are the listeners commanded to line up, but they prostrate with him wherever they are and however they are, said by Shaykh al-Islam.
Source pages p. 497

Commentary
This passage discusses several adab (etiquettes) related to sajdat al-tilawah. First, it is makruh tahriman (prohibitively disliked) to recite a surah that contains a sajdah verse but intentionally skip that verse, because it resembles disdain for the prostration. However, it is not disliked to recite the sajdah verse alone (without other verses), as that is a direct hastening to the act. But it is recommended (mandub) to add at least one or more verses to the sajdah verse to avoid giving the impression that the sajdah verse is superior to others, since all Quranic verses are equally the word of Allah. Next, it is recommended to conceal the recitation of the sajdah verse from listeners who are not prepared to perform sajdah (e.g., due to impurity or lack of readiness), out of compassion. Then, if the reciter was sitting, he should stand for the sajdah. This is based on a report from Aisha. Finally, the listener should not raise his head from prostration before the reciter raises his head, because the reciter is the original cause of obligation and the listener follows him. However, this is not a formal imam-follower relationship (iqtida), so the reciter need not step forward, nor do listeners need to form rows; they prostrate wherever they are.

Key Terms
الاستنكاف (al-istinkāf): Disdain or arrogance; skipping the sajdah verse resembles arrogance towards prostration to Allah.
المبادرة (al-mubādara): Hastening to perform the sajdah by reciting only the sajdah verse.
الاقتداء (al-iqtidā'): Following the imam in prayer; here it is not true iqtida because there is no takbirat al-ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) To make the recitation longer.
B) To avoid giving the impression that the sajdah verse is superior to other verses.
C) Because it is mandatory to recite at least two verses.
D) To allow listeners time to prepare for sajdah.

Key Takeaway
Skipping a sajdah verse is makruh due to resemblance to disdain; reciting it alone is recommended as hastening; listeners follow the reciter without formal congregation.

Conditions and Manner of Sajdat al-Tilawah
Conditions and manner of sajdat al-tilawah, including refinement on takbirs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five conditions for valid sajdat al-tilawah, describe its prescribed manner, and explain why the two takbirs are sunnah not wajib according to the corrected Hanafi position.

Core Idea
Sajdat al-tilawah shares prayer's conditions except takbirat al-ihram; it is one sajdah between two sunnah takbirs, no tashahhud or taslim.

The sajdat al-tilawah is a distinct worship triggered by reciting or hearing a prostration verse. While sharing many conditions with formal prayer, it is simpler. This lesson unpacks its validity conditions and precise manner, including a key intra-Hanafi refinement on the status of the accompanying takbirs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the shurut (conditions)
List the five conditions: taharah from hadath and khabath, covering awrah, facing qibla (with effort if confused), and intention. Note that takbirat al-ihram is explicitly excluded.
The conditions mirror those of prayer, but without the opening takbir.
2
Understand the recommendation for delay
If the sajdah cannot be performed immediately, the reciter or listener is recommended to say the specified du'a and then make up the sajdah later.
This ensures the obligation is not missed.
3
Describe the kayfiyya (manner)
The sajdah is one prostration between two takbirs: one for going down and one for raising. These takbirs are sunnah, not wajib, according to the corrected view (al-Bada'i').
No raising of hands, no tashahhud, no taslim.
4
Recognize the intra-Hanafi refinement
Some earlier texts considered the takbirs as rukn, but the later correction (by Fakhr al-Islam and in al-Bada'i') establishes them as sunnah. This is the mufta bihi position.
This refinement is an example of tarjih within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وشرط لصحتها أن تكون شرائط الصلاة موجودة في الساجد الطهارة من الحدث والخبث وستر العورة، واستقبال القبلة وتحريها عند الاشتباه والنية إلا التحريمة فلا تشترط لأن التكبير سنة فيها، وفي التتارخانية عن الحجة، ويستحب للتالي أو السامع إذا لم يمكنه السجود أن يقول سمعنا وأطعنا غفرانك ربنا وإليك المصير انتهى يعني ثم يقضيها وكيفيتها أن يسجد سجدة واحدة كائنة بين تكبيرتين تكبيرة للوضع، وتكبيرة للرفع هما سنتان كذا قال في مبسوط فخر الإسلام التكبير ليس بواجب وصححه في البدائع بلا رفع يد إذ لا تحريم لها والتكبير للإنحطاط ولا تشهد لعدم وروده ولا تسليم لأنه يستدعي سبق التحريمة منعدمة وتسبيحها مثل الصلاتية سبحان ربي الأعلى ثلاثاً وهو الأصح
And a condition for its validity is that the conditions of prayer exist in the prostrator: purity from hadath and khabath, covering the awrah, facing the qibla and searching for it in case of confusion, and intention, except takbirat al-ihram, for it is not a condition because the takbir is sunnah in it. In al-Tatarkhaniyya from al-Hujja: It is recommended for the recieter or listener, if he cannot prostrate, to say: 'We have heard and obeyed, Your forgiveness, our Lord, and to You is the return.' End. Meaning he should then make it up. And its manner is that he prostrates one prostration between two takbirs: a takbir for placing (the forehead) and a takbir for raising; both are sunnah. Thus said in Mabsoot of Fakhr al-Islam: The takbir is not obligatory, and it was corrected in al-Bada'i'. Without raising hands, since there is no tahreem for it, and the takbir is for bending down. No tashahhud because it has not been transmitted. No taslim because it requires preceding takbirat al-ihram, which is absent. And its tasbih is like that of prayer: 'Subhana Rabbiya al-A'la' three times, and this is the most sound.
Source pages p. 498

Commentary
This passage details the conditions (shurut) and manner (kayfiyya) of sajdat al-tilawah. The conditions for validity are the same as for prayer: purity from hadath (ritual impurity) and khabath (physical impurity), covering the 'awrah, facing the qibla (with effort if direction is unclear), and intention (niyya). However, takbirat al-ihram is not a condition; it is only sunnah. If one needs to delay the sajdah, it is recommended to say, 'We have heard and obeyed, Your forgiveness...' and then later perform it. The manner is one prostration between two takbirs: one takbir for going down (takbir al-wad') and one for raising (takbir al-raf'). These two takbirs are sunnah, not wajib, as per the stronger view in al-Bada'i'. One does not raise the hands because there is no tahrim (prohibition to begin). There is no tashahhud because it has not been transmitted from the Prophet, and no taslim because taslim requires a preceding tahrim. The tasbih during sajdah is the same as in prayer: 'Subhana Rabbiya al-A'la' three times, which is the most sound opinion.

Key Terms
التحريمة (al-taḥrīma): The initial takbir that prohibits worldly actions in prayer. Not required for sajdat al-tilawah.
التكبير للإنحطاط (al-takbīr lil-inḥiṭāṭ): The takbir said when bowing down to prostrate, sunnah in sajdat al-tilawah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) They are sunnah and not obligatory.
C) They are rukn and invalidate the sajdah if omitted.
D) They are recommended only for the reciter, not the listener.

Key Takeaway
Sajdat al-tilawah is a wajib act triggered by sajdah verses, valid only with the five conditions (except tahrima), and performed as a single prostration between two sunnah takbirs with no tashahhud or taslim.

Conditions and Invalidators of Sajdat al-Tilawah
Ruling on conditions and invalidators of sajdat al-tilawah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the required conditions for sajdat al-tilawah, explain why the Hanafi school does not require takbirat al-ihram, and identify the practical consequence of the intra-Hanafi disagreement on its completion.

Core Idea
Sajdat al-tilawah requires all conditions of prayer except the opening takbir; its validity hinges on when it is considered complete.

In this lesson, we explore the rulings surrounding sajdat al-tilawah (prostration of recitation). The text from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi clarifies the recommended etiquette for the listener, the necessary conditions for validity, and a key intra-Hanafi disagreement about what constitutes completion of the prostration. Understanding these details ensures that your prostration is performed correctly and any potential invalidators are avoided.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended etiquette for the listener
The passage states that it is recommended for the listener not to raise his head before the reciter and not to precede him in placing the forehead. Understand that this is a matter of adab (etiquette) and not a condition.
2
List the conditions required for sajdat al-tilawah
The text enumerates conditions: taharah from hadath and najasah, covering the 'awrah, facing the qiblah, and attempting to determine it if unclear. Note that intention is also required, but specific intention (ta'yin) is not needed. Crucially, takbirat al-ihram is not required.
The condition of facing the qiblah applies even if the prostrator is ahead of the reciter.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi disagreement on completion
According to Imam Muhammad, the prostration is not complete until the head is raised; therefore, if an invalidator (like speech or laughter) occurs before raising, the prostration must be repeated. Imam Abu Yusuf holds that the prostration is complete upon placing the forehead, so no repetition is needed. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) view is that of Muhammad.
This disagreement affects whether the invalidators of prayer apply during the lowering and raising phases.
4
Determine the effect of invalidators
The text states that the prostration is invalidated by deliberate impurity, speech, and loud laughter. If such an invalidator occurs, one must repeat the prostration. If impurity precedes, one can perform wudu and resume from where they left off, analogous to the prostration in prayer.
This ruling is based on Muhammad's view that the prostration continues until the head is raised.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وندب أن لا يرفع السامع الخ) وكذا يستحب أن لا يسبقوه بالوضع كذا في الشرح قوله: (ولذا لا يؤمر التالي الخ) هذا يخالف ما في الشرح عن النوازل أنه يتقدم، ويصطف الناس خلفه اهـ إلا أن يقال هذا على وجه الندب، ونفي الأمر منصب على السنة المؤكدة، وذكر في الدراية أن المرأة تصلح إماماً للرجل فيها اهـ لأنها إمامة صورية لا حقيقة . قوله : ( حيث كانوا) ولو متقدمين عليه . قوله: (وكيف كانوا أي على أي صفة كانوا قوله : (والنية) أي نية أن هذا السجود للتلاوة، وأما نية التعيين فلا تشترط ، وقالوا إنها تفسد بمفسدات الصلاة من نحو حدث عمد، وكلام، وقهقهة فعليه إعادتها، وفي سبق حدث يتوضأ، ويبني كما لو وجدت هذه الأشياء في سجدة الصلاة، ولا يخفي أن هذا كله على قول محمد لأن العبرة لتمام الركن، وهو إنما يحصل عنده بالرفع، ولم يوجد بعد، وهو الأصح على ما مر، ولا يتصور شيء من ذلك عند أبي يوسف، لأن السجدة قد تمت عنده بمجرد الوضع فينبغي أن لا تفسد على قوله كذا في الحلبي، وابن أمير حاج قال في الشرح، وقد يقال : الرفع، وإن لم يكن من تمامها، فما دام في الوضع، فهو فيها كمن أطال القراءة والقيام وهو في الفرض، فإذا قهقه أو عمل المنافي حصل في حقيقة السجود فبطل الجزء الملاقي له فيبطل الكل ببطلانه انتهى . قوله: (ويستحب للتالي أو السامع الخ) تحصيلاً للإمتثال بالقدر الممكن قوله : ( وصححه في البدائع) مقابله رواية الحسن عن الإمام الركن في السجدة وضع الجبهة، والتكبير عند الرفع حتى لو تركه يعيد.
His statement: (And it is recommended that the listener does not raise his head, etc.) And similarly it is recommended that they do not precede him in placing [the forehead] – as in the Sharh. His statement: (And therefore the reciter is not commanded, etc.) This contradicts what is in the Sharh from al-Nawazil that he advances and people line up behind him – unless it is said that this is on a recommendatory basis, and the negation of command refers to the emphasized sunnah. It is mentioned in al-Diraya that a woman suffices as imam for a man therein because it is a formal imamate, not a real one. His statement: (wherever they are) even if they are ahead of him. His statement: (and however they are) i.e., in whatever condition. His statement: (and intention) i.e., intention that this prostration is for recitation; specific intention is not required. They said that it is invalidated by the invalidators of prayer such as deliberate impurity, speech, and loud laughter – so he must repeat it. And if impurity occurs before, he performs wudu and builds upon it, as if these things occurred in the prostration of prayer. And it is not hidden that all this is according to Muhammad's saying because consideration is given to the completion of the pillar, which according to him is achieved by raising [the head], and it has not yet occurred – and this is the most correct as previously mentioned. None of this is conceivable according to Abu Yusuf because the prostration is completed with him by merely placing [the forehead], so it should not be invalidated according to his saying – as in al-Halabi and Ibn Amir Hajj. He said in the Sharh: It may be said: raising, even if it is not part of its completion, as long as one is in the placement, it is like one who prolongs the recitation and standing in the obligatory prayer – so if he laughs loudly or does something contrary, it occurs in the reality of prostration, so the part it touches becomes invalid, and the whole becomes invalid due to its invalidity – end. His statement: (and it is recommended for the reciter or listener, etc.) to achieve compliance as much as possible. His statement: (and he corrected it in al-Bada'i') its opposite is the narration of al-Hasan from the Imam that the pillar in prostration is placing the forehead and the takbir upon raising – even if one omits it, he repeats.
Source pages p. 498

Commentary
This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi is a critical refinement of rulings related to sajdat al-tilawah. It addresses the etiquette for the listener: it is recommended not to raise his head before the reciter lifts his, and also not to precede him in placing the forehead. The commentator notes a seeming contradiction with a narration from al-Nawazil that the reciter should stand in front and the listeners line up behind him, but resolves it by explaining that the command to not raise the head is on the level of a recommended act, while the negation of commanding the reciter to advance refers to the emphasized sunnah. A point from al-Diraya is mentioned: a woman can act as imam for men in this prostration because it is a formal imamate, not a real one. The conditions for validity are then detailed: the prostrator must have the conditions of prayer (taharah from hadath and najasah, covering the 'awrah, facing the qiblah, attempting to determine it if unclear, and intention), except for takbirat al-ihram which is not required. The passage discusses the effect of invalidators: according to Imam Muhammad, the prostration is not complete until the head is raised, so if an invalidator occurs during the prostration, it must be repeated; but according to Abu Yusuf, the prostration is complete upon placing the forehead, so it is not invalidated. The most correct view is that of Muhammad. It is recommended for the reciter or listener who cannot prostrate immediately to say 'We hear and obey, Your forgiveness, our Lord, and to You is the return' and then make it up later. Finally, it mentions that al-Bada'i' corrects that the takbir is sunnah, not wajib, contrary to a narration from al-Hasan ibn Ziyad.

Key Terms
سجدة التلاوة (sajdat al-tilawah): The prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a verse of prostration (ayat al-sajdah) in the Quran.
التحريمة (al-tahrimah): The opening takbir (takbirat al-ihram) that initiates the prayer; not required for sajdat al-tilawah.
الركن (al-rukn): The essential part of an act; without it, the act is void. In sajdat al-tilawah, according to the relied-upon view, the rukn involves both placing and raising the head.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi relied-upon view, which of the following invalidates sajdat al-tilawah?
A) Forgetting to have the intention
B) Sneezing before placing the forehead
C) Speaking deliberately before raising the head
D) Facing slightly away from the exact qiblah direction

Key Takeaway
Sajdat al-tilawah requires the conditions of prayer (except takbirat al-ihram), and according to the relied-upon Hanafi position, it is invalidated by speech and other invalidators occurring before raising the head.

Method of Sajdat al-Tilawah in the Hanafi School
Description of the manner of performing the prostration of recitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the correct Hanafi method of performing sajdat al-tilawah and distinguish between what is sunnah and what is not required (like tashahhud and taslim).

Core Idea
Sajdat al-tilawah is a single prostration between two sunnah takbirs, without tashahhud or taslim.

This lesson details the practical method of sajdat al-tilawah as established in the Hanafi school. It clarifies which actions are sunnah (the two takbirs) and which are absent (tashahhud, taslim). The ruling is based on transmitted practice and serves as a refinement against incorrect additions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core act
Sajdat al-tilawah consists of a single prostration (sajdah). It is not a full prayer unit.
2
Understand the placement of takbirs
The prostration is performed between two takbirs: one when going down (takbirat al-wad') and one when coming up (takbirat al-raf'). Both are sunnah, not wajib.
This is the most correct Hanafi view, as corrected in al-Bada'i'.
3
Recognize what is not included
No hand raising (raf' al-yadayn), no tashahhud, and no taslim (salam) are performed, as these require a preceding takbirat al-ihram, which is absent.
4
Note the recommended acts
The tasbih (glorification) recited is 'Subhana Rabbi al-A'la' three times, the same as in prayer. It is recommended to stand up after the prostration and to be brief, even if performing multiple prostrations.
Al-Kamal (Ibn al-Humam) noted that this prostration fulfills the 'falling down' praised in Quranic verses.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكيفيتها أن يسجد سجدة واحدة كائنة بين تكبيرتين تكبيرة للوضع، وتكبيرة للرفع هما سنتان كذا قال في مبسوط فخر الإسلام التكبير ليس بواجب وصححه في البدائع (بلا رفع يد) إذ لا تحريم لها والتكبير للإنحطاط ولا تشهد لعدم وروده (ولا) تسليم لأنه يستدعي سبق التحريمة، منعدمة وتسبيحها مثل الصلاتية سبحان ربي الأعلى ثلاثاً وهو الأصح، وقال الكمال: وهي لأن الخرور الذي مدح به أولئك فيه أكمل، وفي السيد، ويندب أن يقوم، ويخرسا جداً، ولو كان عليه سجدات كثيرة، ويستحب إذا فرغ منها أن يقوم اهـ ملخصاً.
And its manner is that one prostrates a single prostration between two takbirs: a takbir for placing and a takbir for raising. Both are sunnah – as stated in Mabsut Fakhr al-Islam: the takbir is not obligatory, and he corrected it in al-Bada'i' (without raising hands) because there is no tahrimah for it, and the takbir is for bending down. And there is no tashahhud because it has not been narrated, and (no) taslim because it requires preceding takbirat al-ihram, which is absent. And its tasbih is like that of the prayer: 'Subhana Rabbi al-A'la' three times – this is the most correct. And al-Kamal said: It is because the prostration that is praised in those [verses] is more complete. And in al-Sayyid: It is recommended to stand up and be very brief, even if one has many prostrations. And it is recommended when one finishes them to stand up – summarized.
Source pages p. 498

Commentary
This passage details the practical method of performing sajdat al-tilawah. It consists of one prostration (sajdah) between two takbirs: one takbir when going down (takbirat al-wad') and one when coming up (takbirat al-raf'). Both takbirs are sunnah, not wajib, as confirmed in al-Bada'i'. The hands are not raised because there is no takbirat al-ihram in this prostration; the takbir is simply for the action of bending down. No tashahhud is recited because it was not transmitted from the Prophet (peace be upon him). No taslim (salam) is given because that would require a preceding tahrimah, which is absent. The tasbih (glorification) during the prostration is the same as in the prayer: 'Subhana Rabbi al-A'la' three times – this is the most correct view. Al-Kamal (Ibn al-Humam) remarked that the prostration is the 'falling down' (khurur) that is praised in verses like 'They fall down on their faces' (Quran 17:107). From al-Sayyid (probably one of the commentators), it is recommended to stand up after performing the prostration and not to prolong it, even if one has multiple prostrations to perform; upon finishing all, one stands up. This manner applies whether the prostration is performed during prayer or outside of it, though there are additional considerations for the former.

Key Terms
الخرور (al-khurur): The act of falling down in prostration, or the prostration itself.
التسبيح (al-tasbih): The glorification recited during prostration: 'Subhana Rabbi al-A'la' three times.
تحريمة (tahrimah): The opening takbir that prohibits what was previously permissible and commences the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many takbirs are recommended (sunnah) in sajdat al-tilawah according to the most correct Hanafi view as stated in the passage?
A) One takbir at the beginning
B) Two takbirs: one going down and one coming up
C) Four takbirs like funeral prayer
D) No takbir is required

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi method of sajdat al-tilawah is a single prostration with two sunnah takbirs, reciting the usual tasbih, without tashahhud or taslim, and it is recommended to stand and be brief.

Ruling on Sajdat al-Shukr and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Statement of ruling and intra-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the classical Hanafi ruling on sajdat al-shukr and explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding its permissibility.

Core Idea
Sajdat al-shukr is makruh according to Abu Hanifa, but Abu Yusuf and Muhammad allow it as mubah.

This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi presents the ruling on sajdat al-shukr (prostration of thankfulness). While the classical Hanafi position is that it is makruh (disliked), there is an intra-madhhab disagreement: Abu Hanifa's two principal students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, are reported to permit it. Understanding this ikhtilaf helps you appreciate how later Hanafi practice sometimes shifted toward permissibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main ruling
Read the opening sentence: 'sajdat al-shukr is makruh according to Abu Hanifa'. This is the primary hukm stated by al-Quduri.
The text attributes this view to Abu Hanifa explicitly.
2
Locate the evidence for Abu Hanifa's view
Al-Kamal (Ibn al-Humam) explains that acts less than a rak'ah are not qurbah (religious devotion) except where text specifies (sajdat al-tilawah). Hence sajdat al-shukr is not legislated as an act of worship.
This is the core argument: no general license for single prostrations as qurbah.
3
Note the ikhtilaf and its nuances
The text reports that Abu Yusuf and Muhammad allow it (mubah), and even a narration from Abu Hanifa could be interpreted as permissibility. The majority of Hanafis, however, adhere to the makruh view.
The dispute centers on whether sajdat al-shukr is a valid qurbah or not.
4
Analyze the alternative reasoning
Some suggest Abu Hanifa only negated obligation, not permissibility, due to the impossibility of counting blessings. Others say he considered a two-rak'ah prayer as the complete thankfulness, citing the Prophet's action at the Conquest of Makkah.
The hadith about prostrating when seeing an afflicted person is claimed to be abrogated.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
For a Hanafi today: following Abu Hanifa, one avoids sajdat al-shukr; following the Sahibayn, one may perform it without sin. The mufta bihi in later practice tends toward permissibility.
This ikhtilaf does not break the unity of the madhhab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل سجدة الشكر مكروهة عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله قاله القدوري : وقال الكمال وعند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف ما دون الركعة ليس بقربة شرعاً إلا في محل النص وهو سجدة التلاوة فلا يكون السجود في غيره قربة انتهى وعن محمد عن أبي حنيفة أنه كرهه وروي عن أبي حنيفة أنه قال: لأراه شيئاً ثم قيل : إنه لم يرد به نفي شرعيتها،قربة بل أراد نفي وجوبها شكر العدم إحصاء نعم الله تعالى فتكون مباحة، أو لا يراها شكراً تاماً وتمام الشكر في صلاة ركعتين كما فعل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يوم فتح مكة كذا في السير الكبير، وقال الأكثرون إنها ليست بقربة عنده، بل هي مكروهة لا يثاب عليها وما روي أنه عليه السلام كان يسجد إذا رأى مبتلى فهو منسوخ (وقالا) أي صلاة ذات ركوع وسجود ولذا لم يشرع في صلاة الجنازة قوله : (أن يقال ذلك) أي التسبيح في غير النفل أي في صلاة غير النفل، وهي صلاة الفرض لأنّ سجدة الصلاة أفضل من سجدة التلاوة، ويقال فيها ذلك قوله : (وفيه) أي في النقل وحكم خارج الصلاة كذلك قوله : (بحوله وقوته) زاد الحاكم فتبارك الله أحسن الخالقين، وصحح هذه الزيادة. قوله: (أو قوله اللهم اكتب) الذي رواه الترمذي من حديث ابن عباس : اللهم اجعلها لي عندك ذخراً، وأعظم لي بها أجراً وضع عني بها ،وزراً وتقبلها مني كما تقبلتها من داود ،اهـ، وقوله : هو بالنصف عطفاً على ما شاء قوله : ( وإن كان خارج الصلاة الخ لو قال المؤلف : وفيه، وخارج الصلاة يقول: ما شاء مما ورد لكان أخصر. قوله : (من ذلك المذكور من الدعاء، أو غيره والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم، وأستغفر الله العظيم.
Chapter: The prostration of thankfulness is disliked (makruh) according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him. Al-Quduri stated it. And al-Kamal said: According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, what is less than a rak'ah is not a religious act (qurbah) legislatively except in the place of the text, which is the prostration of recitation, so prostration in other than it is not an act of worship – end. And it is narrated from Muhammad from Abu Hanifa that he disliked it. And it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that he said: 'I see it as something.' Then it was said: He did not intend thereby to negate its legality as an act of worship, but rather he intended to negate its obligation due to the inability to count the blessings of Allah, so it is permissible (mubah). Or he did not consider it a complete thankfulness, and the complete thankfulness is in a prayer of two rak'ahs, as the Prophet (peace be upon him) did on the day of the conquest of Makkah – as in al-Siyar al-Kabir. And the majority said that it is not a religious act according to him, rather it is disliked, and one is not rewarded for it. And what is narrated that he (peace be upon him) used to prostrate when seeing an afflicted person is abrogated. And they (the two) said: i.e., a prayer with bowing and prostration, and therefore it was not legislated in the funeral prayer. His statement: (that it should be said) i.e., the tasbih in other than supererogatory prayer, i.e., in prayer other than supererogatory, which is obligatory prayer, because the prostration of prayer is superior to the prostration of recitation, and it is said therein. His statement: (and in it) i.e., in the transmitted [prayer] and the ruling outside prayer is similar. His statement: (by His power and strength) – al-Hakim added: 'So blessed is Allah, the best of creators,' and he authenticated this addition. His statement: (or his saying: O Allah, write...) which al-Tirmidhi narrated from the hadith of Ibn 'Abbas: 'O Allah, make it for me a treasure with You, and increase for me thereby reward, and remove from me thereby burden, and accept it from me as You accepted it from Your servant Dawud.' His statement: 'or whatever he wishes' – meaning reciting other supplications. His statement: (and if outside prayer...) – the author could have been more concise by saying: 'in it and outside prayer, he says whatever he wishes from what has been narrated.' His statement: (from that mentioned of supplication or other) – and Allah knows best, and I seek forgiveness from Allah the Mighty.
Source pages p. 499

Commentary
This section begins the discussion on sajdat al-shukr (prostration of thankfulness). The primary ruling is that it is makruh (disliked) according to Imam Abu Hanifa, as quoted by al-Quduri. Al-Kamal (Ibn al-Humam) explains that according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, any act less than a rak'ah (like a single prostration) is not legislated as a devotion (qurbah) except in explicitly specified cases, i.e., sajdat al-tilawah. Therefore, sajdat al-shukr is not considered an act of worship; it is either mubah (permissible) or makruh. A narration from Abu Hanifa states he 'saw it as something,' but this is interpreted as negating obligation due to the impossibility of counting Allah's blessings, not negating its permissibility. The majority of Hanafi scholars hold that it is makruh and not rewarded. The argument against it includes that complete thankfulness is expressed through a two-rak'ah prayer, as the Prophet did at the Conquest of Makkah, and that any hadith about prostrating upon seeing someone afflicted is abrogated. In contrast, Imam Muhammad (al-Shaybani) and Abu Yusuf are reported to allow it, as seen in later practice. The passage also includes a brief digression on supplications for sajdat al-tilawah when performed outside prayer, recommending various well-known du'as.

Key Terms
سجدة الشكر (sajdat al-shukr): The prostration performed to thank Allah upon receiving a blessing or deliverance from harm.
قربة (qurbah): An act of devotion that brings one closer to Allah; legally a recommended or supererogatory act that earns reward.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for Abu Hanifa's ruling that sajdat al-shukr is not a qurbah?
A) It is not mentioned in the Quran or Sunnah
B) Acts less than a rak'ah are not qurbah except where text specifies (sajdat al-tilawah)
C) It is only allowed in the Maliki school
D) It was abrogated by a later hadith

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has an internal difference on sajdat al-shukr: Abu Hanifa holds it makruh, while his students consider it permissible.
