Du'a in prostration for nafl and fard prayers
Commentary on the rule for tasbeeh in nafl vs fard sajdah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the permissible supplications in prostration during fard prayer versus nafl prayer, and state the Hanafi ruling for each.

Core Idea
In fard prayer, only the customary tasbeeh is recited; in nafl prayer, any transmitted du'a is allowed.

This lesson examines a key detail in prayer: what can be recited in prostration. The Hanafi school distinguishes between obligatory (fard) and supererogatory (nafl) prayers, allowing more flexibility in the latter. The source passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi expands on the matn's ruling, clarifying that in nafl, any transmitted supplication is permitted, while in fard, only the tasbeeh is sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act in question
The act is the recitation of supplications (dhikr/du'a) during the prostration of prayer.
2
State the ruling for fard prayer
In fard prayer, the worshipper should recite the customary tasbeeh ('Subhana rabbiyal a'la') and may not replace it with other supplications. This is sunnah muakkadah.
3
State the ruling for nafl prayer
In nafl prayer, one may say any supplication that has been transmitted from the Prophet (peace be upon him), such as the du'a from the hadith of Ibn Abbas.
4
Note the basis for nafl flexibility
The permissibility is inferred from general permission in the Sunnah, including specific hadiths like the one recorded by Tirmidhi.
5
Apply outside prayer
Outside prayer (e.g., prostration of recitation), the same flexibility applies: any transmitted supplication may be said.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ينبغي أن يقال ذلك في غير النفل، وفيه يقول ما شاء مما ورد كسجد للذي خلقه، وجهي وصوره وشق سمعه وبصره بحوله وقوته أو قوله : اللهم اكتب لي عندك بها أجراً وضع عني بها وزراً واجعلها لي عندك ذخراً وتقبلها مني كما تقبلتها من عبدك داود وإن كان الصلاة قال كل ما أثر ذلك . من سجدة الشكر مكروهة عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله قاله القدوري : وقال الكمال وعند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف ما دون الركعة ليس بقربة شرعاً إلا في محل النص وهو سجدة التلاوة فلا يكون السجود في غيره قربة انتهى وعن محمد عن أبي حنيفة أنه كرهه وروي عن أبي حنيفة أنه قال: لأراه شيئاً ثم قيل : إنه لم يرد به نفي شرعيتها قربة بل أراد نفي وجوبها شكر العدم إحصاء نعم الله تعالى فتكون مباحة، أو لا يراها شكراً تاماً وتمام الشكر في صلاة ركعتين كما فعل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يوم فتح مكة كذا في السير الكبير، وقال الأكثرون إنها ليست بقربة عنده، بل هي مكروهة لا يثاب عليها وما روي أنه عليه السلام كان يسجد إذا رأى مبتلى فهو منسوخ (وقالا) أي صلاة ذات ركوع وسجود ولذا لم يشرع في صلاة الجنازة قوله : (أن يقال ذلك) أي التسبيح في غير النفل أي في صلاة غير النفل، وهي صلاة الفرض لأنّ سجدة الصلاة أفضل من سجدة التلاوة، ويقال فيها ذلك قوله : (وفيه) أي في النفل وحكم خارج الصلاة كذلك قوله : (بحوله وقوته) زاد الحاكم فتبارك الله أحسن الخالقين، وصحح هذه الزيادة. قوله: (أو قوله اللهم اكتب) الذي رواه الترمذي من حديث ابن عباس : اللهم اجعلها لي عندك ذخراً، وأعظم لي بها أجراً وضع عني بها وزراً وتقبلها مني كما تقبلتها من داود، اهـ، وقوله : هو بالنصف عطفاً على ما شاء قوله : ( وإن كان خارج الصلاة الخ لو قال المؤلف : وفيه، وخارج الصلاة يقول: ما شاء مما ورد لكان أخصر. قوله : (من ذلك المذكور من الدعاء، أو غيره والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم، وأستغفر الله العظيم.
It is appropriate to say that in other than supererogatory prayer, and in it (supererogatory) he says whatever he wishes of what is transmitted, like 'I prostrate to the One who created it, my face and my form, and split open my hearing and sight by His power and strength' or the saying: 'O Allah, write for me with it a reward, and remove from me with it a burden, and make it for me a provision with You, and accept it from me as You accepted it from Your servant Dawud.' And if he is outside prayer, he says everything that has been transmitted. From the prostration of gratitude: it is disliked according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, al-Quduri said it. Al-Kamal said: According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, what is less than a rak'ah is not a legal act of worship except in the place of the text, which is the prostration of recitation, so prostration in other than that is not an act of worship. End. And from Muhammad from Abu Hanifa that he disliked it. And it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that he said: 'I consider it a thing' then it was said: He did not intend by it to negate its legitimacy as an act of worship, but rather intended to negate its obligation as gratitude for the inability to count Allah's blessings, so it is permissible. Or he does not consider it complete gratitude, and the complete gratitude is in a prayer of two rak'ahs as the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, did on the day of the conquest of Makkah. Thus in al-Siyar al-Kabir. And the majority said that it is not an act of worship with him, rather it is disliked and there is no reward for it. And what is narrated that the Prophet used to prostrate when he saw an afflicted person is abrogated. (And they two said) i.e., a prayer with bowing and prostration, and thus it is not prescribed in the funeral prayer. His saying: 'that it be said' i.e., the tasbeeh in other than supererogatory prayer, i.e., in non-supererogatory prayer, which is obligatory prayer, because the prostration of prayer is better than the prostration of recitation, and it is said in it. His saying: 'and in it' i.e., in supererogatory prayer, and the ruling outside prayer is likewise. His saying: 'by His power and strength' al-Hakim added 'so blessed be Allah, the best of creators' and authenticated this addition. His saying: 'or the saying: O Allah, write' which al-Tirmidhi narrated from the hadith of Ibn 'Abbas: 'O Allah, make it for me a provision with You, and magnify for me with it a reward, and remove from me with it a burden, and accept it from me as You accepted it from Dawud.' End. And his saying: 'is by half' as a coordination on 'whatever he wishes.' His saying: 'and if he is outside prayer, etc.' If the author said: 'and in it, and outside prayer, he says whatever he wishes of what is transmitted' it would be more concise. His saying: 'from that mentioned of supplication, or other than it. And Allah, exalted, knows best, and I seek forgiveness from Allah, the Magnificent.'
Source pages p. 499

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) explaining a ruling from the matn regarding the permissible phrases in prostration. The ruling distinguishes between obligatory (fard) and supererogatory (nafl) prayers. In obligatory prayer, the worshipper should recite the customary tasbeeh (subhana rabbiyal a'la) and may not replace it with other supplications, because the prostration of prayer is superior to the prostration of recitation. In supererogatory prayer, however, one may say any supplication that has been transmitted from the Prophet (peace be upon him), such as the dua of 'I prostrate to the One who created it...' or the dua from the hadith of Ibn Abbas. Outside of prayer, when prostrating for recitation or gratitude, one may also say any transmitted words. The commentator al-Tahtawi notes that the matn could have been more concise by stating the rule for inside and outside prayer together. The passage also briefly mentions the ruling on Sajdat al-Shukr, indicating it is disliked according to Abu Hanifa, but this is elaborated in the next section.

Key Terms
النفل (al-nafl): Supererogatory (voluntary) prayers beyond the obligatory ones.
سجدة التلاوة (sajdat al-tilawah): Prostration performed when reciting certain verses of the Quran.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on reciting 'subhana rabbiyal a'la' in the prostration of a fard prayer?
A) It is haram.
B) It is sunnah muakkadah.
C) It is wajib.
D) It is mubah.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, fard prayer prostration requires the customary tasbeeh, while nafl prayer allows any transmitted supplication.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Sajdat al-Shukr
Intra-Hanafi dispute with critical refinement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the intra-Hanafi dispute on Sajdat al-Shukr, identify the evidence for each position, and apply the mufta bihi ruling in practice.

Core Idea
Sajdat al-Shukr is disputed: Abu Hanifa says makruh, the Sahibayn say qurba; the mufta bihi is mustahabb for a cause.

This lesson explores an internal Hanafi disagreement on whether one should prostrate in gratitude for new blessings. Abu Hanifa viewed it as disliked due to the impossibility of counting blessings, while his two main disciples considered it a virtuous act. Later Hanafi authorities reconciled these views, leading to a nuanced recommended practice. Understanding this dispute clarifies how the school handles divergent opinions within its own ranks.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
Recognize that Sajdat al-Shukr is a prostration performed to thank Allah for a new blessing or the removal of a calamity. The core dispute is whether it is a disliked (makruh tanzihan) act or a rewarded act of worship (qurba).
The matn states it is disliked, reflecting Abu Hanifa's view.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and his dalil
Abu Hanifa holds it is makruh tanzihan. His evidence: blessings are countless, so if it were obligatory, it would be required every moment, which is an impossible obligation (taklif ma la yutaq).
This reasoning is based on qiyas and the principle of avoiding undue hardship.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and their dalil
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad consider it a qurba (act of worship) for which one receives reward. Their evidence: the practice of Abu Bakr, 'Umar, 'Ali, and the Prophet's own prostration when receiving good news (hadith from Abu Dawud).
They argue these actions are not abrogated and establish recommendation.
4
Note the later majority and the mufta bihi
The majority of later Hanafis (after the three imams) followed Abu Hanifa's dislike, but the mufta bihi in later authoritative sources (al-Durr, Ibn 'Abidin) is that it is mustahabb when there is a cause, though disliked after the fard prayer due to potential misunderstanding by the ignorant.
Thus the practical ruling: recommended with a cause, but avoid performing it immediately after obligatory prayers.
5
Apply the mufta bihi to a scenario
Example: A person receives news of a new job. It is mustahabb for them to perform Sajdat al-Shukr. However, if they do so right after Fajr prayer in the mosque, it is makruh because onlookers may mistakenly believe it is obligatory or a sunnah prayer.
This illustrates the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) of the dispute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل سجدة الشكر مكروهة أي تنزيهاً قوله : لعدم إحصاء نعم الله (تعالى) فلو وجبت لوجبت في كل لحظة لأن نعم الله تعالى على عباده متواترة مترادفة وفيه تكليف ما لا يطاق قوله : (وقال الأكثرون مقابل قوله : ثم لك: من صلى عليك صليت عليه ومن سلم عليك سلمت عليه وفي التتارخانية قال صاحب الحجة : عندي أن قول الإمام محمول على الإيجاب وقول محمد على الجواز والاستحباب فيعمل بهما لا . بكل نعمة سجدة شكراً كما قال أبو Section: The prostration of gratitude is disliked (disliked as tanzihan). His saying: 'Due to the inability to count the blessings of Allah.' So if it were obligatory, it would be obligatory at every moment because the blessings of Allah upon His servants are successive and continuous, and that entails an impossible obligation. His saying: 'And the majority said' as opposed to his saying: 'Then it was said that he did not intend' etc. His saying: 'So it is abrogated' is refuted by the actions of the great Companions after him (peace be upon him) such as the prostration of Abu Bakr at the conquest of al-Yamamah and the killing of Musaylimah, and the prostration of 'Umar at the conquest of al-Yarmuk, which is a valley in the region of Syria, and the prostration of 'Ali when he saw Dhu al-'Udhabah killed at the river. And it is narrated that he called upon Allah for an hour, then fell prostrate, and he did that three times and said: 'I asked my Lord and interceded for my community, and He gave me a third of my community, so I fell prostrate in gratitude to my Lord; then I raised my head and asked my Lord for my community, and He gave me a third of my community, so I fell prostrate in gratitude; then I raised my head and asked my Lord for my community, and He gave me the last third, so I fell prostrate to my Lord.' Narrated by Abu Dawud. His saying: 'It is an act of worship for which one receives reward, and the fatwa is upon it.' In al-Durr: 'And by it is issued fatwa.' And in Ibn Amir Hajj: 'And it is apparent, and how could it not be when there have come about it more than one hadith.' End. In al-Durr: 'Sajdat al-Shukr is recommended, fatwa is issued by it, but it is disliked after prayer because the ignorant think it is sunnah or obligatory, and every permissible act that leads to that is disliked.' End. His saying: 'He (the Prophet) would prostrate when something pleasing came to him, i.e., he witnessed it, like the head of Abu Jahl when it was brought to the Prophet and placed before him; he prostrated five times in gratitude.' His saying: 'or was informed of it,' i.e., without witnessing it, like his prostration when Jibril informed him that Allah says: 'Whoever sends blessings upon you, I send blessings upon him, and whoever greets you, I greet him.' In al-Tatarkhaniyyah, the author of al-Hujjah said: 'In my view, the statement of the Imam is interpreted as obligation, and the statement of Muhammad as permissibility and recommendation, and one acts upon both, but not for every blessing a prostration of gratitude as Abu Hanifa said, but it is permissible to prostrate the prostration of gratitude at a time of happiness for a blessing or recollection of a blessing, thanking for it by prostration, and that is not outside the bounds of recommendation.' In Furuq al-Ashbah: 'He said: Sajdat al-Shukr is permissible with the Imam, not obligatory, and that is the meaning of what is narrated that it is not legislated.' In the first principle of al-Ashbah: 'And the relied-upon view is that the disagreement is about its being sunnah, not about its permissibility.' End. In al-Hindiyyah: 'Its form is: one upon whom a clear blessing has newly come, or Allah blessed him with wealth, or a child, or he found a lost item, or a calamity was averted, or his sick person was cured, or an absent person arrived, it is recommended that he perform it like the prostration of recitation. But if he prostrates without cause, it is neither an act of worship nor disliked.' End. His saying: 'Important benefit' (from al-hamm meaning what one is concerned with, meaning one should pay attention to it, i.e., care for it). His saying: 'Every descent' (nazilah) meaning a state of descending, with the meaning of arrival, and al-nazlah means the cold (in the dictionary). His saying: 'Important' (muhimmah) meaning causing grief, which is sadness (in the dictionary). His saying: 'One should pay attention' — it would be better to mention it after his saying 'important benefit'. His saying: 'And it is that which was intended to be collected in the preceding when enumerating its places.'
Source pages p. 499

Commentary
This passage is a detailed critical refinement (hāshiya) on the ruling of Sajdat al-Shukr (prostration of gratitude). It presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa holds it to be makruh tanzihan (disliked as a matter of tanzih), while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (al-Shaybani) consider it a qurba (act of worship) for which one is rewarded. The text explains the reasoning behind Abu Hanifa's view: the blessings of Allah are innumerable, so if this prostration were obligatory, it would be required at every moment, which is an impossibility (taklif ma la yutaq). The majority of later Hanafi scholars (al-aktharun) also sided with the dislike. However, the text also cites strong evidence for the opposite view, including the practice of Abu Bakr, Umar, and Ali (may Allah be pleased with them), and a hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) prostrating in gratitude. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) according to later sources like al-Durr is that it is mustahabb (recommended) but disliked after prayer due to fear of innovation by ignorant people. The passage further clarifies that the prostration is permissible with a cause (like a new blessing) and that the ikhtilaf is only about its sunniyyah, not its jawaz (permissibility). The final part provides a 'fāʾidah muhimmah' (important benefit) emphasizing the need to pay attention to this prostration for every important matter.

Key Terms
سجدة الشكر (sajdat al-shukr): Prostration performed to thank Allah for a new blessing or removal of calamity.
قربة (qurba): An act of worship that brings one closer to Allah and for which reward is expected.
مكروهة تنزيهاً (makruh tanzihan): Disliked but not prohibited; avoiding it is better than doing it, but doing it is not sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling of Sajdat al-Shukr when performed for a specific new blessing?
A) It is wajib.
B) It is makruh tahriman and sinful.
C) It is mustahabb (recommended).
D) It is haram.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's operative ruling on Sajdat al-Shukr is that it is mustahabb for a cause, but avoidance after prayer is recommended to prevent misunderstanding.

The Prostration of Thanksgiving (Sajdat al-Shukr)
Ruling and details on the prostration of thanksgiving.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Sajdat al-Shukr, explain its evidence, and identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
Sajdat al-Shukr is mustahabb, not wajib — rewarding but not binding.

The prostration of thanksgiving is an act of devotion recommended upon receiving a blessing or good news. This lesson examines its legal status, evidence from the Sunnah, and the internal Hanafi discussion about whether it is merely permissible or meritorious.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is Sajdat al-Shukr? What hukm level does the text assign? The mufta bihi is mustahabb (sunnah ghayr muakkadah).
The text explicitly says 'mustahabb bihi yufta'.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof is cited? The hadith of Abu Bakr (RA) that the Prophet would prostrate upon receiving good news.
The hadith is reported by the six except al-Nasa'i.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith indicate recommendation and not obligation? The Prophet's action (fi'l) without a command indicates istihbab, not wujub.
In Hanafi usul, fi'l without command indicates desirability.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
What is the difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn? Abu Hanifa: ja'iz (permissible); Sahibayn: qurbah (rewarded act).
The text cites Muhammad and Abu Yusuf in one narration as considering it a qurbah.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Which position is relied upon for fatwa? Mustahabb, but disliked after prayer due to potential misconception.
Al-Tahtawi and later authorities confirm this.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

جمعها لهذه الفائدة، وتقريب الأمر مع حكم السجود رجاء فضل الله الكريم الودود (في مجلس واحد وسجد) بتلاوته (الكل) آية (منها) سجدة (كفاه الله تعالى (ما أهمه) من أمر دنياه وآخرته ونقله عنه أيضاً المحقق ابن الهمام وغيره من الشراح رحمهم الله .
Book of Prayer. Muhammad and Abu Yusuf in one of the two narrations from him: (It) i.e. the prostration of thanksgiving (is an act of devotion for which one is rewarded) because the six except al-Nasa'i narrated from Abu Bakr that the Prophet, if something pleasing came to him or he was given glad tidings, he would prostrate. (Its manner is that he says the takbir facing the qibla, prostrates, praises Allah, thanks Him, and glorifies Him, then raises his head with takbir) like the prostration of recitation, with its conditions. (An important benefit for repelling every important calamity) It is necessary to pay attention to learning it and teaching it. (He said) the Shaykh al-Imam Hafiz al-Haqq wa al-Millah wa al-Din Abdullah ibn Ahmad al-Nasafi in his book al-Kafi, a commentary on al-Wafi: Whoever recites all of the prostration verses—and they are those intended to be collected in what preceded...

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on the prostration of thanksgiving (sajdat al-shukr). It opens by stating that according to Muhammad and Abu Yusuf in one narration, it is an act of devotion (qurbah) rewarded, citing the hadith that the Prophet (peace be upon him) would prostrate when receiving good news. The text then describes its manner: like the prostration of recitation, with takbir, facing qibla, and glorifying Allah. It emphasizes the benefit of learning it to repel calamities. The passage then narrates historical instances of prostrations by the Companions, including the Prophet's three prostrations for intercession as reported by Abu Dawud. The commentary clarifies the fatwa position: it is mustahabb (recommended) but disliked after prayer due to ignorant people thinking it obligatory. It also notes the disput within the Hanafi school: Abu Hanifa considered it permissible but not obligatory, while Muhammad and Abu Yusuf in one view deem it a recommended good deed. The relied-upon position is that it is mustahabb. The conditions are that it should be done for a tangible blessing like wealth or recovery from illness, and if done without reason, it is neither a good deed nor disliked.

Key Terms
سجدة الشكر (sajdat al-shukr): A prostration performed upon receiving a blessing or good news, as an act of gratitude to Allah.
قربة (qurbah): An act that brings one closer to Allah and merits reward.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi (relied-upon ruling) in the Hanafi school, what is the legal status of Sajdat al-Shukr?
A) Wajib (obligatory)
B) Mustahabb (recommended)
C) Haram (forbidden)
D) Mubah (permissible only)

Key Takeaway
Sajdat al-Shukr is a recommended prostration of gratitude, not obligatory, and it is best performed outside of obligatory prayers to avoid misconception.

The Name, Virtues, and Special Hour of Friday
Introduction defining Friday's name and virtues.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi perspective on the etymology of Friday, enumerate its virtues, and state the two scholarly opinions on the special hour of acceptance.

Core Idea
Friday is the best day, named for gathering, and its blessings culminate in a special hour of answered prayer.

This passage opens the chapter on Friday prayer (Salat al-Jumu'ah) by delving into the meaning behind its name and highlighting its unparalleled virtues. It also discusses a well-known hadith about a special hour of acceptance, presenting the two most reliable opinions about its timing. Understanding these foundations enriches our appreciation of this weekly worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the etymology of 'Jumu'ah'
Note that the word is derived from 'ijtima'' (gathering). The passage gives several reasons for the name, with the strongest being that Adam was created on Friday.
The commentary clarifies that the opinion in Fath al-Bari is preferred.
2
List the virtues of Friday mentioned
Scan the passage for the list: it is the festival of believers, a day of increase in blessings, souls gather, graves are visited, the deceased is safe from punishment, Hell is not kindled, and it is the best day.
Also includes the recommendation to recite Surah al-Kahf.
3
Examine the hadith about the special hour
The text quotes a hadith: 'There is an hour on Friday when a Muslim servant asks Allah for something while praying, He will give it.'
This hadith is widely narrated and highlights the importance of supplication on Friday.
4
Analyze the two opinions on the special hour
Ibn Salam says it is the last hour of Friday. Another opinion says it is from the imam's emergence to the end of prayer. The passage states both are the most correct.
This reflects the Hanafi recognition of legitimate differences in non-binding matters.

سميت جمعة لاجتماع الناس فيها، وقيل: لأنّ كمال الخلائق جمع فيه، وقيل: لأن خلق آدم عليه السلام جمع فيه قال في فتح الباري: وهذا أصح الأقوال، وقيل: لأن أوّل اجتماع آدم وحواء عليهما السلام بالأرض كان فيه ، وقيل : لأن الله تعالى يجمع فيه بين العباد، والرحمة، ويقال له عيد المؤمنين ويوم المزيد لتزايد الخيرات فيه، وفيه تجتمع الأرواح وتزار القبور، ويأمن الميت من عذاب القبر ومن مات فيه أو في ليلته أمن منه، ولا تسجر فيه جهنم، وفيه يزور أهل الجنة ربهم عز وجل، وخص يومها بقراءة سور الكهف، وقال : طلعت فيه الشمس يوم الجمعة فيه خلق آدم، وفيه أهبط، وفيه تيب عليه، وفيه مات، وفيه تقوم الساعة، وما من دابة إلا وهي مصيخة : يوم الجمعة من حين تصبح حتى تطلع الشمس شفقاً . من الساعة إلا الجن والإنس، وفيه ساعة لا يصادفها عبد مسلم، وهو يصلي يسأل الله شيئاً إلا أعطاه إياه اهـ والمصيخة المنتظرة قال عبد الله بن سلام : الساعة المعلومة هي آخر ساعة . من يوم الجمعة قال أحمد: أكثر الأحاديث على قول ابن سلام وقيل : هي من وقت خروج الإمام إلى المنبر إلى فراغ الصلاة، وهذان القولان أصح الأقاويل فيها، وهي اخير يوم .
Chapter of Friday. It is from 'ijtima'' (gathering) with sukun on the meem, and the reciters (Qurra') add a dammah; in al-Misbah, damming the meem is a language. It was named Jumu'ah because people gather in it, and it is said because the perfection of creation was gathered in it, and it is said because the creation of Adam (peace be upon him) was gathered in it. Al-Fath al-Bari: This is the most correct saying. And it is said because the first meeting of Adam and Eve (peace be upon them) on earth was in it, and it is said because Allah the Exalted gathers the servants and mercy in it. It is called the festival of the believers and the day of increase because good deeds increase in it. In it souls gather, graves are visited, the deceased is safe from punishment, and whoever dies in it or its night is safe from it. Hell is not kindled in it. In it the people of Paradise visit their Lord, Exalted is He. It is specific to reciting Surat al-Kahf. And he said: The sun rose on Friday; in it Adam was created, in it he was sent down, in it repentance was accepted from him, in it he died, in it the Hour will be established. There is no creature except that it listens on Friday from morning until the sun rises in fear of the Hour, except jinn and humans. In it there is an hour during which if a Muslim servant asks Allah for something while praying, He will give it to him. (The listening creatures are waiting). Abdullah ibn Salam said: The known hour is the last hour of Friday. Ahmad said: Most hadiths support Ibn Salam's statement. And it is said: It is from the time the imam comes out to the minbar until the end of the prayer. These two opinions are the most correct among the sayings regarding it. And it is the best day.
Source pages p. 501

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on Friday prayer by explaining the etymology of the word 'Jumu'ah' and its various interpretations. It highlights that Friday is called Jumu'ah because of the gathering of people, or because the perfection of creation was gathered in it, or because Adam was created on that day. The commentator notes that the strongest opinion, as stated in Fath al-Bari, is that it is named for the creation of Adam. The passage then enumerates the virtues of Friday: it is the festival of believers, a day of increase in blessings, souls gather, graves are visited, and the deceased is safe from punishment. It is recommended (khus) to recite Surah al-Kahf. Additionally, the hadith about the special hour of acceptance is discussed: Ibn Salam says it is the last hour, while another opinion says it is from the imam's emergence to the end of prayer. The commentator concludes that these two are the most correct views. The day is described as the best day of the week.

Key Terms
الجمعة (al-jumu'ah): The name of Friday, derived from al-ijtima' (gathering), referring to the weekly gathering for the Friday prayer.
يوم المزيد (yawm al-mazid): An epithet for Friday meaning 'day of increase' because of the abundant blessings and rewards.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Friday is the best day of the week, named for gathering, and its blessings include a special hour of prayer acceptance, though its exact timing is not definitively fixed.

Virtue of Multiple Sajdah Āyāt in One Sitting
Describes virtue and ruling for multiple sajdah āyāt in one sitting.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling and preferred method for prostrating after multiple sajdah verses recited in one sitting, and explain the virtue of doing so.

Core Idea
For each sajdah āyah recited in one sitting, prostrate immediately after each verse; Allah suffices the one who does so.

This lesson examines a transmitted report regarding the immense virtue of reciting and prostrating for multiple Āyāt as-Sajdah in a single sitting. The passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi explains that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said that whoever does so will be sufficed by Allah in all worldly and religious concerns. The commentary also resolves the preferred method of performing the prostrations, emphasizing immediate prostration to avoid slight dislike and maintain the Quranic order.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its virtue
The passage describes reciting all (or multiple) verses of prostration (āyāt as-sajdah) in one sitting and prostrating after each. The virtue is that Allah suffices the person from all concerns of this world and the next.
The hadith is transmitted by Ibn al-Humam and others, indicating a strong basis in the Hanafi tradition.
2
Determine the ruling (hukm)
Based on the proof (dalil), the Hanafi position is that this act is mustahabb (recommended), not obligatory. The wording 'kafāhu Allah' indicates a promise of sufficiency, which implies encouragement but not compulsion.
The hadith is ahad (single-chain), so zanni al-thubut, hence the ruling is at the level of mustahabb.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on timing
There are two opinions: (1) recite the verse and then prostrate after each, or (2) recite all verses and then prostrate once. The commentary (al-Tahtawi) strongly prefers the first opinion (immediate prostration after each verse).
The objection of al-Kamāl that delaying prostration 'changes the Quranic order' is refuted by immediate prostration.
4
Identify the mufta bihi and tarjih basis
The relied-upon opinion is to prostrate immediately after reciting each verse. This avoids the slight dislike (karāhah tanzīhiyyah) of delaying, as mentioned in al-Durr.
Imam Tahtawi explicitly says 'the second opinion is preferable' based on removing karahah.
5
Apply the ruling in practice
When reciting multiple sajdah verses in one sitting, one should perform a separate sajdah immediately after each verse, with the appropriate intention and conditions (e.g., taharah, facing qiblah).
The conditions for sajdah tilawah (like wudu, covering awrah) are standard and apply here as well.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جمعها لهذه الفائدة، وتقريب الأمر مع حكم السجود رجاء فضل الله الكريم الودود (في مجلس واحد وسجد) بتلاوته (الكل) آية (منها) سجدة (كفاه الله تعالى (ما أهمه) من أمر دنياه وآخرته ونقله عنه أيضاً المحقق ابن الهمام وغيره من الشراح رحمهم الله . قوله: (لهذه الفائدة وهي دفع المهم. قوله : (وتقريب الأمر) عطف على اسم الإشارة. قوله : (مع حكم السجود) أي فيما تقدم، والظرف متعلق بقوله جمعها. قوله : (الودود) أي المحبوب أو المحب. قوله : ( وسجد بتلاوته لكل آية منها سجدة قال في الدر: وظاهره أنه يقرؤها أولاً، ثم يسجد، ويحتمل أن يسجد لكل بعد قراءتها اهـ قلت والثاني أولى لما تقدم أن تأخيرها مكروه تنزيهاً، ولدفع أشكال الكمال بأن فيه تغيير نظم القرآن لأن السجود يكون فاصلاً فتأمل. قوله : (ما أهمه) أي من الأمر الذي قصد السجود له ويحتمل التعميم والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم وأستغفر الله العظيم.
He gathered them for this benefit, and to make the matter easy along with the ruling of prostration, hoping for the bounty of Allah, the Generous, the Loving. (In one sitting and prostrated) by reciting (all) the verse (of) a prostration from them, Allah, may He be exalted, suffices him (from what concerns him) of the affairs of his world and his Hereafter. And it was also transmitted from him by the investigator Ibn al-Humam and other commentators, may Allah have mercy on them. He said: (for this benefit) meaning to repel what is important. He said: (and to make the matter easy) is a conjunction of the demonstrative pronoun. He said: (with the ruling of prostration) meaning in what has preceded, and the adverb is attached to his statement 'he gathered them'. He said: (the Loving) meaning the Beloved or the Lover. He said: (and prostrated by its recitation for every verse of prostration from them). He said in al-Durr: Its apparent meaning is that he recites it first, then prostrates, and it is possible that he prostrates for each after its recitation. I said: The second is preferable due to what has preceded that delaying it is slightly disliked (makruh tanzihan), and to repel the objection of al-Kamal that it changes the order of the Quran because prostration becomes an interruption, so reflect. Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from a transmitted report regarding the virtue of reciting multiple Āyāt as-Sajdah in one sitting. The matn states that whoever gathers all the verses of prostration (from a specific surah? or all in the Quran?) and recites them in one sitting, prostrating after each verse, Allah will suffice him from all worldly and Hereafter concerns. The commentary notes that it is preferable to prostrate immediately after reciting each verse, as delaying prostration is slightly disliked (makruh tanzihan) and avoids disrupting the Quranic order. The proof is transmitted from the investigator Ibn al-Humam and others.

Key Terms
سجدة (sajdah): A verse of the Quran that requires prostration upon recitation or hearing.
كفاه الله (kafāhu Allah): Allah suffices him, i.e., protects from anxieties and fulfills needs.

Reciting multiple sajdah verses and prostrating immediately after each in one sitting is a meritorious act with the promise of Allah's sufficiency.

Friday Prayer (Jumuʿah): Definition and Obligation
Defines Jumuʿah and establishes its obligation via Quran and Sunnah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of Jumuʿah, explain its obligation as fard 'ayn, and identify the primary Quranic proof for its obligation.

Core Idea
Friday prayer is an individual obligation on every eligible Muslim, established by the Quranic command to hasten to remembrance.

This passage from the chapter on Friday prayer introduces the term Jumuʿah, explores its linguistic roots and virtues, and firmly establishes its legal status. Understanding that Friday prayer is fard 'ayn — not merely recommended or communal — is essential for every Muslim who meets the conditions. The proof is drawn directly from the Quran, showing the strength of the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Understand the naming of Friday
Identify the various opinions on why the day is called Jumuʿah, all centering on the concept of gathering. Note that the author cites Fath al-Bari for the most correct opinion.
The name reflects the communal nature of the prayer.
2
Recognize the virtues of Friday
Review the hadith-based merits listed, such as being the best day, creation of Adam, and the special hour. This establishes the day's significance before addressing the ruling.
These virtues reinforce the importance of attending Friday prayer.
3
Identify the ruling and its evidence
Locate the explicit statement: 'Salat al-Jumuʿah is fard 'ayn by the Book and the Sunnah.' Then examine the Quranic verse (62:9) as the primary proof.
The imperative 'fās'aw' indicates obligation in Hanafi usul.
4
Analyze the Quranic argument
Understand how the verse obligates Friday prayer: the command to hasten to remembrance upon the call. The author explains that 'remembrance' includes the prayer and sermon, making the prayer itself obligatory.
The logical link: obligation to attend implies obligation of the act attended.
5
Note the consensus and linguistic refinements
The passage also clarifies pronunciations and historical naming, but the core takeaway is the uncontested obligation (muttafaq alayh) of Friday prayer among all schools.
No intra-Hanafi or inter-madhhab dispute on the obligation itself.

Chapter of Friday. It is named Friday (Jumuʿah) because people gather on it. It is said: because the completeness of creation was gathered on it. It is said: because the creation of Adam, peace be upon him, was gathered on it. He said in Fath al-Bari: And this is the most correct opinion. It is said: because the first meeting of Adam and Eve, peace be upon them, on earth was on it. It is said: because Allah, may He be exalted, gathers on it between His servants and mercy. It is called the festival of the believers and the Day of Increase for the increase of good deeds on it. On it souls gather, graves are visited, the deceased is safe from the punishment of the grave, and whoever dies on it or its night is safe from it. Hell is not kindled on it. On it the people of Paradise visit their Lord, may He be mighty and majestic. It is specified with reciting Surat al-Kahf on its day. He said: The sun rose on it. On Friday Adam was created, on it he was descended, on it his repentance was accepted, on it he died, on it the Hour will be established. There is no creature except that it is listening on Friday from when morning comes until the sun rises in fear of the Hour, except jinn and humans. On it there is an hour that no Muslim slave makes, while he is praying, asking Allah for anything except that He gives him it. End quote. Al-Musayyikhah means waiting. Abdullah ibn Salam said: The known hour is the last hour of Friday. Ahmad said: Most of the hadiths are on Ibn Salam's saying. It is said: It is from the time the imam comes out to the minbar until the completion of the prayer. These two sayings are the most correct sayings concerning it. And it is the best day. Friday prayer is an individual obligation by the Book and the Sunnah from a day that exceeds forty. The Prophet said: Indeed the day of Friday is the master of days and the greatest of them with Allah, greater than the Festival of Sacrifice and the Festival of Fitr. And he said: The promised day is the Day of Resurrection, the witnessed day is the Day of Arafah, and the witness is the day of Friday. Ibn al-Musayyib said: Friday is more beloved to Allah than supererogatory Hajj. Ibn Abbas narrated a marfuʿ hadith: Friday is the Hajj of the poor; in another narration: the Hajj of the needy. He said: (It is from gathering) and it is a verbal noun of 'ijtamaʿa'. He said: (with sukun of the mim) for the passive because faʿlah with sukun is for the passive like humzah, i.e., the day in which gathering happens, and with it al-Aʿmash recited. He said: (and the reciters vowelled it) meaning they vowelled the mim following the dammah of the jim. He said: (the language of Hijaz) which is the well-known eloquent language. He said: (and with fatha it is the language of Tamim) meaning the active participle, i.e., the gathering day like dahkah and humzah and lamzah for one who does a lot of that. Its ta is for exaggeration as in 'allamah, not for femininity, otherwise it would not describe the day. With it reading is like with sukun, and both are irregular recitations. Al-Zajjaj narrated kasr as in the commentaries of al-Bukhari, and Sharh al-Mishkat and al-Nahr, and he denied it because faʿlah with kasr is not from the Arabic patterns. Whoever says it with sukun makes its plural Jumuʿ, and whoever says it with dammah makes its plural Jumuʿat. It is without sukun a name for the day, and with sukun a name for the days of the week. Its first is Saturday, and the first of days is Sunday. There is disagreement about this naming despite agreement that it used to be called in the Jahiliyyah 'Arubah with fatha of the important 'ayn, dammah of the ra, and with a ba. Al-Zajjaj, al-Farra, Abu Ubayda, and Abu Umar said that the pure Arabs used to call Saturday Shiyar, Sunday Awwal, Monday Ahwan, Tuesday Jabbar, Wednesday Dubar, Thursday Mu'nis, and Friday 'Arubah, i.e., then they transferred them to those well-known names. Ibn Hazm asserted that it is an Islamic name and was not in the Jahiliyyah. It is reported that the people of Madinah prayed it before the Messenger of Allah arrived. That was because the Ansar said to the Jews: a day on which they gather every seven days, and likewise to the Christians: come, let us make a day on which we gather, remember Allah, pray, and thank Him. So they made it the day of 'Arubah, and it was the first Friday in Islam. As for the first Friday that the Messenger of Allah gathered for, it was in the mosque of Banu Salim ibn Awf; he gave a sermon and prayed in it. He said: ((by the Book) is His saying, Exalted: When the call is made for prayer on Friday, hasten to the remembrance of Allah and leave off trade (al-Jumuʿah/62). He ordered hastening to the remembrance of Allah conditional upon the call for prayer. The apparent meaning is that remembrance is the prayer, and it is possible it means the sermon. In either case, it indicates the obligation of Friday. The first is apparent, and the second is likewise because obligating hastening to the condition is a branch of obligating the conditional. Do you not see that whoever is not obligated to pray is not obligated to hasten to the sermon by consensus? And what is mentioned in the tafsir is that what is meant is both the sermon and the prayer, and that is more fitting because it applies to both together.
Source pages p. 501

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on Friday prayer defines the term Jumuʿah, discusses its linguistic origins, virtues, and then establishes its obligation. It begins by explaining why it is called Jumuʿah, giving several opinions and citing Fath al-Bari. Then it lists numerous virtues of Friday based on hadith. After that, it states the ruling: Salat al-Jumuʿah is fard 'ayn (individual obligation) by the Quran and Sunnah. The proof is the verse from Surat al-Jumuʿah (62:9) which commands hastening to the remembrance of Allah upon the call to prayer. The commentary explains that 'remembrance' refers to the Friday prayer or the sermon, and in either case it indicates the obligation of Friday prayer itself. It then discusses a point about the conditionality: one who is not obligated to pray is not obligated to attend the sermon by consensus. The passage also covers historical details about the naming and the first Friday prayer in Islam.

Key Terms
الجمعة (al-Jumuʿah): The day of Friday, or the Friday prayer itself. Derived from 'jam' (gathering).
فرض عين (farḍ 'ayn): An obligation that must be performed by every legally responsible individual, not a communal duty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary Quranic proof for the obligation of Friday prayer cited in this passage?
A) 'O you who believe, when the call is made for prayer on Friday, hasten to the remembrance of Allah and leave off trade'
B) 'Establish prayer and give zakah'
C) 'And perform the prayer at the two ends of the day'
D) 'And bow with those who bow'

Key Takeaway
Friday prayer is an individual obligation (fard 'ayn) on every eligible Muslim, as proven by the Quranic command in Surat al-Jumuʿah.

Proofs for the Obligation of Jumu'ah
Presents textual and rational evidence establishing Jumu'ah as an individual obligation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three proofs for Jumu'ah's obligation according to the Hanafi school and explain why the school holds it is fard 'ayn.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah is fard 'ayn – an individual obligation proven by Quran, consensus, and rational necessity.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi case for Jumu'ah as a personal obligation. We will examine the primary textual evidence from the Quran, the consensus of the Ummah, and a rational argument that underscores its binding nature. The commentary also addresses a dissenting view and distinguishes between mere negligence and contempt.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine the legal status of Jumu'ah according to the Hanafi school. It is ruled as fard 'ayn (individual obligation).
Fard 'ayn is the highest level of obligation; failure without excuse is a major sin.
2
Examine the Quranic proof
Locate the Quranic verse (62:9). Notice the imperative verb 'fas'aw' (hasten) and the prohibition of sale. Understand how the imperative and the prohibition of a normally permissible act indicate obligation.
The verse commands hastening to the remembrance of Allah at the call to prayer.
3
Analyze the consensus (ijma')
The text asserts that Muslims have unanimously agreed upon the obligation of Jumu'ah since the time of the Prophet. Note the exception (Ibn Kaj) which is dismissed as an error.
Ijma' is a definitive proof (qat'i) in Hanafi usul.
4
Understand the rational argument (ma'qul)
Follow the reasoning: Jumu'ah replaces Dhuhr, which is an obligation. It is not permissible to abandon an obligation except for a more emphatic one, so Jumu'ah must be more emphatic.
This is a qiyas type argument based on the replacement of Dhuhr.
5
Note the hadith warning and key distinction
The hadith in Ibn Majah threatens severe punishment for abandoning Jumu'ah. Important: distinguish between tahawun (negligence) and istikhfaf (contempt); only the latter is kufr.
The hadith also emphasizes attending even under an unjust ruler.

قوله : (بالكتاب) هو قوله تعالى : إذا نودي للصلاة من يوم الجمعة فاسعوا إلى ذكر الله وذروا البيع [الجمعة / ٦٢] رتب الأمر بالسعي إلى ذكر الله على النداء للصلاة والظاهر أنّ المراد بالذكر الصلاة، ويجوز أن يراد به الخطبة، وعلى كل تقدير يفيد افتراض الجمعة فالأول ظاهر، والثاني كذلك لأن افتراض السعي إلى الشرط فرع افتراض المشروط ألا ترى أن من لم تجب عليه الصلاة لم يجب عليه السعي إلى الخطبة بالإجماع، والمذكور في التفسير أنّ المراد الخطبة والصلاة جميعاً، وهو الأحق لصدقه عليهما معاً، ثم إن من هذا مقتضى الله تعالى أكد ذلك بتحريم مباح، وهو البيع وهو لا يكون إلا لأمر واجب كما هو الحكمة. قوله : في الحلبية. قوله : (ونوع من المعنى) أي ودليل من المعنى المعقول قال في الشرح : وأما المعنى فلانا أمرنا بترك الظهر لإقامة الجمعة والظهر فريضة، ولا يجوز ترك فرض إلا لفرض هو آكد، وأولى منه فدل على أن الجمعة أكد الظهر في الفريضة. قوله : (ذلك) أي لافتراضها بهذه الأدلة. قوله : (وقال عليه السلام) بيان للسنة قوله: (في حديث قاله في خطبة . قوله : ( في مقامي (هذا الذي في ابن ماجه، وغيره تقديم هذا على قوله في شهري هذا، وفيه بعد قوله : في شهري هذا زيادة، ولفظها فريضة واجبة إلى يوم القيامة فمن تركها جحوداً، واستخفافاً بحقها في حياتي، وبعد موتي، وله إمام عادل الخ. قوله تهاوناً بها أي كسلاً فالتهاون غير الاستخفاف وعبارة القاموس تفيد الإتحاد قوله : ( وله إمام عادل ، أو جائر) إنما ذكره ليفيد وجوب إقامتها مع الإمام الجائر، وأن جوره ليس عذراً مسقطاً لها، وإلا فالاستخفاف مكفر، وإن لم يكن إمام أصلاً. قوله: (فلا الله شمله) الشمل بالكسر والفتح العذق، أو القليل الحمل منه فشبه أمور الإنسان بالعذق جمع بجامع صدورها عن أصل واحد وأطلق عليها الشمل، وجمع الشمل كناية عن عدم تفرق أموره، واختلافها وانعكاسها قوله ولا قاموس أي لا يجعله قابلاً للخير، فهو كناية عن صرفه عن الخيرات. قوله : ( يجعله في أسفل درك جهنم) محمول على شدة العذاب، وإنما ذكر ذلك لأنه فعل فعل المنافقين حيث أقر بالوحدانية، وتوابعها، وترك الجمعة، والمنافقون في الدرك الأسفل من النار، أو محمول على من تركها جحد، أو مات على هذه العقيدة. قوله : أكد من الظهر قد علمت وجهه.
His statement: (by the Book) is His statement, Exalted: 'When the call is proclaimed for the prayer on the day of Jumu'ah, hasten to the remembrance of Allah and leave off trade' [Surah al-Jumu'ah 62:9]. He linked the command to hasten to the remembrance of Allah with the call to prayer. And the apparent meaning is that what is meant by 'remembrance' is the prayer, and it is possible that what is meant is the sermon. On either interpretation, it establishes the obligation of Jumu'ah. The first is apparent, and the second is also so because obligating the journey to the condition is subsidiary to obligating the conditioned. Do you not see that whoever is not obligated to pray is not obligated to come to the sermon by consensus. And what is mentioned in the exegesis is that what is meant is both the sermon and the prayer together, and that is more correct because it applies to both. Then from this... So the Exalted emphasized that by prohibiting what is permissible (sale), and that is only for an obligatory matter, as is the wisdom. His statement: (and by consensus) said in the commentary: The Muslims from the time of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) to our day have unanimously agreed on its obligation without anyone denying it, and it is an individual obligation (fard 'ayn) except according to Ibn Kaj, one of the followers of al-Shafi'i, who said it is a collective obligation (fard kifayah). But this is an error, as mentioned in al-Halabiyyah. His statement: (and a kind of rational meaning) meaning a proof from rational meaning. He said in the commentary: As for the rational, it is that we are commanded to leave Dhuhr to perform Jumu'ah, and Dhuhr is an obligation. And it is not permissible to leave an obligation except for an obligation that is more emphatic and more entitled. This indicates that Jumu'ah is more emphatic in obligation than Dhuhr. His statement: (that) i.e., for its obligation by these proofs. His statement: (and he, peace be upon him, said) is an explanation of the Sunnah. His statement: (in a hadith he said in a sermon). His statement: (in my station) which is in Ibn Majah and others, placed 'this' before 'my month', and after 'my month' there is an addition: 'an obligatory duty until the Day of Judgment. So whoever leaves it out of denial and contempt for its right in my life and after my death, and he has a just or unjust ruler...' His statement: 'out of negligence' i.e., laziness, so negligence is other than contempt. But the wording of al-Qamus suggests unity. His statement: 'and he has a just or unjust ruler' - he only mentioned that to imply the obligation of performing it under an unjust ruler, and that his injustice is not an excuse to exempt him. Otherwise, contempt is disbelief, even if there is no ruler at all. His statement: 'so may Allah not gather his affairs' - 'shamal' means a cluster of dates... He compared the affairs of a person to a cluster, and the gathering of the cluster is a metaphor for the coherence of his affairs. His statement: 'and not bless his matter' - in Ibn Majah: 'and not complete his matter.' His statement: 'verily, he has no prayer' i.e., complete prayer. The same is said for what follows if he does not deny or despise; otherwise, the statement is literal. His statement: 'Allah has sealed his heart' - satara, like 'khatama' (sealed), i.e., He does not make it receptive to good, so it is a metaphor for turning him away from good deeds. His statement: 'He places him in the lowest depths of Hell' - it is understood as severe punishment. He only mentioned that because he did the act of the hypocrites, as he affirmed tawhid and its consequences but left Jumu'ah, and the hypocrites are in the lowest depths of Hell. Or it is understood as referring to one who leaves it out of denial or dies on that belief. His statement: 'more emphatic than Dhuhr' - you have already learned its reason.
Source pages p. 502

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary (sharh) on the proofs for the obligation of Jumu'ah. The commentator addresses each proof: first, the Quranic verse (62:9) which commands hastening to the remembrance of Allah, which is interpreted as the prayer or sermon, both indicating obligation. He argues that even if interpreted as the sermon, its obligation is subsidiary to the prayer. Second, he notes the consensus (ijma') of Muslims, except for an aberrant view attributed to Ibn Kaj (Shafi'i) that it is fard kifayah, which he dismisses as error. Third, he presents a rational argument: since Jumu'ah replaces Dhuhr, and Dhuhr is obligatory, Jumu'ah must be more emphatic to justify the replacement. The commentator then explains a hadith about severe warnings for abandoning Jumu'ah, emphasizing that even under an unjust ruler one must attend. The commentary clarifies that negligence (tahawun) is different from contempt (istikhfaf), and that the latter is disbelief (kufr). The hadith about Allah sealing the heart is explained as a metaphor for being deprived of goodness, and the punishment in Hell is for those who abandon in denial or die on that belief. The overall message reinforces the paramount importance of Jumu'ah.

Key Terms
فرض عين (fard 'ayn): An obligation each individual must personally fulfill; cannot be fulfilled by others.
فرض كفاية (fard kifayah): An obligation on the community; if sufficient members perform it, others are absolved.
الاستخفاف (istikhfaf): Contempt or belittling of a religious command; considered kufr (disbelief) when directed at an agreed-upon obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Jumu'ah is fard 'ayn – an individual obligation proven by definitive Quranic command, unanimous consensus, and rational necessity.

The Seven Conditions for Jumu'ah to be Obligatory
Lists the first three of seven conditions for Jumu'ah obligation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the seven conditions for the obligation of Jumu'ah and explain why each is required.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah obligations require seven specific personal conditions beyond general prayer conditions.

The obligation of Jumu'ah prayer is not unconditional; it depends on several additional personal conditions beyond those of other prayers. In this lesson, we examine a passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi that begins to enumerate these seven conditions. Although the text is cut short, we will learn the complete list from the Hanafi school and understand the rationale behind each.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first condition: masculinity
The text states that women are excluded from the obligation. Determine why masculinity is a condition and what other prayers' obligation differs.
Women are exempt because Jumu'ah requires presence in congregation, and the burden is lifted due to domestic responsibilities. They may attend if they wish.
2
Identify the second condition: freedom
Slaves are exempt because their time belongs to their master. Consider how this relates to the requirement of ownership of time.
In the Hanafi school, a slave is not obligated to attend Jumu'ah; the master's right overrides.
3
Identify the third condition: residence (being a muqim)
Travellers are exempt from Jumu'ah. The text mentions al-iqamah. Understand the minimum travel distance and duration that triggers exemption.
The Hanafi standard for travel is typically three days journey (approx. 77 km or more).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (سبعة شرائط) اعلم أن لوجوبها شرائط زائدة على شرائط سائر الصلوات وهي في المصلي، ولصحتها شروط . والجمعة فرض أكد من الظهر (على) كل (من اجتمع فيه سبعة شرائط) وهي (الذكورة) خرج به النساء (والحرية) خرج به الأرقاء (والإقامة) خرج بـ
His statement: (seven conditions) - know that for its obligation there are conditions additional to the conditions of other prayers, and they are related to the person praying. And for its validity there are conditions. And Jumu'ah is a more emphatic obligation than Dhuhr upon everyone in whom seven conditions are combined: (1) masculinity - thereby women are excluded; (2) freedom - thereby slaves are excluded; (3) residence - thereby...
Source pages p. 503

Commentary
This passage begins the listing of the seven conditions (shurut) that must be present for Jumu'ah to become obligatory on an individual. The commentator notes that these are in addition to the general conditions of other prayers, and they relate to the person (fihi). He then starts enumerating: the first is masculinity, which excludes women; the second is freedom, which excludes slaves; the third is residence (i.e., being a muqim, not a traveler). The text ends abruptly during the third condition. In the Hanafi school, the full list of seven conditions for obligation is: (1) masculinity, (2) freedom, (3) residence (being a muqim), (4) good health (being free from illness that prevents attending), (5) being free from blindness, lameness, or similar severe hardship, (6) being male (already mentioned), (7) and being sane and adult (implied). But the text only mentions three.

Key Terms
الذكورة (al-dhukurah): The condition of being male; women are exempt from the obligation of Jumu'ah.
الحرية (al-hurriyah): Freedom as opposed to slavery; slaves are not obliged to attend Jumu'ah.
الإقامة (al-iqamah): Being a resident (muqim), not a traveler; travellers are exempt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Jumu'ah is obligatory only when seven specific conditions are met; any missing condition lifts the obligation.

Proving Jumu'ah's Obligation and Its Seven Conditions
Proofs and conditions for Jumu'ah obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the proofs for Jumu'ah being fard 'ayn, list its seven conditions of obligation, and distinguish between conditions of obligation and validity according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah is fard 'ayn on every eligible male resident in a city, backed by explicit hadith and ijma.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi clarifies the Hanafi position on Friday prayer, which is a central weekly obligation. You will learn the strong evidence that makes Jumu'ah a personal duty (fard 'ayn) and the precise conditions that determine who must attend. Understanding these distinctions will help you avoid common misconceptions about congregational responsibilities.

Guided Path
1
Identify the proofs for obligation
Locate the hadiths cited and the mention of ijma' and rational meaning (ma'na). Note how the explicit word 'farada' indicates obligation.
The first hadith is from the Farewell Sermon; the second threatens sealing of the heart for missing three Jumu'ahs.
2
Extract the seven conditions
From the text, list the seven conditions of obligation (shurut al-wujub): masculinity, freedom, residency, residing in a city (misr), health, sanity, adulthood. Note that the hadith 'except four' gives some of these.
The passage explicitly says 'seven conditions' and names the first four; the last three are inferred from the hadith.
3
Analyze the definition of misr
Understand that 'misr' means a large city with a judge and established Jumu'ah. Its outskirts (rabad) within a bowshot are included; those outside are not obligated even if they hear the call.
This is based on the practice of the Companions and the hadith 'no Jumu'ah except in a congregational city.'
4
Distinguish wujub conditions from valid conditions
The passage contrasts conditions for obligation (shurut al-wujub) and conditions for validity (shurut al-sihhah). Absence of a wujub condition means no obligation but the prayer if performed may still be valid; absence of a valid condition invalidates the prayer.
For example, a traveler is not obligated to attend Jumu'ah, but if he attends and prays, it is valid.
5
Evaluate the ikhtilaf with Ibn Kaj
Identify the Shafi'i view (Ibn Kaj) that Jumu'ah is fard kifayah. See how Al-Tahtawi refutes it, labeling it an error, and reaffirms the Hanafi position.
The practical difference: under fard 'ayn every individual sins for missing Jumu'ah; under fard kifayah the sin is collective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة والإجماع، ونوع من المعنى يكفر جاحدها لذلك وقال عليه السلام في حديث: واعلموا أن الله تعالى فرض عليكم الجمعة في يومي هذا في شهري هذا في مقامي هذا فمن تركها تهاوناً بها واستخفافاً بحقها وله إمام عادل أو جائر فلا جمع الله شمله ولا بارك له في أمره ألا فلا صلاة له ألا فلا زكاة له ألا فلا صوم له إلا أن يتوب فمن تاب تاب الله عليه. وقال: من ترك ثلاث جمع متواليات من غير عذر طبع الله على قلبه ومن يطبع الله على قلبه يجعله في أسفل درك جهنم والجمعة فرض أكد من الظهر على كل من اجتمع فيه سبعة شرائط وهي الذكورة خرج به النساء والحرية خرج به الأرقاء والإقامة خرج به المسافر وأن تكون الإقامة بمصر خرج به المقيم بقرية لقوله عليه السلام: "الجمعة حق واجب على كل مسلم في جماعة إلا أربعة مملوك أو امرأة أو صبي أو مريض" وفي البخاري أو مملوك أو مسافر ولقوله عليه السلام: "لا جمعة ولا تشريق ولا صلاة فطر ولا أضحى إلا في مصر جامع أو مدينة عظيمة" ولم ينقل عن الصحابة رضي الله عنهم أنهم حين فتحوا البلاد اشتغلوا بنصب المنابر والجمع إلا في الأمصار دون القرى ولو كان لنقل ولو آحاداً فلا بد من الإقامة بمصر أو فيما هو داخل في حد الإقامة بها أي بالمصر وهو المكان الذي من فارقه بنية السفر يصير مسافراً ومن وصل إليه يصير مقيماً في الأصح كربض المصر وفنائه الذي لم ينفصل عنه بغلوة كما تقدم ولا يجب على من كان خارجه ولو سمع النداء المصر سواء كان سواده قريباً من المصر أو من كذلك وهي في غير المصلي والفرق بينهما أنه بانتفاء الأول يصح الأداء وبانتفاء الثاني لا يصح
The book of prayer. And consensus, and a kind of rational meaning. The denier of it becomes a disbeliever because of that. And he (peace be upon him) said in a hadith: 'Know that Allah the Exalted has made Jumu'ah obligatory upon you on this day of mine, in this month of mine, in this place of mine. So whoever abandons it with negligence and disrespect for its right, having a just or unjust Imam, Allah will not gather his affairs, nor bless him in his matter. Indeed, no prayer for him, indeed no zakat for him, indeed no fast for him, unless he repents. And whoever repents, Allah turns to him.' And he said: 'Whoever abandons three consecutive Jumu'ahs without an excuse, Allah seals his heart, and whoever Allah seals his heart, He puts him in the lowest depth of Hell.' And Jumu'ah is a more emphasized obligation than Zuhr upon everyone in whom seven conditions are combined: masculinity (excluding women), freedom (excluding slaves), residency (excluding the traveler), and that the residency be in a city (excluding the resident of a village), due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'Jumu'ah is a right obligatory upon every Muslim in congregation except four: a slave, a woman, a boy, or a sick person.' And in al-Bukhari: 'or a slave or a traveler.' And due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'There is no Jumu'ah, no takbir al-tashriq, no Eid prayer, no sacrifice except in a congregational city or a great town.' And it has not been narrated from the Companions (may Allah be pleased with them) that when they conquered lands, they engaged in setting up pulpits and performing Jumu'ah except in cities, not in villages. And if it were narrated, it would be rare and by individuals. So residency in a city is necessary, or in what is within the limit of residency connected to it, that is, the city. It is the place from which when one departs with the intention of travel he becomes a traveler, and when one arrives he becomes a resident according to the most correct view, like the outskirts of the city and its courtyard which is not separated from it by a bowshot as previously mentioned. And it is not obligatory upon one who is outside it, even if he hears the call, whether his town is near the city or far. Likewise, these are conditions in the person praying, and for its validity there are conditions, and the difference between the two is that with the absence of the first, the performance is valid, and with the absence of the second, it is not.
Source pages p. 503

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya Al-Tahtawi is a critical refinement of Maraqi al-Falah, establishing the obligation of Jumu'ah prayer and its conditions. The commentary first presents the proofs of obligation: ijma' (consensus), rational proof (since Zuhr is abandoned for Jumu'ah, the latter must be more emphatic), and hadith. Two hadiths are cited: one from the Prophet's farewell sermon threatening those who neglect Jumu'ah with spiritual loss, and another stating that Allah seals the heart of one who misses three consecutive Jumu'ahs without excuse. These establish Jumu'ah as a fard 'ayn (personal obligation) — not fard kifayah, as Ibn Kaj (a Shafi'i scholar) erroneously held. The text then lists seven conditions for obligation: masculinity, freedom, residency, being in a city (misr), health, sanity, and adulthood (implied by the hadith 'except a boy'). The commentary explains the first four conditions: women, slaves, travelers, and villagers are exempt. It emphasizes that the city (misr) must be a large settlement where Jumu'ah was established by the Companions. The definition of misr includes its outskirts within a bowshot; those outside are not obliged even if they hear the call. Finally, the passage distinguishes between conditions for obligation (shurut al-wujub) and conditions for validity (shurut al-sihhah): absence of a wajib condition makes the prayer permissible but not compulsory, while absence of a sahih condition invalidates the prayer.

Key Terms
فرض عين (fard 'ayn): An obligation that must be performed by every individual who meets the conditions; not fulfilled by others doing it.
مصر (misr): A large city or town that has a judge (qadi) and where Jumu'ah was historically established; it is a condition for obligation.
شرائط الوجوب (shurut al-wujub): Conditions that must be present for an act to be obligatory. If absent, the act is not required but may be valid if performed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is NOT a condition for Jumu'ah to be obligatory?
A) Being male
B) Being free
C) Being a resident of a city (misr)
D) Being a traveler

Key Takeaway
Jumu'ah is fard 'ayn upon every eligible Muslim male resident in a city; those exempt include women, slaves, travelers, villagers, sick, minors, and the insane.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Shurut Wujub al-Jumu'ah: The Conditions for Friday Prayer Obligation
Conditions and exemptions for Jumu'ah prayer from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the seven conditions for Jumu'ah prayer obligation and explain the requirement of residence in a city (misr).

Core Idea
Jumu'ah is fard 'ayn only for the free, male, healthy, resident, sighted, able-bodied, and safe from oppression.

The obligation of Jumu'ah is established by the hadith and consensus, but it applies only to those who meet specific conditions. The passage from al-Tahtawi clarifies these conditions step by step, beginning with the requirement of living in a city (misr) and defining its boundary. In this lesson, we will walk through each condition and its evidence from the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the proof text
Start with the hadith: 'Jumu'ah is an obligatory right upon every Muslim in congregation except four...' This hadith is the primary evidence for both the obligation and the exemptions.
The hadith is ahad, but the obligation is established by consensus and continuous practice (tawatur 'amali).
2
Extract the basic conditions from the exemptions
The hadith exempts a slave, a woman, a boy, and a sick person. From these exemptions, we infer the conditions: free, male, adult, healthy. The traveler is added in another narration.
Conditions are derived from exemptions via the legal maxim: al-mutlaq bi al-muqayyad.
3
Understand the additional condition: residence in a city (misr)
The hadith 'No Jumu'ah except in a congregational city (misr jam')' establishes that the prayer is only valid in a city. The passage defines the city's boundary as the area from which leaving with travel intention makes one a traveler, measured by a ghalwah (about 400 cubits).
This definition is critical because it determines who must attend based on residence, not distance or call audibility.
4
Note the conditions from the commentary: safety and physical ability
The text adds two conditions: safety from an oppressor (aman min zalim) and soundness of legs (salamat al-rijlayn). These are based on the principle that hardship removes obligation. The insolvent fearing imprisonment is likened to one hiding from an oppressor.
Heavy rain is also an excuse, but it is classified as an 'udhr (excuse) rather than a condition.
5
Confirm the additional condition: soundness of eyes
The blind are exempted by Abu Hanifa; the two companions differ if a guide is available. This is a separate dispute, but the condition 'salamat al-'aynayn' is listed in the matn.
The mufta bihi view on the blind will be covered in the next lesson.

The book of prayer: The traveler and that residence (is in a city) excludes the resident in a village due to his saying peace be upon him: 'Friday is an obligatory right upon every Muslim in congregation except four: a slave, a woman, a boy, or a sick person.' And in al-Bukhari: 'or a slave or a traveler.' And due to his saying peace be upon him: 'No Friday, no tashreeq, no Fitr prayer, no Adha prayer except in a congregational city or a great town.' And it is not transmitted from the Companions that when they conquered lands they occupied themselves with setting up pulpits and gathering except in cities, not villages; and if it were, it would have been transmitted, even if by solitary reports. So residence in a city is necessary. Or residence in what is within the limit of residence in the city, which is the place where one who departs from it with the intention of travel becomes a traveler, and one who reaches it becomes a resident in the soundest view, like the outskirts of the city and its courtyard that is not separated from it by a ghalwah (bowshot) as previously mentioned. And it is not obligatory on one who is outside it even if he hears the call, whether his village is near the city or far in the soundest view, so one does not act on what is said contrary to it even if authenticated. And the fourth: health, excludes the sick due to what we narrated, and the old man who is weak is annexed to the sick. And the fifth: safety from an oppressor, so it is not obligatory on one who hides from an oppressor, and the insolvent who fears imprisonment is annexed to him, just as tayammum is permitted for him. And the sixth: soundness of the eyes, so it is not obligatory on the blind according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) if he finds a guide—this is the issue of one capable through another's capability. And the seventh: soundness of the legs, so it is not obligatory on the lame due to his inability to walk, by agreement. And among excuses is heavy rain. As for puberty and intellect, they are not one. His saying: 'And it is not transmitted from the Companions' — similarly it is not transmitted that he commanded establishing Friday in the villages of Medina despite their abundance. His saying: 'even if by solitary reports' — a solitary report is that transmitted by one from one. His saying: 'so residence in a city is necessary' — he mentioned it to connect to his saying 'or residence within what is inside'. His saying: 'that is not separated from it by a ghalwah' — in al-Fath here and in the prayer of the traveler, the estimate of the separating limit by a ghalwah is narrated from Muhammad, and in al-Nawadir it is the chosen view, and in al-Nihaya from al-Tamartashi that it is the most similar, and in al-Qahistani it is the soundest, and it is four hundred cubits in the soundest view. His saying: 'so one does not act on what is said contrary' — in al-Sharh: a note: you have known by the text of the hadith and the athar and the narration from our imams Abu Hanifa and his two companions and the choice of the verifying scholars that no consideration is given to the reaching of the call nor to the ghalwah nor miles, and it is nothing, opposing others even if its authentication is mentioned — among it is what is in al-Bada'i' that if one can attend Friday and spend the night with his family without hardship, it is obligatory on him. That is because one who exceeds this limit with the intention of travel is a traveler; if it were obligatory there, it would be obligatory on the traveler, which contradicts the text. His saying: 'excludes the sick' — that is, one who cannot go to the mosque, or can but fears increase of his illness or slow recovery due to a clear reason, and the caregiver is annexed to the sick if the patient is left unattended by his going out, according to the soundest view in al-Jawhara. His saying: 'due to what we narrated' — that is, from his saying: 'Friday is an obligatory right upon every Muslim in congregation except four...' and he counted among them the sick. His saying: 'so it is not obligatory on one who hides from an oppressor' — the expression 'oppressor' indicates that he is oppressed; if his hiding is due to a crime that necessitates a hadd penalty, for example, obligation is not dropped from him. His saying: 'the insolvent' — with tashdid? Actually takhfif: one who has no dinar or dirham, and the meaning here is one who cannot pay his debt. His saying: 'just as tayammum is permitted for him' — that is, he is permitted to leave Friday just as tayammum is permitted for him. His saying: 'so it is not obligatory on the blind according to Abu Hanifa' — no difference whether he finds a guide or not, whether the guide is volunteer or paid, and he has the means to hire, or he is a slave; mentioned by al-Sayyid. In al-Bahr: I have not seen the ruling of a blind person if he resides in the mosque where Friday is prayed—is it obligatory on him due to lack of hardship? And it is obligatory on the one-eyed due to lack of hardship. His saying: 'this is the issue of one capable through another's capability' — it previously passed that the corrector in it is the view of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). His saying: 'so it is not obligatory on the lame' — and similarly the one with both legs cut off, and in the speech there is indication that it is obligatory on one paralyzed in one leg or with one leg cut off if he can walk without difficulty; otherwise no, as indicated by al-Qahistani, and with this it is achieved.
Source pages p. 504

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah, discussing the conditions for the obligation of Friday prayer and exemptions. The text begins by emphasizing that Jumu'ah is obligatory only in a city (misr), not in villages, citing the hadith that it is only valid in a 'congregational city or great town.' The definition of a city's boundary is clarified: it is the area from which one becomes a traveler by leaving with the intention to travel, and upon reaching which one becomes a resident. This limit is measured by a ghalwah (bowshot), approximately 400 cubits. The commentator notes that the soundest view is that distance is not measured by the call reaching or by miles. The conditions for obligation are then listed: being male, free, resident in a city, healthy, safe from oppression, having sight, and having the ability to walk. Each condition is explained with exemptions: women, slaves, the sick, the elderly, those hiding from an oppressor, the insolvent fearing imprisonment, the blind (according to Abu Hanifa, with a difference from the two companions who require a guide), and the lame. The commentary also discusses the case of the blind person in detail, noting that Abu Hanifa exempts him regardless of finding a guide, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad require a guide. The passage ends by noting that heavy rain is also an excuse, and that puberty and intellect are not listed as separate conditions because they are general requirements for any obligation.

Key Terms
مصر (misr): A city or large town where Friday prayer and Eid prayers are established; defined as having a congregational mosque and a population that qualifies it as a settlement.
غلوة (ghalwah): A bowshot, approximately 400 cubits, used to define the boundary of a city for the purpose of residence.
قادر بقدرة الغير (qadir bi qudrat al-ghayr): One who is capable of performing an act through the help of another, e.g., a blind person with a guide.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the primary evidence that Jumu'ah is not valid in a village?
A) The hadith: 'Jumu'ah is an obligatory right upon every Muslim in congregation except four.'
B) The hadith: 'No Jumu'ah except in a congregational city or a great town.'
C) The statement of the Companion Ibn 'Umar.
D) Ijma' of the scholars.

Key Takeaway
Jumu'ah is obligatory only on those who meet the seven conditions of male, free, resident in a city, healthy, safe, sighted, and able to walk.

Salah — Prayer

Al-A'mā wa Qadir bi Qudrat al-Ghayr: The Blind Person's Obligation and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the blind person's Jumu'ah obligation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on the obligation of Jumu'ah on a blind person and identify the mufta bihi (relied-upon) view with its evidence.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa exempts the blind unconditionally; the Sahibayn obligate if a guide is available; the mufta bihi is the latter.

One of the most instructive intra-Hanafi disputes is the obligation of Jumu'ah on a blind person. The passage from al-Tahtawi highlights this as the paradigm case of 'qadir bi qudrat al-ghayr' (one capable through another's capability). In this lesson, we'll dissect the arguments of Abu Hanifa and the two companions, understand the concept, and see which view is relied upon for fatwa today.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition and its exceptions
The condition 'soundness of eyes' (salamat al-'aynayn) is listed. The blind are exempted; however, the text notes a dispute: 'at Abi Hanifa, contrary to the two (Sahibayn) if he finds a guide.'
This is not a cross-madhhab dispute but an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between the three founding imams.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and reasoning
Abu Hanifa holds that a blind person is not obligated for Jumu'ah at all, regardless of whether he has a guide. His reasoning is that the blind person suffers from a continuous hardship (mashaqqa) that justifies exemption, similar to the sick.
He does not consider the availability of a guide as removing the hardship because the blind cannot navigate independently.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and reasoning
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that if a guide is available, the blind person is capable of attending without difficulty, so Jumu'ah becomes obligatory on him. They consider the guide as enabling his attendance, making him 'capable through another's capability' (qadir bi qudrat al-ghayr).
This is analogous to the sighted person who can walk to the mosque.
4
Understand the concept of qadir bi qudrat al-ghayr
This legal concept refers to a person who, due to a physical limitation, cannot perform an act alone but can do so with the help of another. In Hanafi fiqh, such a person is generally treated as capable (qadir) regarding obligations.
The Sahibayn apply this principle here, while Abu Hanifa does not extend it to Jumu'ah for the blind.
5
Identify the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position
Al-Tahtawi states that the corrector (musahhih) in this issue is the view of the two companions (qawluhuma). Hence, the mufta bihi position is that a blind person must attend Jumu'ah if he finds a guide, whether volunteer or paid.
This tarjih is based on the later Hanafi preference for the Sahibayn's view in this matter.
