أفاد التعبير بظالم لم أنه مظلوم فإن كان اختفاؤه لجناية منه توجب حداً مثلاً لا يسقط عنه الوجوب . قوله : (المفلس) بالتخفيف الذي لا دينار له ولا درهم والمراد به هنا من لا يقدر على وفاء دينه. قوله : (كما ذكره السيد قال في البحر ولم أر حكم الأعمى إذا كان مقيماً بالجامع الذي يصلي فيه الجمعة هل تجب عليه لعدم الحرج اهـ وتجب على الأعور لعدم الحرج. قوله : (وهي مسئلة القادر بقدرة الغير قد تقدم أن المصحح فيها قولهما. قوله: (فلا تجب على المقعد) ومثله مقطوع الرجلين وفي الكلام إشارة إلى أنها تجب على مفلوج إحدى الرجلين، أو مقطوعها إذا كان يمكنه المشي بلا مشقة وإلا فلا أشار إليه القهستاني، وبهذا يحصل
The book of prayer: The traveler and that residence (is in a city) excludes the resident in a village due to his saying peace be upon him: 'Friday is an obligatory right upon every Muslim in congregation except four: a slave, a woman, a boy, or a sick person.' And in al-Bukhari: 'or a slave or a traveler.' And due to his saying peace be upon him: 'No Friday, no tashreeq, no Fitr prayer, no Adha prayer except in a congregational city or a great town.' And it is not transmitted from the Companions that when they conquered lands they occupied themselves with setting up pulpits and gathering except in cities, not villages; and if it were, it would have been transmitted, even if by solitary reports. So residence in a city is necessary. Or residence in what is within the limit of residence in the city, which is the place where one who departs from it with the intention of travel becomes a traveler, and one who reaches it becomes a resident in the soundest view, like the outskirts of the city and its courtyard that is not separated from it by a ghalwah (bowshot) as previously mentioned. And it is not obligatory on one who is outside it even if he hears the call, whether his village is near the city or far in the soundest view, so one does not act on what is said contrary to it even if authenticated. And the fourth: health, excludes the sick due to what we narrated, and the old man who is weak is annexed to the sick. And the fifth: safety from an oppressor, so it is not obligatory on one who hides from an oppressor, and the insolvent who fears imprisonment is annexed to him, just as tayammum is permitted for him. And the sixth: soundness of the eyes, so it is not obligatory on the blind according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) if he finds a guide—this is the issue of one capable through another's capability. And the seventh: soundness of the legs, so it is not obligatory on the lame due to his inability to walk, by agreement. And among excuses is heavy rain. As for puberty and intellect, they are not one. His saying: 'And it is not transmitted from the Companions' — similarly it is not transmitted that he commanded establishing Friday in the villages of Medina despite their abundance. His saying: 'even if by solitary reports' — a solitary report is that transmitted by one from one. His saying: 'so residence in a city is necessary' — he mentioned it to connect to his saying 'or residence within what is inside'. His saying: 'that is not separated from it by a ghalwah' — in al-Fath here and in the prayer of the traveler, the estimate of the separating limit by a ghalwah is narrated from Muhammad, and in al-Nawadir it is the chosen view, and in al-Nihaya from al-Tamartashi that it is the most similar, and in al-Qahistani it is the soundest, and it is four hundred cubits in the soundest view. His saying: 'so one does not act on what is said contrary' — in al-Sharh: a note: you have known by the text of the hadith and the athar and the narration from our imams Abu Hanifa and his two companions and the choice of the verifying scholars that no consideration is given to the reaching of the call nor to the ghalwah nor miles, and it is nothing, opposing others even if its authentication is mentioned — among it is what is in al-Bada'i' that if one can attend Friday and spend the night with his family without hardship, it is obligatory on him. That is because one who exceeds this limit with the intention of travel is a traveler; if it were obligatory there, it would be obligatory on the traveler, which contradicts the text. His saying: 'excludes the sick' — that is, one who cannot go to the mosque, or can but fears increase of his illness or slow recovery due to a clear reason, and the caregiver is annexed to the sick if the patient is left unattended by his going out, according to the soundest view in al-Jawhara. His saying: 'due to what we narrated' — that is, from his saying: 'Friday is an obligatory right upon every Muslim in congregation except four...' and he counted among them the sick. His saying: 'so it is not obligatory on one who hides from an oppressor' — the expression 'oppressor' indicates that he is oppressed; if his hiding is due to a crime that necessitates a hadd penalty, for example, obligation is not dropped from him. His saying: 'the insolvent' — with tashdid? Actually takhfif: one who has no dinar or dirham, and the meaning here is one who cannot pay his debt. His saying: 'just as tayammum is permitted for him' — that is, he is permitted to leave Friday just as tayammum is permitted for him. His saying: 'so it is not obligatory on the blind according to Abu Hanifa' — no difference whether he finds a guide or not, whether the guide is volunteer or paid, and he has the means to hire, or he is a slave; mentioned by al-Sayyid. In al-Bahr: I have not seen the ruling of a blind person if he resides in the mosque where Friday is prayed—is it obligatory on him due to lack of hardship? And it is obligatory on the one-eyed due to lack of hardship. His saying: 'this is the issue of one capable through another's capability' — it previously passed that the corrector in it is the view of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). His saying: 'so it is not obligatory on the lame' — and similarly the one with both legs cut off, and in the speech there is indication that it is obligatory on one paralyzed in one leg or with one leg cut off if he can walk without difficulty; otherwise no, as indicated by al-Qahistani, and with this it is achieved.
Source pages p. 504

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah, discussing the conditions for the obligation of Friday prayer and exemptions. The text begins by emphasizing that Jumu'ah is obligatory only in a city (misr), not in villages, citing the hadith that it is only valid in a 'congregational city or great town.' The definition of a city's boundary is clarified: it is the area from which one becomes a traveler by leaving with the intention to travel, and upon reaching which one becomes a resident. This limit is measured by a ghalwah (bowshot), approximately 400 cubits. The commentator notes that the soundest view is that distance is not measured by the call reaching or by miles. The conditions for obligation are then listed: being male, free, resident in a city, healthy, safe from oppression, having sight, and having the ability to walk. Each condition is explained with exemptions: women, slaves, the sick, the elderly, those hiding from an oppressor, the insolvent fearing imprisonment, the blind (according to Abu Hanifa, with a difference from the two companions who require a guide), and the lame. The commentary also discusses the case of the blind person in detail, noting that Abu Hanifa exempts him regardless of finding a guide, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad require a guide. The passage ends by noting that heavy rain is also an excuse, and that puberty and intellect are not listed as separate conditions because they are general requirements for any obligation.

Key Terms
قادر بقدرة الغير (qadir bi qudrat al-ghayr): One who is capable of performing an act through the help of another, e.g., a blind person with a guide.
الأعمى (al-a'mā): The blind person, specifically one who cannot see the road.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Who is the 'musahhih' (corrector) in the issue of the blind person's Jumu'ah obligation according to al-Tahtawi?
A) Abu Hanifa
B) Abu Yusuf
C) Muhammad al-Shaybani
D) Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn)

Key Takeaway
A blind person's obligation for Jumu'ah depends on the availability of a guide; the mufta bihi view obligates him, reflecting the principle of qadir bi qudrat al-ghayr.

Conditions of Health and Safety for Jumu'ah
Explaining the fourth and fifth conditions for Jumu'ah obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions of health and safety from an oppressor for Jumu'ah obligation and identify which persons are excused according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The sick, elderly, those hiding from an oppressor, and insolvent are excused from Jumu'ah due to inability or hardship.

This lesson examines the fourth and fifth conditions for the obligation of Jumu'ah: health and safety from an oppressor. The text from Maraqi al-Falah, with Hashiya al-Tahtawi, explains these exceptions. Understanding these conditions helps us apply the rule in cases of illness, fear, and debt.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditions
Locate the fourth and fifth conditions in the passage: health (sihha) and safety from an oppressor (amn min zalim). These are shurut wujub (conditions for obligation).
These conditions must be present for Jumu'ah to be obligatory.
2
Understand the exceptions
For health: the sick are excused, and the elderly weak are annexed (mulhaq) by analogy. For safety: one hiding from an oppressor is excused, and the insolvent fearing imprisonment is annexed. Note the qiyas to tayammum.
The annexation shows the Hanafi methodology of qiyas.
3
Analyze the dalil
The primary dalil is the hadith: 'Jumu'ah is obligatory upon every Muslim except four...'. The sick are explicitly excluded. The other cases are analogically derived.
Refer to the dalil_block for the hadith text.
4
Apply the conditions
Given a scenario with one of these excuses, determine whether Jumu'ah is obligatory. Consider if the person meets the condition of ability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بعيدا على الأصح فلا يعمل بما قيل بخلافه وإن صحح (و) الرابع (الصحة) خرج به المريض لما روبنا، والشيخ الكبير الذي ضعف ملحق بالمريض (و) الخامس (الأمن من ظالم فلا تجب على من اختفى من ظالم ويلحق به المفلس الخائف من الحبس كما جاز له التيمم (و) السادس (سلامة العينين) فلا تجب على الأعمى عند أبي حنيفة خلافاً لهما إذا يوصله، وهي مسئلة القادر بقدرة الغير (و) السابع (سلامة الرجلين) فلا تجب على المقعد لعجزه عن السعي اتفاقاً، ومن العذر المطر العظيم، وأما البلوغ، والعقل فليسا خاصين فلذا لم يذكرهما
(Far) on the correct opinion, so one does not act on what is said contrary to it even if it is corrected. (And) the fourth: health; excluded by it the sick due to what we narrated, and the elderly who are weak are annexed to the sick. (And) the fifth: safety from an oppressor; so it is not obligatory on one who hides from an oppressor, and the insolvent who fears imprisonment is annexed to him just as tayammum is permissible for him. (And) the sixth: soundness of the eyes; so it is not obligatory on the blind according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to the two (companions) if he finds a guide, and this is the issue of one able by another's ability. (And) the seventh: soundness of the legs; so it is not obligatory on the paralytic due to his inability to walk, by agreement, and from the excuses is heavy rain. As for puberty and sanity, they are not specific (to Jumu'ah), hence they were not mentioned.
Source pages p. 505

Commentary
This passage discusses the conditions for the obligation of Jumu'ah prayer, specifically the fourth to seventh conditions and some excuses. The commentator explains that these conditions are from the matn of Maraqi al-Falah. The fourth condition is health (sihha): the sick are exempted based on the hadith 'Jumu'ah is a right obligatory upon every Muslim in congregation except four...' including the sick. The elderly who are weak are treated like the sick. The fifth condition is safety from an oppressor: one who hides from an oppressor is not obligated, and the insolvent (mufalis) who fears imprisonment is included. This is justified by analogy: just as such a person is allowed tayammum, he is allowed to miss Jumu'ah. The sixth condition is soundness of eyes: here there is an intra-Hanafi dispute. Abu Hanifa says the blind are not obligated even if they find a guide, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) say the blind are obligated if they find a guide. This is the famous 'issue of one able by another's ability' (al-qadir bi qudrat al-ghayr). The commentator notes that the corrector in this matter is the view of the two (Sahibayn), but the text follows Abu Hanifa's view. The seventh condition is soundness of legs: the paralytic (muq'ad) is not obligated by agreement. Then excuses: heavy rain is an excuse, as is snow and mud (mentioned later). The passage concludes that puberty and sanity are not specific to Jumu'ah because they are general conditions for all prayers, so they are not mentioned here.

Key Terms
المريض (al-marīḍ): The sick person; one whose illness prevents him from attending Jumu'ah without undue hardship.
الشيخ الكبير (al-shaykh al-kabīr): The elderly person who is weak due to old age; annexed to the sick for Jumu'ah exemption.
المفلس (al-mufallis): The insolvent debtor who fears imprisonment; excused from Jumu'ah by analogy to one hiding from an oppressor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, who is excused from Jumu'ah due to the safety condition?
A) Anyone who fears any type of harm.
B) One hiding from an oppressor and the insolvent fearing imprisonment.
C) Only those being actively persecuted.
D) Anyone who owes debt.

Key Takeaway
Health and safety from oppression are conditions for Jumu'ah obligation; those unable due to sickness, old age, fear of oppression, or insolvency with fear of prison are excused.

Soundness of Eyes and Legs: The Blind and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explaining the sixth and seventh conditions for Jumu'ah, including the intra-Hanafi dispute on the blind.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi dispute on the obligation of Jumu'ah for the blind and apply the principle of 'al-qadir bi qudrat al-ghayr'.

Core Idea
The blind are excused from Jumu'ah according to Abu Hanifa even if a guide is available; the Sahibayn obligate if a guide is available.

This lesson explores the sixth and seventh conditions for Jumu'ah obligation: soundness of eyes and legs. The text presents a significant intra-Hanafi dispute on the blind, revolving around the principle of one able by another's ability (al-qadir bi qudrat al-ghayr). Understanding this dispute clarifies how Hanafi scholars balance ability and hardship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditions
Locate the sixth and seventh conditions: soundness of eyes (salamat al-'aynayn) and soundness of legs (salamat al-rijlayn). The exceptions are the blind and the paralytic respectively.
These are shurut wujub (conditions for obligation).
2
Note the dispute on the blind
Observe the statement: 'so it is not obligatory on the blind according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to the two (Sahibayn) if he finds a guide.' This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
The two refer to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
3
Understand the principle
The text identifies this as the issue of 'al-qadir bi qudrat al-ghayr' (one able by another's ability). Abu Hanifa does not consider a person obligated if they need assistance from others for worship; the Sahibayn do.
This principle appears in other fiqh issues too, e.g., Hajj.
4
Identify the thamarah
The practical consequence: a blind person with a guide is obligated according to Sahibayn but not according to Abu Hanifa. Thus the fatwa depends on which view is followed.
Later Hanafi practice prefers the view of the Sahibayn.
5
Consider other excuses
Note the seventh condition: the paralytic is excused by agreement. Also, heavy rain is an excuse (not a condition but an exemption).
The text mentions rain as a sample excuse.

Source Text

This passage discusses the conditions for the obligation of Jumu'ah prayer, specifically the fourth to seventh conditions and some excuses. The commentator explains that these conditions are from the matn of Maraqi al-Falah. The fourth condition is health (sihha): the sick are exempted based on the hadith 'Jumu'ah is a right obligatory upon every Muslim in congregation except four...' including the sick. Key Terms
الأعمى (al-a'mā): A blind person; the Hanafi school disputes whether Jumu'ah is obligatory on him if a guide is available.
القادر بقدرة الغير (al-qādir bi qudrat al-ghayr): One who is able to perform an act only through the assistance of another; in this context, a blind person with a guide.

First Condition of Jumu'ah: The City and Multiple Congregations
Explaining the first condition of validity (city or its precinct) and the dispute over multiple Jumu'ah in one city

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the first condition for Jumu'ah validity according to the Hanafi school and explain the ruling on multiple Jumu'ahs in a city, including the intra-Hanafi dispute and its practical consequence.

Core Idea
Multiple Jumu'ahs are permissible in a city; the correct opinion allows them, and precautionary zuhr is only for the elite.

This lesson addresses the first condition for the validity of Jumu'ah prayer: that it must be held in a city (miṣr) or its precinct (finā'). A key intra-Hanafi dispute arises from this condition: can multiple Jumu'ah prayers be held in the same city? The correct opinion says yes, but a weak opinion restricts it. We will explore the proofs, the practical consequences, and why the Author cautions against a common 'precautionary' practice that can harm the faith of laypeople.

Guided Path
1
Identify the First Condition
State the condition: Jumu'ah must be performed in a city (miṣr) or its precinct (finā'), including the 'Eid prayer ground. The finā' is considered part of the city for the needs of its residents.
This condition is from the text: 'الأول (المصر أو فناؤه)'.
2
State the Correct Hanafi Position on Multiplicity
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (the correct opinion), multiple Jumu'ahs are valid in many places within the city and its precinct. This is the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position.
The text says: 'وتصح إقامة الجمعة في مواضع كثيرة بالمصر وفنائه، وهو قول أبي حنيفة ومحمد في الأصح'.
3
Note the Weak Opinion and Its Consequence
Abu Yusuf's weak opinion prohibits multiple Jumu'ahs in one city. According to that view, only the first congregation (by starting time) is valid; others must pray ẓuhr. Some advise praying four rak'ahs of ẓuhr after Jumu'ah as precaution.
The text calls it 'القول الضعيف المانع من جواز التعدد'.
4
Analyze the Author's Critique of Precautionary Zuhr
The Author argues that true precaution is following the stronger proof (the permissibility of multiplicity). Praying ẓuhr as caution causes harm: the ignorant may believe Jumu'ah is not obligatory or that the obligatory act is multiple. Therefore, this fatwa is given only to the elite (khawāṣṣ).
The text: 'وليس الاحتياط في فعلها لأن الاحتياط هو العمل بأقوى الدليلين... ولا يفتى بالأربع إلا للخواص'.
5
Determine the Practical Fatwa
For the general public, multiple Jumu'ahs are fully valid and no ẓuhr is required. The weak opinion is not applied except in rare cautionary cases for knowledgeable individuals.
The mufta bihi is the permissive view, as supported by al-Sarakhsī and others.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويشترط لصحتها) أي صلاة الجمعة (ستة أشياء) الأول (المصر أو فناؤه) سواء مصلى العيد وغيره لأنه بمنزلة المصر في حق حوائج أهله، وتصح إقامة الجمعة في مواضع كثيرة بالمصر وفنائه، وهو قول أبي حنيفة ومحمد في الأصح ومن لازم جواز التعدد سقوط اعتبار السبق وعلى القول الضعيف المانع من جواز التعدد قيل بصلاة أربع بعدها بنية آخر ظهر عليه، وليس الاحتياط في فعلها لأن الاحتياط هو العمل بأقوى الدليلين وأقواهما إطلاق جواز تعدد الجمعة وبفعل الأربع مفسدة اعتقاد الجهلة عدم فرض الجمعة أو تعدد المفروض في وقتها ولا يفتى بالأربع إلا للخواص
(And it is required for its validity) i.e., Jumu'ah prayer (six things): the first (the city or its precinct) whether it is the 'Eid prayer place or other, because it is like the city regarding the needs of its residents. And the establishment of Jumu'ah is valid in many places within the city and its precinct—this is the saying of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad in the correct opinion. And from the necessary consequence of permitting multiplicity is the dropping of consideration of precedence. And according to the weak opinion—which prohibits multiplicity—it is said that one prays four (rak'ahs) after it with the intention of the last zuhr that is upon him. And precaution is not in doing that (the four), because precaution is acting upon the stronger of the two proofs, and the stronger of them is the unrestricted permissibility of multiple Jumu'ahs. And by doing the four, there is the harm of the ignorant believing the non-obligation of Jumu'ah or the multiplicity of the obligatory act in its time. And the four are not given as a fatwa except to the elite.
Source pages p. 506

Commentary
This passage from the hashiyah explains the first condition for the validity of Jumu'ah prayer: the city (misr) or its precinct (fina'). The commentary clarifies that the 'Eid prayer place and other areas within the city's precinct are considered part of the city for this purpose. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold the correct opinion that Jumu'ah can be performed in multiple locations within a city and its precinct, and this is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi). The weak opinion (Abu Yusuf's) prohibits multiple Jumu'ahs in one city, and according to that view, if multiple are held, only the first one (by precedence) is valid. Those who follow the weak opinion sometimes advise praying four rak'ahs of zuhr after Jumu'ah with the intention of the last zuhr that is due upon them, as a precaution. However, the commentator argues that this is not true precaution, because true precaution is to follow the stronger proof, which is the permissibility of multiple Jumu'ahs. Moreover, praying zuhr after Jumu'ah can cause laypeople to doubt the obligation of Jumu'ah itself. Therefore, the fatwa of praying four rak'ahs is only given to the elite (khawass) who understand the issue, not to the general public.

Key Terms
المصر (al-miṣr): A city or large town that is a center; the condition for Jumu'ah validity is that it must be held in a misr or its fina' (precinct).
الفناء (al-finā'): The precinct or vicinity of a city, including open spaces and 'Eid prayer grounds that serve the needs of the city's residents.
السبق (al-sabq): Precedence; when multiple Jumu'ahs are held, who started first. In the weak opinion, precedence determines validity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Only one.
B) Two maximum.
C) Multiple, as many as needed.
D) None, because Jumu'ah must be in the central mosque.

Key Takeaway
The correct Hanafi position allows multiple Jumu'ahs in a city; precautionary ẓuhr is not for the public, but only for the elite who follow the weak opinion.

Jumu'ah Condition: City and Multiplicity
Explains the condition of the city and the ruling on multiple Friday prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition for Jumu'ah validity regarding the city and explain the ruling on multiple Friday prayers, including the intra-madhhab dispute and the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Multiple Friday prayers in one city are absolutely permissible – the condition is the city, not singularity.

This passage from al-Tahtawi's Hashiya addresses two interconnected issues: the requirement that Jumu'ah be held in a city or its outskirts, and whether multiple Jumu'ah can be held simultaneously within that city. The author clarifies that the soundest Hanafi position, contrary to some weak opinions, permits multiplicity absolutely, and warns against publicising the precautionary four-rak'at prayer due to potential misunderstanding.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition and its evidence
Read the first part of the passage to determine what is required for Jumu'ah validity: the city (misr) or its outskirts (fina'). Note the hadith cited: 'لا جمعة ولا تشريق إلا في مصر جامع' and understand how Hanafis interpret this.
The hadith is zanni in transmission and meaning, but it is the primary dalil.
2
Distinguish the three Hanafi positions on multiplicity
Identify the views of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (absolute permissibility), the zahir al-riwayah (two places only), and Abu Yusuf (only one place or two with conditions). Understand which is considered 'al-ashah' (soundest).
The text contrasts 'al-ashah' (absolute) with 'muqabil al-ashah' (apparent narration of two places).
3
Apply the tarjih principle to determine the mufta bihi
See how al-Sarakhsi, al-'Ayni, and others prefer absolute permissibility, and note that this is the position taken for fatwa. Understand that the condition (misr) is met in each group, so multiplicity is valid.
The maxim: al-ashah is relied upon even if opposed by zahir al-riwayah.
4
Evaluate the ihtiyat prayer and its limitations
Read the discussion about praying four rak'ats after Jumu'ah with the intention of the last Dhuhr. Understand why the author says true precaution is following the stronger evidence, and why this prayer is only for the elite.
Publicizing the ihtiyat prayer can lead to misunderstanding about the obligation of Jumu'ah.

It is required for its validity, i.e., Friday prayer, six things. First: the city or its outskirts, whether the Eid prayer place or elsewhere, because it is like the city regarding the needs of its people. And it is valid to hold Friday prayer in many places in the city and its outskirts. This is the statement of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad in the soundest opinion. And from the permissibility of multiplicity follows the dropping of consideration of precedence. And on the weak opinion that prevents multiplicity, it is said to pray four [rak'ats] after it with the intention of the last Dhuhr that is due. And precaution (ihtiyat) is not in doing it, because precaution is acting by the stronger of the two proofs, and the stronger of them is the absolute permissibility of multiplicity of Friday prayer. And by doing the four there is corruption of the ignorant people's belief that Friday is not obligatory, or multiplicity of the obligatory in its time. And the four are not given as a fatwa except to the elite. And their action is... combining what is in al-Bahr of obligation and what is in al-Shamni of intentionality, as benefited by some virtuous ones. His statement: 'And from the excuse is heavy rain,' and likewise snow and mud. He said in al-Sharh: We have mentioned that it drops attendance for congregation, end. His statement: 'they are not specific' i.e., to Friday. His statement: 'and other than it' he said it absolutely, so it includes what has a building and other than it, and the explanation of the outskirts has preceded recently. His statement: 'in the soundest opinion' al-Sarakhsi said: with it we take, and upon it is the fatwa as in Sharh al-Majma' by al-'Ayni, and as in al-Fath. And the opposite of the soundest is what is in al-Bada'i': that the apparent of the narration is permissibility in two places, so it is not permissible in more than that, and upon it is reliance, end. For the school is absolute permissibility. And what al-Shaykh al-'Allamah al-Maqdisi said in Nur al-Shum'ah from the Imam: it is not permissible except in one place in the single city. And what al-Imam al-Zahid al-'Attabi said: otherwise it appeared to him that it is not permissible except in two places, and if they do it, the Friday prayer is for the first, and if they pray together, their prayer is all invalid. And the soundest is absolute permissibility in places due to the absoluteness of the proof, end. Benefited from al-Sharh. His statement: 'and on the weak opinion' it is the statement of Abu Yusuf. His statement: 'the one who prevents multiplicity, then Friday prayer according to him is for the preceding one, and it is invalidated by simultaneity and ambiguity, then precedence is considered by starting, and it is said by finishing, and it is said by both.' His statement: 'it is said to pray four' i.e., the obligation of that. His statement: 'with the intention of the last Dhuhr that is due' it is the best because if Friday prayer is not valid, then Dhuhr is due upon him, and if it suffices, the four are for the Dhuhr that is due, so it falls, and if there is no Dhuhr upon him, then [it is] supererogatory, end. And it is said: he intends the sunnah, and it is said: the Dhuhr of his day as in al-Qunyah. His statement: 'and precaution is not in doing it, etc.' al-Burhan al-Halabi said: the doing is precaution because the disagreement regarding it is strong, because it was not prayed in the time of the Salaf except in one place in the city, and that the correct is permissibility of multiplicity for necessity does not prevent the legitimacy of precaution, end. His statement: 'and the stronger of them is the absolute permissibility of multiplicity of Friday prayer' due to the absoluteness of the hadith: 'There is no Friday prayer and no tashriq except in a congregational city.' So the city is a condition for its establishment, and it is present in every group, end. His statement: 'and by doing the four' is a predicate fronted to his statement 'corruption of belief, etc.' His statement: 'non-obligation of Friday' is the object of belief, and his statement 'or multiplicity' is coordinated with it. He said in al-Sharh: In doing the four there is a great corruption, which is the belief that Friday is not obligatory because they observe Dhuhr prayer, so they become lazy in performing Friday, or their belief that Friday and Dhuhr after it are obligatory, end. His statement: 'and the four are not given as a fatwa except to the elite' al-'Allamah al-Maqdisi said after quoting what indicates prohibition of it: we say: they [pray] it in their homes.
Source pages p. 506

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement from al-Tahtawi's Hashiya on Maraqi al-Falah, discussing the first condition for the validity of Friday prayer: that it be held in a city (misr) or its outskirts (fina'). The author explains that Jumu'ah is valid in multiple locations within a city, and this is the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani, which is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) view. The text clarifies that the necessity of precedence (sabq) falls away when multiplicity is permitted. A weak opinion, attributed to Abu Yusuf, prohibits multiplicity; according to him, if multiple prayers occur, only the first is valid, and if they coincide, all are invalid. Under this weak opinion, some scholars recommend praying four rak'ats after Jumu'ah with the intention of the last Dhuhr prayer that was due (a form of ihtiyat or precaution). However, the author strongly argues that ihtiyat does not lie in performing these four rak'ats, because true precaution is to follow the stronger evidence, which supports absolute permissibility. Moreover, publicly performing the four rak'ats leads to misunderstanding among the common people—either making them think Jumu'ah is not obligatory or that two obligatory prayers are due at the same time. Therefore, the fatwa of the four rak'ats is only given to the elite (khawass) who can understand the nuance. The text then delves into detailed commentary on the conditions of excusing rain, snow, mud, and the definition of the outskirts. It cites various authorities: al-Sarakhsi, al-'Ayni, al-Bada'i', al-Maqdisi, and al-'Attabi, all affirming the soundest opinion of absolute permissibility of multiple Jumu'ah prayers in a city, based on the hadith: 'There is no Friday prayer and no tashriq except in a congregational city.' This hadith establishes the city as a condition, and since the condition is met in each group, multiplicity is valid. The passage concludes by emphasizing the corruption caused by publicly praying the four rak'ats and reiterates that it is only for the elite.

Key Terms
المصر (al-misr): A settled area with a ruler, judge, market, and public facilities; effectively a city or large town where Friday prayer is established.
الفناء (al-fina'): The outskirts or attached areas of a city, such as suburbs, where the city's needs (like markets and cemeteries) are located.
التعدد (al-ta'addud): The holding of more than one Friday prayer in the same city simultaneously.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) It is permissible absolutely, regardless of need.
C) It is only permissible in two locations.
D) It is permissible only with the ruler's permission.

Key Takeaway
Multiple Friday prayers in a city are absolutely permissible in the Hanafi school; the condition is the city, not unity of location.

The Second Condition: Ruler or Deputy Leading Jumu'ah
Discusses the requirement that the ruler or his deputy lead Friday prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition that the ruler or his deputy must lead Jumu'ah and identify when necessity permits otherwise.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah requires the ruler or his deputy as imam; otherwise it is invalid unless necessity permits.

This lesson examines the second condition for the validity of Friday prayer (Jumu'ah) in the Hanafi school: that the prayer be led by the ruler (sultan) or his authorized deputy. The source text from al-Tahtawi's Hashiya explains the reasoning behind this requirement and covers exceptional scenarios involving usurpers, impossibility of permission, non-Muslim rulers, and the continuity of deputies. Understanding this condition is crucial for correctly performing Jumu'ah in various political contexts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Condition
Read the first sentence of the Arabic passage to identify the second condition of validity: that the ruler or his deputy leads Jumu'ah. Note the purpose: to prevent disputes over leadership.
2
Examine the Proof
Locate the proof cited by al-Hasan and Ibn al-Mundhir: the continuous practice of the Salaf. Understand that this is a qawl sahabi and ijma' that establishes the condition.
The proof is zanni in transmission but considered qati in practice.
3
Analyze Exceptional Cases
Go through the exceptions: usurpers (mutaghallib) who effectively govern, necessity when the ruler is absent or dead, non-Muslim rulers, and deputies after the caliph's death. Note the conditions for each exception.
Necessity is key: 'if not possible to seek permission, people may gather on a man'.
4
Understand the Necessity Ruling
Focus on the ruling that if seeking permission is impossible due to death or fitna, and people gather on a man, Jumu'ah is valid. Contrast this with doing so without necessity, which is impermissible.
The example of Ali during the siege of Uthman is cited.
5
Apply to Modern Contexts
Consider how this ruling applies in situations like Muslim minorities in non-Muslim states or political instability. The passage permits Jumu'ah under non-Muslim rule, but emphasizes seeking a Muslim governor.
Later Hanafi fatwas allow elected community imams under necessity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و) الثاني من شروط الصحة أن يصلي بهم السلطان) إماماً فيها (أو نائبة) يعني من أمره بإقامة الجمعة للتحرز عن تفويتها بقطع الأطماع في التقدم وله الإستنابة وإن كان السلطان هو من له العهد، وإلى فوقه قال الحسن: أربع إلى السلطان، وذكر منها الجمعة، والعيدين، ومثله لا يعرف إلا سماعاً فيحمل عليه وقال ابن المنذر : مضت السنة أن الذي يقيم الجمعة السلطان أو من بها أمره فإن لم يكن كذلك صلوا الظهر. كذا في الحلبي والمتغلب الذي لا عهد له أي لا منشور له إذا كانت سيرته بين الرعية سيرة الأمراء، ويحكم بينهم بحكم الولاة تجوز إقامته الجمعة .اهـ. قوله : ( يعني من أمره بإقامة الجمعة) وهو الأمير، أو القاضي، أو الخلفاء كما في العناية، ولو عبداً ولي عمل ناحية، وإن لم تجزأ قضيته، وأنكحته، وإذا لم يمكن استئذان السلطان ،لموته أو فتنة . واجتمع الناس على رجل فصلى بهم جاز للضرورة كما فعل علي في محاصرة عثمان رضي الله عنهما وإن فعلوا ذلك لغير ما ذكر لا يجوز لعدم الضرورة، وروي ذلك عن محمد في العيون، وهو الصحيح، وفي مفتاح السعادة عن مجمع الفتاوي غلب على المسلمين ولاة الكفار يجوز للمسلمين إقامة الجمع، والأعياد، ويصير القاضي قاضياً بتراضي المسلمين، ويجب عليهم أن يلتمسوا والياً مسلماً أهـ، ولو مات الخليفة، وله ولاة على أمور العامة كان لهم أن يقيموا الجمعة لأنهم أقيموا لأمور المسلمين، فكانوا على حالهم ما لم يعزلوا حلبي، وفي البحر والنهر. يجوز لقاضي القضاة كقاضي العساكر بمصر إقامة الجمعة، وتولية الخطباء، ولا يتوقف ذلك على إذن كما أن له أن يستخلف للقضاء وإن لم يؤذن له مع أنّ القاضي ليس له الإستخلاف إلا بإذن السلطان لأن توليته قاضي
And the second of the conditions of validity is that the ruler pray with them as imam therein, or his deputy, meaning the one he ordered to establish Friday prayer, in order to guard against its loss by cutting off ambitions for leadership. And he may appoint a deputy. And the sultan is the one who has the covenant, and above him, al-Hasan said: four [are exclusive] to the sultan, including Friday and the two Eids. And the likes of this is only known by hearing, so it is to be interpreted accordingly. And Ibn al-Mundhir said: The sunnah has passed that the one who establishes Friday is the sultan or the one he commands. If not, they pray Dhuhr. This is in al-Halabi. And the usurper (mutaghallib) who has no letter of appointment, if his conduct among the subjects is like the conduct of princes and he judges between them by the judgment of governors, his establishment of Friday is permissible. End. His statement: 'meaning the one he ordered to establish Friday prayer' and he is the prince, or the judge, or the caliphs as in al-'Inayah. Even if he is a slave appointed to the work of a district, even if his judiciary and marriage contracts are not valid. And if seeking permission of the sultan is not possible due to his death or civil strife, and the people gather upon a man and he prays with them, it is permissible due to necessity, as did 'Ali during the siege of 'Uthman, may Allah be pleased with them both. But if they do that for other than what is mentioned, it is not permissible due to lack of necessity. And that is narrated from Muhammad in al-'Uyun, and it is the correct view. And in Miftah al-Sa'adah from Majma' al-Fatawa: If non-Muslim governors dominate Muslims, it is permissible for Muslims to establish Friday and the two Eids, and the judge becomes a judge by mutual consent of the Muslims, and they must seek a Muslim governor. End. And if the caliph dies while he has deputies over public affairs, they may establish Friday because they were appointed for the affairs of Muslims, so they remain as they were until they are dismissed. Halabi. And in al-Bahr and al-Nahr: It is permissible for the chief judge, like the judge of the armies in Egypt, to establish Friday and appoint preachers, and that does not depend on permission, just as he may appoint a deputy for judgment even if not permitted, even though the judge does not have the right to deputize except with the sultan's permission, because his appointment [cut off].
Source pages p. 507

Commentary
This passage from al-Tahtawi's Hashiya covers the second condition for the validity of Friday prayer: that it be led by the ruler (sultan) or his authorized deputy. The purpose is to prevent infighting and competition for leadership (imamah). The text explains that the ruler or his deputy must order the establishment of Jumu'ah. It then addresses exceptional cases: if the ruler is a usurper (mutaghallib) who acts like a prince, his leading Jumu'ah is valid. If the ruler has died or there is civil strife, people may choose a man to lead out of necessity, as 'Ali did during the siege of 'Uthman. However, if done without necessity, it is not permissible. The text also discusses the scenario where non-Muslims rule over Muslims: Muslims may still hold Jumu'ah and 'Eid prayers, and a judge may be established by mutual consent, but they must seek a Muslim ruler. Finally, it mentions that if the caliph dies but his deputies remain, they can continue to lead Jumu'ah. The passage emphasizes the importance of authority and order in the congregational prayer.

Key Terms
السلطان (al-sultan): The legitimate ruler with authority over the Muslims, often specifically the caliph or his governor.
المتغلب (al-mutaghallib): A usurper who seizes power without official appointment but acts like a ruler in practice.
نائبه (na'ibuh): The ruler's deputy or appointee authorized to lead Jumu'ah, such as a judge or governor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a non-Muslim ruler dominates a Muslim land, what is the ruling on Muslims holding Friday prayer?
A) It is not permissible until a Muslim ruler is installed.
B) It is permissible for Muslims to hold Jumu'ah and 'Eid prayers, and they must seek a Muslim governor.
C) Only Dhuhr prayer is valid under non-Muslim rule.
D) Muslims can hold Jumu'ah only with the non-Muslim ruler's permission.

Key Takeaway
Jumu'ah requires the ruler or his authorized deputy to lead; necessity permits exceptions such as under non-Muslim rule or when seeking permission is impossible.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Condition of Sultan or His Deputy for Jumu'ah and Ruling on Istikhlaf
Explaining the second condition of Jumu'ah validity and the permissibility of appointing a substitute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition for the validity of Jumu'ah regarding the imam and explain the permissibility of appointing a deputy (istikhlaf) by implication.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah requires the Sultan or his deputy to prevent disputes; implicit permission suffices for appointing substitutes.

The Hanafi school requires that Jumu'ah be led by the ruler (Sultan) or his authorized deputy to maintain order and prevent conflict. This condition is based on transmitted sunnah and rational reasoning. But what happens when the appointed imam cannot lead? The text discusses the permissibility of appointing a substitute (istikhlaf) even without explicit permission, relying on the principle that the original delegation implies authority to delegate further.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Condition
State that the second condition for Jumu'ah validity is that the prayer is led by the Sultan or his deputy. The text explicitly says: 'الثاني من شروط الصحة أن يصلي بهم السلطان إماماً فيها أو نائبه'.
This condition is a shart (condition) for validity, not a rukn (pillar).
2
Understand the Wisdom
The condition exists 'للتحرز عن تفويتها بقطع الأطماع في التقدم' — to guard against losing the prayer by cutting off ambitions to advance. This prevents disputes that could cause the time to lapse.
The rational proof (dalil ma'qul) is that without a central authority, people would compete for leadership and miss the prayer.
3
Examine the Transmitted Proof
Ibn al-Mundhir states: 'مضت السنة أن الذي يقيم الجمعة السلطان أو من بأمره' — the sunnah is that the one who establishes Jumu'ah is the Sultan or the one he commands. This is the transmitted proof (dalil manqul).
This proof is from the practice of the early community.
4
Explore the Ruling on Istikhlaf
The text asserts that the appointed person may appoint a substitute (istikhlaf) by implication (dalalah). When the Sultan delegates authority, he implicitly permits further delegation to handle obstacles like illness or death. This is supported by statements from al-Bada'i', al-Bahr, and others. The fatwa in 945 AH established absolute permissibility of istikhlaf.
This is a critical refinement: earlier restrictions (e.g., by al-Zayla'i) are rejected.
5
Note Exceptions and Subsidiary Rules
If the substitute is appointed after the khutbah but before the imam's ihram, he must have attended the khutbah or part of it. The preacher and imam need not be the same person. In cases of necessity (death, fitna, or non-Muslim rulers), Jumu'ah may be led by a de facto leader or by mutual consent.
These rules show the school's flexibility to ensure Jumu'ah is not abandoned.

And the second of the conditions of validity is that the Sultan should lead them as imam in it, or his deputy, meaning the one he commands to establish Jumu'ah, to guard against its being lost by cutting off ambitions to advance, and he may appoint a deputy even if... With the Sultan is the one who... Al-Hasan said: four (conditions) to the Sultan, including Jumu'ah and the two Eids, and the like is not known except by hearing, so it is attributed to him. Ibn al-Mundhir said: The established sunnah is that the one who establishes Jumu'ah is the Sultan or the one he commands; otherwise they pray Zuhr. As in al-Halabi. And the usurper who has no covenant, i.e., no patent, if his conduct among the subjects is the conduct of princes and he judges among them with the judgment of governors, it is permissible for him to establish Jumu'ah. His saying: (meaning the one he commands to establish Jumu'ah) and he is the governor, or the judge, or the caliphs as in al-'Inayah, even if a slave is appointed over a district, even if his judgment and marriage are not valid. And when seeking permission from the Sultan is impossible due to his death or fitnah, and the people gather around a man and he leads them, it is permissible out of necessity, as 'Ali did during the siege of 'Uthman, may Allah be pleased with them both. But if they do so for other than that, it is not permissible due to lack of necessity. That is related from Muhammad in al-'Uyun, and it is the correct view. In Miftah al-Sa'adah from Majma' al-Fatawa: If non-Muslim rulers dominate the Muslims, it is permissible for the Muslims to establish Jumu'ah and the Eids, and the judge becomes a judge by the mutual consent of the Muslims, and they must seek a Muslim ruler. And if the caliph dies and he has deputies over public affairs, they may establish Jumu'ah because they were appointed for the affairs of Muslims, so they remain in their position until they are removed. In al-Bahr and al-Nahr: It is permissible for the chief judge, like the judge of the armies in Egypt, to establish Jumu'ah and appoint preachers, and that does not depend on permission, just as he may appoint a substitute for judgment even if he was not permitted, because his appointment as a judge... (page 508) ...the Sultan did not explicitly permit him by implication, whether due to an excuse or otherwise, whether present or absent. If he is preceded by an event (hadath) after beginning the prayer, then anyone suitable as imam, his succession is valid. If before his ihram for the prayer after the khutbah, then it is required that the successor have attended the khutbah or part of it. And the third: in the enumeration of judges, permission is implied, as al-Kamal stated in the chapter on judgment, and it does not depend on the confirmation of the ruler called al-Basha. And in al-Bahr also, al-'Allamah Ibn Jarbash stated in al-Tuhfah regarding Jumu'ah that the permission of the Sultan or his deputy is only a condition at the time of building the mosque; thereafter, permission is not required for every preacher. So when the supervisor appoints a preacher for the mosque, he may lead himself or appoint a deputy, and the permission continues for every preacher. And in Majma' al-Anhur: Appointing a deputy in our time is absolutely permissible because in the year 945 AH the Imam's permission occurred, and that is the fatwa. And in al-Quniyah: Unity of the preacher and imam is not a condition according to the chosen view. In al-Dhakhirah: If a sane boy gives the khutbah and an adult leads the prayer, it is permissible, but unity is better as in Sharh al-Athar. In al-Mujarrad, Abu Hanifah said: Permission for the khutbah is permission for Jumu'ah, and permission for Jumu'ah is permission for the khutbah. If he said 'Give the khutbah to them but do not lead them in prayer,' it is permissible for him to lead them. His saying: (to guard against its being lost) is the reason for requiring the Sultan or his deputy. His saying: (by cutting off ambitions) is connected to 'guard'; indeed, ambitions cause loss because of the dispute among those ambitious to advance, so the time may pass while they are in dispute, and this is an intellectual proof, while the transmitted proof is what we have mentioned. His saying: (and he may appoint a deputy, etc.) In al-Bada'i': Whoever owns Jumu'ah owns its establishment over someone else. In al-Bahr: It is explicit or nearly explicit about the permissibility of appointing a deputy absolutely, and al-Zayla'i's restriction of appointment to preceding event has no evidence. What is in al-Durar that the preacher may not appoint a deputy unless delegated is refuted by Ibn al-Kamal. His saying: (by implication) is connected to an implied operator indicating that he has the right to appoint by implication. In al-Sharh: When he permits someone to establish it, he owns appointment even if not explicitly delegated because when the supreme imam delegated it to him with the knowledge that obstacles preventing its establishment like illness, event during prayer, or time constraints may occur and he cannot wait for the supreme imam because it cannot be delayed beyond the time, that is implied permission for appointment, and the language of the situation is more eloquent than the language of the article, as the commentators said. His saying: (his succession is valid) because the successor does not initiate (the prayer), and the khutbah is a condition for initiation, and it existed for the original (imam). His saying: (must have attended the khutbah or part of it) because the khutbah is a condition for validity for the one who initiates the tahrimah of Jumu'ah, which is the imam, and it is not a condition for every worshipper, so it is as if the deputy gave the khutbah himself. Otherwise, the deputy's commencement is not valid at all unless he appoints another who attended the khutbah, which is valid. His saying: (also) i.e., just as suitability for imamah is required, or just as that is required for the imam if he is not the preacher. In al-Sharh: Know that it is permissible for the holder of the khutbah function to pray behind his deputy without excuse, just as it is permissible for the Sultan to pray behind his subordinate who establishes Jumu'ah even though the Sultan is capable of giving the khutbah himself.
Source pages p. 507

Commentary
This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi is a critical refinement of the text of Maraqi al-Falah, discussing the second condition for the validity of Jumu'ah prayer: the presence of the Sultan or his deputy as the imam. The author explains that the condition exists to prevent disputes that could cause the prayer to be missed. He then discusses various rulings related to this condition: the permissibility for a usurper (mutaghallib) to lead Jumu'ah if he acts as a ruler, and the permissibility of appointing a deputy (istikhlaf) even without explicit permission, by implication (dalalah). The passage cites many Hanafi sources, concluding that in our time, istikhlaf is absolutely permissible due to the precedent set by the Imam in 945 AH. The text also addresses subsidiary issues: the requirement for a substitute to have attended the khutbah if appointed before the imam starts the prayer, and the permissibility of the preacher being different from the imam. The author balances transmitted evidence (sunnah) with rational reasoning (cutting off ambitions), emphasizing that the condition is a means to preserve the communal aspect of Jumu'ah.

Key Terms
السلطان (al-sultan): In this context, the ruler or his authoritative deputy who can legally lead the Jumu'ah prayer.
نائب (na'ib): The deputy appointed by the Sultan to lead Jumu'ah, including governors, judges, or any authorized person.
استنابة (istinabah): The act of appointing a deputy (khalifah) to lead the Jumu'ah prayer in one's place, which can be done explicitly or by implication.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as discussed in this passage, what is the second condition for the validity of Jumu'ah?
A) The prayer must be led by the Sultan or his deputy.
B) The khutbah must be given by the same person who leads the prayer.
C) The prayer must be performed in a mosque built with the Sultan's permission.
D) The imam must be appointed by the chief judge.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires the Sultan or his deputy for Jumu'ah validity, but allows implicit delegation (istikhlaf) to prevent the prayer from being missed.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Conditions for Istikhlaf in Jumu'ah Prayer
Critical refinement of istikhlaf rulings in Jumu'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for istikhlaf in Jumu'ah prayer according to the Hanafi school and distinguish the rulings when the need arises before vs. after the imam's commencement of the prayer.

Core Idea
Implicit permission suffices for istikhlaf; the substitute must have attended the khutbah if the need arises before starting the prayer.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi critically refines earlier Hanafi positions on istikhlaf (appointing a substitute imam) for Jumu'ah prayer. It clarifies that explicit permission from the Sultan is not always required; the language of the situation (lisān al-ḥāl) implies permission. The key distinction is whether the obstacle occurs before or after the imam starts the prayer, which determines the conditions for the substitute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Istikhlaf in Jumu'ah is permissible (jā'iz) with conditions. Note that it is not obligatory.
The ruling is mubah, not wajib.
2
Distinguish two scenarios
Scenario A: obstacle after imam starts prayer (e.g., hadath). Scenario B: obstacle after khutbah but before starting prayer.
The condition for the substitute differs.
3
Extract conditions for Scenario B
If the need arises before starting prayer, the substitute must have attended the khutbah (or part of it). This is because the khutbah is a condition for the imam who initiates the prayer.
The substitute is considered as having given the khutbah himself.
4
Understand the basis of implicit permission
The Sultan's delegation implies permission for substitution because obstacles are foreseeable and Jumu'ah cannot be delayed. This is a rational proof (dalīl ʿaqlī) and the principle of lisān al-ḥāl.
Lisān al-ḥāl is considered more eloquent than explicit speech.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi refinement
Al-Zayla'i restricted substitution to cases of preceding hadath, but this is rejected by later authorities like Ibn al-Kamal. The mufta bihi is absolute permissibility.
This is a critical refinement of earlier views.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لم يصرح له بها السلطان دلالة بعذر أو بغيره حضر أو غاب عنه وأما إذا سبقه حدث فإن كان بعد شروعه في الصلاة فكل من صلح إماماً صح استخلافه، وإذا كان قبل إحرامه للصلاة بعد الخطبة فيشترط أن يكون الخليفة قد شهد الخطبة، أو بعضها أيضاً (و) الثالث في تعداد القضاة إذن له بذلك دلالة، كما صرح به الكمال في باب القضاء، ولا يتوقف ذلك على تقرير الحاكم المسمى بالباشا اهـ وفي البحر أيضاً، وصرح العلامة ابن جرباش في التحفة في الجمعة بأن إذن السلطان، أو نائبه إنما هو شرط عند بناء المسجد، ثم بعد ذلك لا يشترط الإذن لكل خطيب، فإذا قرر الناظر خطيباً للمسجد فله إقامته بنفسه، وينائبه، وإن الإذن مستصحب لكل خطيب اهـ وفي مجمع الأنهر والاستخلاف في زماننا جائز مطلقاً لأنه وقع في تاريخ خمس وأربعين وتسعمائة إذن الإمام وعليه الفتوى اهـ وفي القنية، واتحاد الخطيب، والإمام ليس بشرط على المختار نهر، وفي الذخيرة: لو خطب صبي عاقل، وصلى بالغ جاز لكن الأولى الاتحاد كما في شرح الآثار، وفي المجرد قال أبو حنيفة: الأذن في الخطبة إذن في الجمعة، والإذن في الجمعة إذن في الخطبة، ولو قال اخطب لهم، ولا تصل بهم أجزاء أن يصلي بهم. He did not explicitly permit him by the Sultan, implicitly, whether with an excuse or without, whether present or absent. If before his assumption of the prayer after the khutbah, then it is necessary that the substitute had attended the khutbah or part of it. His statement: 'his substitution is valid because the substitute has no beginning, and the khutbah is a condition of commencement, and it has been found with respect to the original.' His statement: 'he must have attended the khutbah or part of it' because the khutbah is a condition of validity for the one who initiates the tahrimah of Jumu'ah, i.e., the imam, not for every worshipper, so it is as if the substitute gave the khutbah himself; otherwise, this substitute's commencement in it is not valid at all unless this substitute appoints someone who attended the khutbah, then it is valid. His statement: 'also' meaning as his qualification for imamate is required, or as it is required in the imam if he is not a khatib. The commentary said: know that it is permissible for the holder of the office of khutbah to pray behind his substitute without excuse, just as it is permissible for the Sultan to pray behind his subordinate in establishing Jumu'ah while the Sultan is able to give the khutbah himself. Source pages p. 508

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi addresses the conditions under which a khatib (Friday sermon giver) may appoint a substitute (istikhlaf) for leading the Jumu'ah prayer. The discussion is a critical refinement of earlier rulings from Maraqi al-Falah and other commentaries. The author explains that implicit permission from the Sultan or his deputy is sufficient; explicit permission is not always required. The key distinction is whether the need arises before or after the commencement of the prayer. If the imam is struck by a hadath (invalidating event) after starting the prayer, he can appoint any qualified person as substitute. If the need arises before starting the prayer but after the khutbah, the substitute must have attended the khutbah (or part of it) because the khutbah is a condition for the imam who initiates the prayer, not for the followers. The text cites multiple authorities: al-Bada'i' states that whoever has authority over Jumu'ah can delegate it; al-Bahr declares substitution absolutely permissible; al-Zayla'i's restriction to preceding event is rejected. The rational proof (dalil aqli) is that the Sultan's delegation implies awareness of potential obstacles (illness, hadath, time constraints), so implicit permission for substitution is necessary. The language of the situation (lisan al-hal) is deemed more eloquent than explicit speech. Also, unity of khatib and imam is not a condition according to the chosen view. The passage concludes by noting that a boy may give the khutbah and an adult lead the prayer, though unity is preferred.

Key Terms
الاستخلاف (al-istikhlaf): Appointing a substitute imam to lead the Jumu'ah prayer when the original khatib is unable.
دلالة (dalālah): Implicit indication or inference, as opposed to explicit statement.
لسان الحال (lisān al-ḥāl): The language of the situation or circumstance, used as evidence for implicit permission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, if a khatib is appointed by the Sultan to lead Jumu'ah, and he becomes unable to lead the prayer after the khutbah, what condition must the substitute fulfill?
A) The substitute must have explicit written permission from the Sultan.
B) The substitute must have attended the khutbah or part of it.
C) The substitute must be a mature male who is not a traveler.
D) The substitute must be the same person who gave the khutbah.

Key Takeaway
Implicit permission and lisān al-ḥāl are sufficient for istikhlaf in Jumu'ah; the substitute must have attended the khutbah if the need arises before the imam starts the prayer.

Salah — Prayer

Time and Khutbah: Essential Conditions for Jumu'ah
Defines the time and khutbah as essential conditions for Jumu'ah validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi conditions for Jumu'ah regarding time and khutbah, apply the rulings to determine validity, and explain the key cross-madhhab differences.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah is only valid at Zuhr time with a prior khutbah; both are strict conditions.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi expands on two critical conditions for the validity of Jumu'ah prayer: the time and the khutbah. We will examine why the Hanafi school insists on Zuhr time exclusively, and what precisely makes the khutbah valid. You will also see how the Hanafi position compares with other schools and uncover a subtle intra-Hanafi debate about intention in the khutbah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conditions
The text explicitly names time of Zuhr and the khutbah as conditions for Jumu'ah validity. Locate these in the passage and note their priority (time first, then khutbah as the fourth condition).
The khutbah is listed as the fourth condition after others already known (e.g., congregation).
2
Examine the evidence for the time condition
The text cites the hadith 'When the sun declines, lead the people in Jumu'ah' and the continuous practice of the Prophet and caliphs. Understand that time is a condition for performance (shart al-ada') not just commencement.
The Hanafi position is based on transmittted practice and consensus; time cannot be extended or moved.
3
Analyze the khutbah requirements
The khutbah must be performed before the prayer, with intention (niyyah), and in the presence of at least one eligible listener (even if deaf or sleeping). A sneeze-praise does not suffice. Identify who qualifies as a listener: slave, sick, traveler (even in janabah) but not a boy or woman alone.
The requirement of intention is a point of intra-Hanafi dispute; the relied-upon view requires it.
4
Note cross-madhhab differences
Compare with Imam Malik (time extends to sunset) and Imam Ahmad (valid before noon by analogy with Arafah). For the khutbah, the Imamiyyah (Shi'a) deny it as a condition, but the text says this is a deviant view.
These differences have practical impact on when Jumu'ah can be held.
5
Understand the intra-Hanafi dispute on intention
The text mentions two opinions: one requiring intention for the khutbah (so sneeze praise does not count) and one not requiring it. The mufta bihi (operative position) is that intention is required, as stated in the text and supported by Halabi.
This affects the validity of a khutbah given without specific intention.

(The time of Zuhr) because of his saying: 'When the sun declines, lead the people in Jumu'ah prayer.' So Jumu'ah is not valid before it, and it becomes invalid by its exit due to the loss of the condition. (And) the fourth (condition): the khutbah, even if in Persian from one capable of Arabic. For the validity of the khutbah, it is required that it be performed (before it) as the Prophet did with intention. So even if the khatib sneezes and praises Allah for his sneeze, it does not suffice for the khutbah in its time due to the transmitted practice. And the presence of someone to hear it, even if he is deaf, or sleeping, or far away from those by whom Jumu'ah is valid. So the presence of a slave, or a sick person, or a traveler, even if in a state of janabah, suffices. If someone else attends or he purifies himself after the khutbah, Jumu'ah is valid, but not by a boy or a woman alone. All of them are children. (The time of Zuhr) and Malik said: its time extends to sunset because Zuhr and Asr times are one according to him. His statement: 'because of the saying of the Prophet, etc.' And because it was legislated contrary to analogy due to the reduction of two rak'ahs with the iqamah, so specialities given by the law are observed in it, and it was never reported that he prayed it before the time nor after it, and likewise the rightly guided caliphs and those after them until our day. If it were permissible, he would have done it once to teach permissibility, as in al-Halabi and others. His statement: 'So Jumu'ah is not valid before it' and Imam Ahmad said: it is valid, just as he said about the validity of standing at Arafah before noon. His statement: 'and it becomes invalid by its exit even after sitting for the amount of tashahhud due to loss of its condition, because time is a condition for performance not a condition for commencement, like Fajr prayer. In the absolute statement is an indication of the generality of the ruling that applies to excuses like sleep and crowding according to the school, as in al-Minh and al-Durr. For if it is said: what is the benefit of this issue here, and it has preceded in the twelve? According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): because only the original has been invalidated, not the description. And Muhammad said: because the original also is invalidated according to him in al-Qahistani. His statement: 'and the fourth: the khutbah' is a verbal noun in the sense of passive participle; it is the name for what is spoken about care from 'khutbah'; originally it is speech between two. Al-Qahistani from al-Azahir: it is with dammah for the sermon, plural khutab; with kasrah for seeking marriage; the verb in both is like qatala. It is a condition by consensus, contrary to the Imamiyyah who have diverged. His statement: 'before it' i.e., before the prayer because it is its condition, and the condition of a thing precedes it. The khutbah was in early Islam after the prayer like the Eid khutbah, then it was abrogated and placed before it. In the Mursal of Abu Dawud: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) used to pray Jumu'ah before the khutbah until one day he was giving the khutbah having prayed Jumu'ah, and a man entered and said: 'Dihyah has arrived and when he arrives they meet him with drums.' The people went out thinking there was no problem in leaving the khutbah. So Allah revealed the verse: 'And when they see trade or amusement, they disperse to it' (62:62). So the Prophet (peace be upon him) advanced the khutbah in Jumu'ah and delayed the prayer, as in the commentary. His statement: '(Muhammad?) for his sneeze' as an expression of wonder. His statement: 'does not suffice for the khutbah' is one of two opinions; the second is that intention is not required in it. What benefits it has preceded, and its author, the author of al-Tanwir, mentioned it in al-Dhaba'ih. His statement: 'in its time' so if he gave the khutbah before it and prayed in it, it is not valid because it is among the specializations restricted to it, as in Halabi. His statement: 'not a boy' is in the genitive case as a conjoined to 'abd', meaning the presence of a boy does not suffice.
Source pages p. 509

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi expands on the conditions of Jumu'ah prayer, specifically the time and the khutbah. It begins by stating that Jumu'ah must be performed at the time of Zuhr, based on the prophetic command ('When the sun declines, lead the people in Jumu'ah'). Therefore, it is not valid before that time, and if the time exits, the prayer becomes invalid even if one has sat for tashahhud, because time is a condition for performance, not just initiation. The author contrasts with Imam Malik (time extends to sunset) and Imam Ahmad (valid before time by analogy with Arafah), but the Hanafi position is strict. The fourth condition is the khutbah, which must be performed before the prayer. It can be in Persian even if the khatib knows Arabic, but it must be delivered with intention. A sneeze-induced praise does not count. The presence of at least one listener is required, even if deaf, sleeping, or in janabah; but a boy or woman alone does not suffice. Historical context: originally the khutbah was after the prayer, but was abrogated to before prayer due to the incident of Dihyah. The discussion also mentions an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether the intention (niyyah) is required for the khutbah; the text notes two opinions. The overall ruling is that Jumu'ah is invalid if any of these conditions are missed, even with an excuse.

Key Terms
الخطبة (al-khuṭbah): The sermon delivered before the Jumu'ah prayer, a condition for its validity.
وقت الظهر (waqt al-ẓuhr): The time of Zuhr prayer, which is the only valid time for Jumu'ah according to the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The prayer is valid if the congregation had an excuse.
B) The prayer becomes invalid even after sitting for tashahhud.
C) The prayer can be completed as Zuhr prayer.
D) The prayer is valid only if the imam had intended a substitute.

Key Takeaway
Jumu'ah must be performed within Zuhr time and preceded by a valid khutbah; missing either invalidates the prayer.

Time of Jumu'ah is the Time of Zuhr
Ruling with proof on Jumu'ah time

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the time of Jumu'ah, identify the condition of time (shart al-ada'), and explain the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding completing it as Zuhr.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah prayer is valid only within the Zuhr time window—time is a condition of performance, not just initiation.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi clarifies that Jumu'ah prayer must be performed within the time of Zuhr, beginning from the sun's decline (zawal) until the shadow of an object equals its height. The author refutes the views of Imam Malik (who extends time to sunset) and Imam Ahmad (who allows it before zawal), and addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute about what happens if time exits during the prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on Jumu'ah time
The passage begins by stating that the time of Jumu'ah is the time of Zuhr. This is the Hanafi position. Note that time is a condition of validity.
The ruling is based on the hadith: 'When the sun declines, pray Jumu'ah with the people.'
2
Understand the Hanafi proof
The proof is the Prophetic hadith and the consistent practice of the caliphs. The Hanafis argue that Jumu'ah is legislated with specificities (khususiyyat) that cannot be overridden by qiyas.
The hadith uses an imperative 'salli' and a conditional clause 'idha malat al-shams', making the time a binding condition.
3
Examine the refutation of opposing views
The text refutes Malik's extension to sunset and Ahmad's permission before zawal. Jumu'ah has unique characteristics; it is not analogous to combining prayers or standing at Arafah.
The Hanafi response: Jumu'ah is not subject to qiyas because of its special nature (khususiyyat).
4
Apply the condition of time as shart al-ada'
Time is a condition of performance (shart al-ada'), not just initiation. If time exits even after sitting for tashahhud, the prayer becomes invalid.
This is similar to Fajr: if the sun rises during Fajr, the prayer is invalid.
5
Resolve the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf held that one can complete the invalid Jumu'ah as Zuhr (nqalan). Muhammad al-Shaybani held that it cannot be completed as Zuhr because the original act (Jumu'ah) is void. The mufta bihi is Muhammad's view.
The relied-upon position is that the prayer is completely invalid and must be repeated as Zuhr from the beginning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وقت الظهر) لقوله : إذا مالت الشمس فصل بالناس الجمعة (فلا تصح) الجمعة (قبله وتبطل بخروجه لفوات الشرط وقال مالك : يمتد وقتها إلى الغروب لأنّ وقت الظهر والعصر واحد عنده. قوله : لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم الخ) ولأنها شرعت على خلاف القياس لسقوط الركعتين مع الإقامة فيراعي فيها الخصوصيات التي ورد الشرع بها، ولم يرد قط أنه صلاها قبل الوقت، ولا بعده، وكذا الخلفاء الراشدون ومن بعدهم إلى يومنا هذا، ولو كان جائزاً لفعله مرة تعليماً للجواز كذا في الحلبي، وغيره قوله : فلا تصح الجمعة (قبله وقال الإمام أحمد: تصح كما قال بصحة وقوف عرفة قبل الزوال. قوله : ( وتبطل بخروجه ولو بعد القعود قدر التشهد لفوات شرطها لأن الوقت شرط الأداء لا شرط الإفتتاح كصلاة الفجر، وفي الإطلاق إشارة إلى عموم الحكم اللاحق بعذر كنوم، وزحمة على المذهب كما في المنح والدر فإن قيل : ما فائدة هذه المسئلة هنا، وقد تقدمت في الإثني عشرية، فالجواب أنّ فيه إفادة أنها لا تصح بعد الوقت فلا تكرار نهر، وفيه إفادة أنه لا يتمها ظهراً، وهل يتمها نقلاً عندهما : لأنه إنما بطل الأصل دون الوصف، وقال محمد لا لبطلان الأصل أيضاً عنده قهستاني
(The time of Zuhr) due to his saying: 'When the sun declines, pray Jumu'ah with the people.' So Jumu'ah is not valid before it and becomes invalid by its exiting due to the loss of the condition. Malik said: Its time extends to sunset because the time of Zuhr and Asr are one according to him. His saying: due to the saying of the Prophet, etc., and because it was legislated contrary to analogy due to the reduction of two rak'ahs with the iqamah, so the specificities that the Law came with are observed. It is not reported that he prayed it before the time or after it, nor the rightly guided caliphs after him to this day; if it were permissible, he would have done it once to teach permissibility, as in al-Halabi. His saying: So Jumu'ah is not valid before it. Imam Ahmad said: It is valid just as he said the standing at Arafah before noon is valid. His saying: It becomes invalid by its exit even after sitting for the amount of tashahhud due to the loss of its condition, because time is a condition of performance, not of initiation, like the Fajr prayer. In the absolute expression is an indication of the generality of the ruling attached to an excuse like sleep or crowding, according to the madhhab as in al-Minh and al-Durr. If it is said: What is the benefit of this issue here, and it has preceded in the twelfth? The answer: It benefits that it is not valid after the time, so no repetition, as in al-Nahr. And it benefits that he does not complete it as Zuhr. And it is transmitted from the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) that he should complete it as a transmission because only the essence is invalidated, not the description. Muhammad said: No, because the essence is also invalidated according to him, as in al-Qahistani.
Source pages p. 509

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the hadith of the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wasallam) that Jumu'ah prayer must be performed at the time of Zuhr, i.e., after the sun declines (zawal). The author refutes two opposing views: (1) Imam Malik's view that the time extends to sunset, based on his position that Zuhr and Asr share a single time. (2) Imam Ahmad's view that it is valid before zawal, analogizing to the standing at Arafah. The Hanafi proof relies on the hadith and the continuous practice of the Prophet and the caliphs. The commentator also clarifies that if the time of Jumu'ah exits, the prayer becomes invalid even if one had sat for tashahhud, because time is a condition of performance (shart al-ada'), not merely of initiation (shart al-iftitah). Thus, if someone forgets or is delayed by excuse, the Jumu'ah is invalid and must be made up as Zuhr according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, but Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that even the performance as Zuhr is invalid because the intention for Jumu'ah cannot be changed to Zuhr after the fact.

Key Terms
وقت الظهر (waqt al-zuhr): The time of the Zuhr prayer, starting from the sun's decline (zawal) until the shadow of an object equals its height.
شرط الأداء (shart al-ada'): A condition that must be present at the time of performing the act; if it is missed, the act is invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, what invalidates Jumu'ah prayer even if one has sat for tashahhud?
A) The imam makes a mistake in recitation.
B) The time of Zuhr exits (e.g., the sun sets).
C) Someone enters the mosque late.
D) The khutbah is in Persian.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that Jumu'ah prayer is valid only within the time of Zuhr; time is a condition of performance that must be present throughout the prayer.
